Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Definition of Usul al-Fiqh by Additive Composition
Defines usul al-fiqh through its constituent parts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the additive definition of Usul al-Fiqh by separately defining 'usul' and 'fiqh' according to the Hanafi usul methodology.

Core Idea
Usul al-Fiqh is defined by its parts: 'usul' as foundation, 'fiqh' as derived knowledge of shar'i rulings.

This lesson introduces the classical Hanafi method of defining compound terms. The author first distinguishes between additive and synthetic definitions, then applies the additive method to 'usul al-fiqh'. By understanding the meaning of each component, you gain a precise, foundational understanding of the discipline.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish ta'rif idafi vs ta'rif tammi
Identify that a compound term can be defined either by defining each part separately (additive) or by defining the whole as one unit (synthetic). The author uses both for 'usul al-fiqh'.
This distinction is standard in Hanafi usul works.
2
Define 'usul' (plural of 'asl')
According to the text, 'asl' means 'that upon which something else is built'. This includes both sensory foundations (walls for a roof) and intellectual foundations (proof for a ruling).
The dual usage shows 'asl' can be literal or metaphorical.
3
Define 'fiqh'
The text gives the famous definition: 'knowledge of practical shar'i rulings derived from their detailed evidences'. Note the key qualifiers: 'practical' (excluding beliefs) and 'from detailed evidences' (excluding general principles).
This definition is shared across Sunni schools.
4
Combine the definitions additively
The additive definition of 'usul al-fiqh' becomes: 'the foundations (usul) that are the knowledge (fiqh) of practical shar'i rulings from detailed evidences' – or more precisely, 'the principles (usul) that lead to the knowledge (fiqh) of rulings'.
The synthetic definition is also mentioned but incomplete in the text.

Source Text

بسم اللہ الرحمن الرحیم
الترويحُ لِحَلَّ التَّوْضِيحِ وَالتَّلُويُحِ

تعریف اصول فقہ
تعریف کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) تعریف اضافی (۲) تعریف تعمی

فقہ کی تعین تعریفیں کی گئی ہیں ان میں سے مشہور تعریف مندرجہ ذیل ہے
هو العلم بالاحکام الشرعية العملية من ادلتها التفصيلية یعنی احکام شرعیہ عملیہ کو ادلہ تفصیلیہ سے جانے کا نام فقہ ہے
تعریف لقمی
العلم بالقواعد التي يتوصل بہا الی الفقہ علی وجہ اتحقیق یعنی اصول فقہ ایسے قواعد کے جانے کا نام ہے جن سے فقہ کی
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. At-tarwih li-hall al-tawdih wa al-talwih. Introductory Matters: It is the habit of authors that before starting the book, they mention some introductory matters related to the discipline in which they are writing the book, and they are as follows: (1) Definition, (2) Subject matter, (3) Aim and goal, (4) Necessity, (5) First compiler, (6) Author's biography. Therefore, briefly, we also will write some expositions about them. Definition of Usul al-Fiqh: Definition has two types: (1) Additive definition (ta'rif idafi), (2) Synthetic definition (ta'rif tammi). Additive definition means defining the annexed (mudaf) and the annexed-to (mudaf ilayh) separately. Synthetic definition means defining the mudaf and mudaf ilayh together. If the definiendum is an additive compound, both definitions are made. Usul al-Fiqh, since it is an additive compound (usul is mudaf and fiqh is mudaf ilayh), therefore both its definitions will be given. First, we mention the additive definition. Definition of the annexed (usul): Usul is the annexed, and it is the plural of asl. Asl is called that upon which something else is built, i.e., that upon which its other is founded. It is general, whether the foundation is sensory or intellectual. For example, the foundation of a roof upon walls; thus the walls are asl for the roof. Similarly, the foundation of a ruling upon a proof; thus the proof is asl for the ruling. The first is an example of sensory foundation, and the second of intellectual foundation. Definition of the annexed-to (fiqh): Several definitions of fiqh have been given. Among them, the famous definition is as follows: It is knowledge of the practical shar'i rulings derived from their detailed evidences. That is, fiqh is the name for knowing the practical shar'i rulings from detailed evidences. Synthetic definition: Knowledge of the principles by which one arrives at fiqh in a verified manner. That is, usul al-fiqh is the name for knowing such principles from which fiqh is... [incomplete].
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage introduces the definition of Usul al-Fiqh following the classical method of 'mubadiyat' (introductory matters). The author explains that scholars typically begin a book with six things: definition, subject matter, aim, necessity, first compiler, and author's biography. He then focuses on definition. He distinguishes two types of definition for compound terms: the additive definition (ta'rif idafi) where each part is defined separately, and the synthetic definition (ta'rif tammi) where the compound is defined as a whole. Since 'usul al-fiqh' is an additive compound ('usul' is mudaf, 'fiqh' is mudaf ilayh), both definitions are needed. First, he defines 'usul' (plural of asl) as 'that upon which something else is built', giving examples from sensory (walls supporting roof) and intellectual (proof supporting ruling). This illustrates that 'asl' can be literal or metaphorical. Then he defines 'fiqh' as 'knowledge of the practical shar'i rulings derived from their detailed evidences'—a standard definition in the Hanafi school. Finally, he begins the synthetic definition: 'Knowledge of the principles by which one arrives at fiqh in a verified manner', but the text cuts off before completing. The synthetic definition shows that usul al-fiqh is a tool to derive fiqh, not fiqh itself.

Key Terms
تعريف اضافی (ta'rif idafi): Defining a compound term by defining its components separately (mudaf and mudaf ilayh).
اصل (asl (pl. usul)): That upon which something else is built, whether sensory or intellectual.
فقہ (fiqh): Knowledge of practical shar'i rulings derived from detailed evidences.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the additive definition, what does 'usul' (the annexed) mean?
A) Knowledge of practical rulings
B) That upon which something else is built
C) The detailed evidences of fiqh
D) The principles of jurisprudence

Key Takeaway
Usul al-Fiqh is an additive compound: 'usul' means the foundation (whether sensory or intellectual), and 'fiqh' means knowledge of practical shar'i rulings from detailed evidences; together, usul al-fiqh is the set of principles upon which fiqh is built.

The Three Types of La'nah and Their Rulings
Classification of la'nah into three types with rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify la'nah into its three types and state the hukm for each type according to Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Cursing a specific person whose end is unknown is prohibited, even if that person committed great sins.

This passage from a Hanafi usul text provides a crucial classification of cursing (la'nah) into three types. Understanding this classification is essential for correctly applying Islamic teachings on cursing specific individuals, especially historical figures like Yazid. The passage presents the rulings derived from Quran and Sunnah, emphasizing that the permissibility of cursing depends on whether the person's final state is known from shar'i evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types
Read the passage and extract the three categories of la'nah: general by attribute, specific known disbeliever, and specific person with unknown end.
2
State the ruling for each type
For each type, determine whether it is permissible or impermissible based on the text. Type 1: permissible; Type 2: permissible; Type 3: impermissible.
3
Apply the conditions
For Type 2, note the condition: the person's disbelief at death must be reported by Shari'ah (nass). For Type 3, the prohibition applies regardless of whether the person is alive or dead, because their final state is unknown.
The key distinction is certainty of disbelief at death.
4
Connect to the Yazid debate
Relate the classification to the historical debate: why does the second group (Hanafi position) prohibit cursing Yazid specifically? Because he died as a Muslim outwardly, so he falls into Type 3.
The passage explicitly rejects the claim that Yazid's satisfaction with killing Husayn constitutes kufr.
5
Summarize the dalil for Type 3 prohibition
Identify the hadith evidence cited: 'A believer is not a curser', 'Do not curse with the curse of Allah', 'Cursing a believer is like killing him', and the story of the Prophet cursing specific polytheists at Uhud followed by abrogation.
These hadith establish the general principle of avoiding cursing specific individuals whose end is unknown.

دلیل (۳): الله عز وجل ارشاد فرماتے ہیں و من يقتل مؤمنا متعمدا فجزاء ٥ جهنم خالدافيها وغضب الله عليه ولعنه الخ یعنی جس نے جان بوجھ کر کسی کوقتل کیا تو اس کا بدلہ جہنم ہے اور اس پر اللہ کا غضب اور اس کی لعنت ہے علامہ تفتازانی نے اس سے استدلال کیا ہے کہ یزید نے چونکہ حضرت حسین کے قتل کا حکم دیا ہے تو گویا یہ قاتل ہے اور چونکہ وہ اس پر خوش تھا اور رضاء بالمعصیت کفر ہے اور اسی طرح حق جل مجدہ ارشاد فرماتے ہیں ان الذین یو ذون اللہ ورسولہ علہم اللہ فی الدنیا والآخرة اسی طرح اللہ جل شانہ فرماتے ہیں کہ لعنة الله علی الظالمین اس میں کوئی شک نہیں کہ حضرت حسین کے قاتل اور قتل کے آمر اور اس پر راضی ہونے والے اللہ اور رسول اللہ اللہ کو ایذاء دینے والے ظالم ہیں لہذا ان پر لعنت جائز ہے۔
گروه ثانی دوسرا گر وہ جو لعنت کو جائز نہیں سمجھتا ہے وہ محققین اہل سنت و الجماعت ہیں وہ مندرجہ ذیل ہیں ا۔ امام غزالی ۲۔ حسن بصری ۳- امام رازی ۴۔ امام بخاری اور دیگر متقین او قواعد شرع سے ان حضرات کی تائید ہوتی ہے۔
عند امحققین لعنت کی تین اقسام ہیں۔ قسم اول : مطلقا صفت عامہ کے ساتھ لعنت کرنا جیسے کفارو یہود پرلعنت کرنا اور یہ جائز ہے اور اس طرح کی لعنت بعض صغیرہ گناہوں کے بارہ میں بھی وارد ہوئی ہے مثلاً آپ نے فرما یا لعن الله الواشمات والمستوشمات رواه شیخان اسی طرح آپ علیہ السلام نے فرما یا لعن الله المتشبهين من الرجال بالنساء والمتشبهات من النساء بالرجال رواه البخاری بلکہ بعض مکروہ امور پر بھی لعنت وارد ہوئی ہے کما قال علیہ السلام لعن الله المحلل والمحلل له قسم ثانی : کسی متعین کا فر پر لعنت کرنا جس کے کفر کی خبر شریعت نے دی ہو جیسے فرعون ابوجہل و ابلیس پر لعنت کرنا اس طرح کی لعنت بھی جائز ہے۔
قسم ثالث : کسی ایسے شخص پر لعنت کرنا جس کی موت علی الکٹر معلوم نہ ہو اس طرح کی لعنت نا جائز ہے آگے عام ہے کہ جس پر لعنت کی جارہی ہے وہ زندہ ہو یا مردہ بظاہر کا فرکیوں نہ ہو کیونکہ ممکن ہے اللہ اس کو اسلام کی توفیق دیدے اور اس کا خاتمہ اسلام پر ہو چنانچہ عبد اللہ بن عمر رضی اللہ عنہ سے حدیث ثابت ہے کہ قال قال رسول الله يوم احد اللهم العن ابا سفيان اللهم العن الحارث بن هشام اللهم العن سهيل بن عمر اللهم العن صفوان بن امية فنزلت ليس له من الامرشئ اويتوب عليهم او يعذبهم فانهم ظلمون فتيب عليهم كلهم رواه البخاری آ لعنت نہی کے نازل ہونے سے پہلے کی تو اللہ کی طرف سے نہی وارد ہوئی جیسا کہ حدیث سے واضح ہے اسی طرح ایک حدیث میں آپ نے ارشاد فرمایا کہ لا يكون المؤمن لعانا (رواه الترمذي وقال عليه السلام في مقام آخر لا تلعنوا بلعنة الله رواه ابوداؤ داسی طرح ایک اور حدیث میں ہے من لعن شيئا ليس له باهل رجعت اللعنة عليه (رواه التر بنی اسی طرح ایک اور مقام پر فرمایا لعن المؤمن گفتله رواه مسلم اسی طرح فرمایا که لا تسبوا الاموات فانهم قـدافــضــوا الـى مــاقــدمـوا ( رواه البخاری) ان تمام روایات سے معلوم ہوا کہ نصوص عامہ کی وجہ سے یزید پر لعنت جائز نہیں چنانچہ پہلے گروہ کا پہلی دو دلیلوں سے استدلال درست نہیں کیونکہ اس میں یزید پر با تعیین لعنت نہیں کی گئی یہ لعنت کی پہلی قسم میں شامل ہے اسی طرح تیسری دلیل سے بھی استدلال درست نہیں ایک تو اس وجہ سے کہ کسی مسلمان کو قتل کرنا یا قتل کرنے کا حکم دینا یہ گناہ کبیرہ ہے کفر نہیں دوسرا اس وجہ سے کہ اگر یوں کہا جائے کہ یزید حضرت حسین رضی اللہ عنہ کے قتل پر راضی تھا اور یہ حرام کو جائز سمجھنا ہے اور معصیت کو جائز سمجھنا کفر ہے تو امام غزالی اس کے جواب میں فرماتے ہیں کہ پہلے یہ بات ثابت نہیں کہ یزید نے حضرت حسین کو قتل کرنے کا حکم دیا تھا بلکہ یہ فعل شنیع امیر کوفہ عبید اللہ بن زیاد نے کیا اور یزید ایک مہینہ کی مسافت پر تھا اور اتنے تھوڑے سے وقت میں عبید اللہ کے پاس یزید کاقتل کرنے کا پیغام نہیں پہنچ سکتا بلکہ تاریخ سے ثابت ہے کہ یزید نے ابن زیاد کو کہا تھا رعت لی العداوة في قلب كل بروفاجر وقال رحمک اللہ یاحسین رضی الله عنه لقد قتلك رجل لم يعرف حق الرحم بہر حال یزید نے ابن زیاد کو اس پر سزا نہیں دی اس لئے اس کا یہ فعل شنیع قبیح ہے اور گناہ کبیرہ ہے اور یقیناً حضرت حسین حق پر تھے اور یزید ناحق تھا لیکن اصول اور قواعد شرعیہ کے مطابق اس پر لعنت جائز نہیں بعض لوگ جو اصول شرع سے ناواقف ہیں لعنت جائز نہ سمجھنے والوں پر خوارج کا فتوی لگاتے ہیں تو ہم اس کے بارہ میں وہی کہیں گے جو مولا نا عبد العزیز پر ھاروی علیہ الرحمہ نے فرمایا قبيح افعاله مشهور وحب اهل البيت واجب لكن النهي عن لعنه ليس للقصور في حبهم بل لقواعد الشرع کہ یزید پر لعنت سے منع کرنا یہ اہل بیت سے محبت کے کم ہونے کی وجہ سے نہیں بلکہ قواعد شرع کی وجہ سے ہے واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔
Proof (3): Allah Almighty says: 'And whoever kills a believer intentionally, his recompense is Hell, wherein he will abide eternally, and Allah has become angry with him and has cursed him...' meaning whoever intentionally kills someone, his recompense is Hell and upon him is Allah's wrath and curse. Allamah Taftazani argued that since Yazid ordered the killing of Husayn, he is a killer, and since he was pleased with it and satisfaction with sin is disbelief. Similarly, Allah says: 'Indeed, those who harm Allah and His Messenger – Allah has cursed them in this world and the Hereafter.' Also Allah says: 'The curse of Allah is upon the oppressors.' There is no doubt that the killer of Husayn, the one who ordered the killing, and those pleased with it are harmers of Allah and His Messenger and oppressors, so cursing them is permissible. Second group: The group that does not consider cursing permissible are the verified scholars of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, including Imam Ghazali, Hasan al-Basri, Imam Razi, Imam Bukhari, and other God-fearing scholars. The rules of Shari'ah support them. According to the verifiers, cursing has three types: First type: Cursing in an absolute general manner, like cursing disbelievers and Jews – this is permissible. Such cursing has been mentioned for some minor sins, e.g., the Prophet said: 'May Allah curse the women who tattoo and those who get tattooed' (agreed upon). Similarly, he said: 'May Allah curse men who imitate women and women who imitate men' (Bukhari). Rather, cursing has occurred for some disliked things, as he said: 'May Allah curse the muhallil and the one for whom it is made permissible (tahlil).' Second type: Cursing a specific disbeliever whose disbelief has been reported by Shari'ah, like cursing Pharaoh, Abu Jahl, and Iblis – this is also permissible. Third type: Cursing a person whose death upon disbelief is unknown – this is impermissible. This applies generally whether the cursed person is alive or dead and appears outwardly not a disbeliever, because it is possible that Allah grants him the ability to accept Islam and his end is upon Islam. Thus, a hadith is established from Abdullah ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah said on the Day of Uhud: 'O Allah, curse Abu Sufyan; O Allah, curse al-Harith ibn Hisham; O Allah, curse Suhayl ibn Amr; O Allah, curse Safwan ibn Umayyah.' Then the verse was revealed: 'Not for you is the decision; whether He turns to them in mercy or punishes them; for they are wrongdoers.' So Allah turned to them all (Bukhari). This was before the prohibition of cursing came from Allah, as is clear from the hadith. Similarly, in another hadith the Prophet said: 'A believer is not a curser' (Tirmidhi). And he said elsewhere: 'Do not curse with the curse of Allah' (Abu Dawud). Also: 'Whoever curses something not deserving of it, the curse returns upon him' (Tirmidhi). And he said: 'Cursing a believer is like killing him' (Muslim). And he said: 'Do not revile the dead, for they have gotten what they sent ahead' (Bukhari). From all these narrations it is understood that due to general texts, cursing Yazid is not permissible. Thus, the first group's proofs from the first two evidences are incorrect because they do not specify cursing Yazid; they fall under the first type of cursing. Similarly, the third proof is incorrect: first, because killing a Muslim or ordering his killing is a major sin, not disbelief; second, if it is said that Yazid was pleased with the killing of Husayn and considered the forbidden permissible, and considering sin permissible is disbelief, Imam Ghazali responds that it is not established that Yazid ordered Husayn's killing; rather, this heinous act was done by the governor of Kufa, Ubaydullah ibn Ziyad, while Yazid was a month's distance away, and in such short time the message to kill could not have reached Ubaydullah. Rather, history proves that Yazid told Ibn Ziyad: 'You have kindled enmity in every pious and impious heart' and said 'May Allah have mercy on you, O Husayn, a man who did not recognize the right of kinship has killed you.' Nevertheless, Yazid did not punish Ibn Ziyad for this, so his act is ugly and a major sin, and certainly Husayn was on the right and Yazid on the wrong, but according to principles and rules of Shari'ah, cursing him is not permissible. Some people ignorant of Shari'ah principles apply the fatwa of Khawarij to those who do not consider cursing permissible. Regarding this, we say what Mawlana Abdul Aziz Parhari (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'His evil acts are well-known, and love of Ahl al-Bayt is obligatory, but the prohibition of cursing him is not due to deficiency in love for them, but due to rules of Shari'ah.' And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage presents a classic usul al-fiqh discussion on the permissibility of cursing (la'nah) a specific individual, using the historical case of Yazid ibn Muawiyah and the killing of Imam Husayn (RA). The author first presents the arguments of the group that permits cursing Yazid, citing Quranic verses: 'Whoever kills a believer...' (4:93), 'Those who harm Allah and His Messenger...' (33:57), and 'The curse of Allah is upon the oppressors' (7:44). These verses are interpreted as applying to Yazid since he ordered the killing and was pleased with it. Then the second group, comprising verified Sunni scholars like Imam Ghazali and Imam Bukhari, refutes this by categorizing la'nah into three types: (1) general cursing of attributes (e.g., cursing disbelievers) – permissible; (2) cursing a specific person whose disbelief is known from Shari'ah (e.g., Pharaoh) – permissible; (3) cursing a specific person whose final state is unknown – prohibited. Since Yazid died as a Muslim outwardly (his disbelief is not established), he falls into the third category, so cursing him specifically is not allowed. The text supports this with hadith evidence, including the incident at Uhud where the Prophet cursed specific polytheists but later a verse abrogated that. Also, prophetic hadith prohibit excessive cursing and specify that a believer is not a curser. The author concludes that the first group's proofs actually fall under general cursing, not specific. He further refutes the claim that Yazid's satisfaction with the killing constitutes kufr, arguing that it is a major sin, not disbelief, and that the order for the killing is historically questionable. The final ruling upheld by the Hanafi school (and many scholars) is that cursing a specific person whose death upon disbelief is unknown is impermissible, out of caution and respect for the rules of Shari'ah.

Key Terms
لعنت (la'nah): An imprecation invoking Allah's curse; its ruling depends on the type (general, specific known disbeliever, specific unknown end).
تعیین (ta'yin): Specification of a particular person in the curse.
کفر (kufr): Disbelief; the passage distinguishes between major sin (kabirah) and kufr when evaluating actions like ordering a killing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the classification in this lesson, what is the ruling on cursing a specific person who is known to have died as a disbeliever (e.g., Pharaoh)?
A) Permissible, because his disbelief at death is known from Quran.
B) Impermissible, because we should not curse any individual.
C) Permissible only if he is alive.
D) Impermissible because cursing is always a sin.

Key Takeaway
Cursing a specific person whose end is unknown is prohibited; only general curses or curses on individuals with certain disbelief at death are permissible.

Lexical and Terminological Definitions of Key Usul Terms
Defining key usul al-fiqh terms lexically and terminologically

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the lexical and terminological definitions of key usul al-fiqh terms according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
In usul al-fiqh, the terminological meaning is built upon the lexical root.

Usul al-fiqh terminology often has a lexical origin that illuminates its technical use. This lesson presents the foundational definitions of terms like Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas, as given by Hanafi usul scholars. Mastering these definitions is the first step to understanding how rulings are derived from the sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the lexical meaning
For each term, note its root and literal sense as explained in the passage. For example, 'Sunnah' lexically means 'way' or 'custom'.
2
State the terminological meaning
How does the Hanafi school define it technically? For instance, Ijma is 'agreement of all mujtahids of the Ummah on a legal ruling'.
The Hanafi definition of Ijma requires the consensus of all mujtahids in a generation.
3
Note the key element in each definition
Identify the crucial condition or component. For Qiyas, the presence of a common cause ('illah) is essential to equate the branch with the root.
4
Recognize the relationship between terms
Understand how these definitions interrelate. For example, Qiyas depends on a ruling established by Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لغوی تحقیق:۔ او قدی شتق ہے ایقاد سے بمعنی آگ جلانا (مشکوۃ ) الكوة الغير النافذة“ یعنی جالا (سرائیکی میں ) طاقچہ اور وہ سوراخ جو آر پار نہ ہو۔ الاقتباس : چنگاری سے آگ لینا اور یہاں مطلقا حصول مراد والے معنی میں مستعمل ہے۔ السنة : لغوی معنی ہے عادت اور طریقہ اور اصطلاحی معنی ہے " ما صدر عن النبی الله من قول او فعل او تقرير “۔ اجماع : لغوی معنی ہے عزم اور اتفاق، اصطلاح میں کہتے ہیں اتفاق المجتهدين من امة محمد ال في كل عصر علی حکم شرعی یعنی امت محمدیہ کے مجتہدین کا کسی زمانہ میں کسی حکم شرعی پر اتفاق کر لینا۔ :آراء بیرای کی جمع ہے اصل میں اَرءَ ہی تھا قلب مکانی کی۔ راہ کو ہمزہ کی جگہ اور ہمزہ کو راء کی جگہ پر لے آئے تو اے رائی ہو گیا پھر آمن والے قانون کے تحت دوسرے ہمزہ کو الف سے بدل دیا تو ار ای ہو گیا پھر دُعاء والے قانون کے تحت یا کو ہمزہ سے تبدیل کر دیا تو آراء ہو گیا ، ( آثار ) یہ اثر کی جمع ہے (قیاس ) اس کا لغوی معنی ہے تقدیر الشی باشی یعنی ھی کوئی کے ساتھ نا پنا، برابر کرنا اور اصطلاحی معنی ہے " مساواة الفرع بالاصل لعلہ فی الحکم یعنی ایک ہی حکم میں علت کی وجہ سے فرع کو اصل کے برابر کرنا۔ منهاجا : الطريق الواضح یعنی روشن راسته صادفت : باب مفاعلہ سے ہے بمعنی وجدت اور لاقیت امواجا : موج کی جمع ۔ افواجا : فوج کی جمع ہے۔ الساطع : من السطوع الى الارتفاع بلندی۔ معوانا : کثیر المعونہ زیادہ مددکرنے والا ۔ المحجة : جادة الطریق یعنی وسط طریق۔ سلطان : والی، یہ مشتق ہے السلاطہ سے۔ ھدی : بمعنی ہادی۔ اعتصم : چنگل مارا۔ اغتنم : غنیمت سمجھا۔ ساحہ صحن ۔ الاستصحاب : ساتھ بٹھانا۔ الاستحسان : حمد الفتی حسنا یعنی کسی چیز کو اچھا سمجھنا۔
Lexical analysis: 'Auqada' is derived from 'Iqad' meaning to kindle fire. (Mishkāt) is a niche that is not a passage, i.e., a niche (in Saraiki: a small arch) and a hole that does not go through. Al-Iqtibās: taking fire from a spark, and here it is used in the absolute sense of obtaining what is intended. As-Sunnah: lexical meaning is custom and way, and terminological meaning is 'what emanated from the Prophet (peace be upon him) in terms of speech, action, or tacit approval.' Al-Ijmāʿ: lexical meaning is resolve and agreement, terminologically it is: 'the agreement of the mujtahids of the Ummah of Muhammad (peace be upon him) in any era on a legal ruling.' Ārāʾ: plural of 'ray'; originally 'arʼ', then a metathesis occurred: the rāʼ is moved to the place of the hamzah and the hamzah to the place of the rāʼ, becoming 'arāy', then by the rule of 'āmin' the second hamzah is replaced with alif, becoming 'arāy', then by the rule of 'duʿā'' the yā is replaced with hamzah, becoming 'ārāʾ'. (Āthār) is the plural of 'athar'. (Qiyās) lexical meaning is 'estimation of a thing by another', i.e., measuring, equating; terminological meaning is 'equating a branch to a root in a ruling due to a common cause', i.e., to equate the branch to the root in the same ruling because of the cause. Minhājan: 'the clear path' i.e., bright road. Ṣādafat: from the form of mufāʿalah, meaning 'I found' and 'I met'. Amwājan: plural of 'mawj' (wave). Afwājan: plural of 'fawj' (group). al-Sāṭiʿ: from 'al-sutūʿ' meaning 'height, elevation'. Muʿāwinan: 'one who provides much help, great helper'. al-Muḥajjah: 'the main road' i.e., middle of the road. Sulṭān: 'ruler', derived from 'al-salāṭah'. Hādī: meaning 'guide'. Iʿtaṣama: 'clung to'. Ightanama: 'considered as booty'. Sāḥah: 'courtyard'. al-Istiṣḥāb: 'keeping as companion'. al-Istiḥsān: 'deeming something good' i.e., considering something good.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage appears to be a comprehensive lexical analysis of key usul terminology. The author begins by defining each term both linguistically and terminologically, which is a standard method in Hanafi usul works. The definitions align with the Hanafi school's understanding. For instance, Sunnah is defined as the Prophet's sayings, actions, and tacit approvals, which is the standard definition. Ijmāʿ is defined as the consensus of mujtahids on a legal ruling. The definition of Qiyās includes the condition of 'illah for equating the branch with the root, reflecting the Hanafi emphasis on effective cause. This passage serves as a memorandum for students to memorize these foundational definitions.

Key Terms
مشکوۃ (Mishkāh): الكوة الغير النافذة: a niche that is not a passage, i.e., a small arch or hole that does not go through.
السنة (al-Sunnah): ما صدر عن النبي الله من قول او فعل او تقرير: what emanated from the Prophet (peace be upon him) in terms of speech, action, or tacit approval.
الاجماع (al-Ijmāʿ): اتفاق المجتهدين من امة محمد ال في كل عصر علی حکم شرعی: agreement of the mujtahids of the Ummah of Muhammad in any era on a legal ruling.
القیاس (al-Qiyās): مساواة الفرع بالاصل لعلة فی الحکم: equating a branch to a root in a ruling due to a common cause.

The terminological definitions of usul terms are built on their lexical roots; Hanafi scholars emphasize precision in these definitions to ensure correct deduction.

Defining 'Ilm al-Tawhid wa al-Sifat: A Precision in Hanafi Usul
Question-answer defining 'ilm al-tawhid wa al-sifat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate between 'ilm al-tawhid wa al-sifat and iman, and explain why 'ilm al-kalam is the correct interpretation according to Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, 'ilm al-tawhid wa al-sifat refers to 'ilm al-kalam, not iman, to preserve the base-based distinction.

This passage from a Hanafi usul text addresses a subtle but critical definitional issue: what does the phrase 'ilm al-tawhid wa al-sifat (knowledge of tawhid and attributes) truly refer to? The text presents a dilemma and resolves it with a distinction between mere conviction and firmly rooted conviction (rusukh). Understanding this distinction is essential for grasping how Hanafi usul grounds its epistemological framework.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two possible meanings
The question in the passage presents two options: 'ilm al-tawhid wa al-sifat could mean iman (faith) or 'ilm al-kalam (scholastic theology). Recognize that these are the two candidates being evaluated.
The dilemma arises because the term appears in the context of a base (mabni) and that which is based upon it (mabni 'alayh).
2
Analyze the problem with the first option
If it meant iman, then the base (the knowledge) and what it grounds (firm conviction) would be identical, which is logically invalid. Understand why this is problematic: iman itself is the firm conviction, so there would be no distinction.
3
Analyze the apparent problem with the second option
If it meant 'ilm al-kalam, that also includes conviction (i'tiqad), so again the base and grounded would seem to be the same. See why this seems to also create an identity problem.
4
Examine the author's resolution
The author adopts the second option ('ilm al-kalam) but introduces a nuance: while absolute conviction is included in 'ilm al-kalam, the firmness (rusukh) of that conviction is not. Rusukh depends on 'ilm al-kalam but is not identical to it. This preserves the distinction.
Key term: rusukh (firmness) is the quality that makes conviction firmly rooted; it is the result of studying kalam.
5
Formulate the key distinction
Therefore, the base is 'ilm al-kalam (theology), and what is based upon it is firmly rooted conviction (i'tiqad raasikh). They are distinct yet causally related. This is the Hanafi precision.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قولہ علی علم التوحید: سوال: علم التوحید والصفات سے مراد یا ایمان ہوگا یا علم کلام ایمان مراد ہو تو یہ درست نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اعتقاد راسخ بھی ایمان کا نام ہے۔ تو بینی اور مبنی علیہ میں فرق نہیں رہے گا۔ اور اگر اس سے مراد علم کلام ہے تو یہ بھی درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ اعتقاد علم کلام میں بھی مندرج ہے۔ پھر بھی مبنی اور مبنی علیہ کا واحد ہو نا لا زم آئے گا۔
جواب :۔ ہم دوسری شق مراد لیتے ہیں کہ علم تو حید سے مراد علم کلام ہے باقی علم کلام میں مطلق اعتقاد تو مندرج ہے لیکن اس کا رسوخ مندرج نہیں بلکہ یہ علم کلام پر موقوف ہے۔
His saying: upon knowledge of tawhid: Question: What is meant by 'knowledge of tawhid and attributes'? Either it means faith (iman) or it means the science of kalam. If faith is meant, that is not correct because firm conviction (i'tiqad raasikh) is also called faith. Then there would be no difference between the base and that which is based upon it. If the science of kalam is meant, that is also not correct because this conviction is within the science of kalam. Still, the base and what is based upon it would necessarily be one. Answer: We adopt the second possibility, that by 'knowledge of tawhid' means the science of kalam. As for the rest, absolute conviction is included in the science of kalam, but its firmness (rusukh) is not included; rather, it depends on the science of kalam.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage is a usul definition question-and-answer. The author is clarifying what 'ilm al-tawhid wa al-sifat refers to in the base text. The question presents a dilemma: if it means iman, then the base (al-mabni) and that upon which it is based (al-mabni 'alayh) become the same, which is invalid. If it means 'ilm al-kalam, then it also includes conviction, again making them the same. The author's answer resolves this by noting that while conviction is included in 'ilm al-kalam, the firmness (rusukh) of that conviction is not; rather, it is dependent on 'ilm al-kalam. Thus, the distinction is preserved. This shows the precision in defining technical terms in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
علم التوحید والصفات ('ilm al-tawhid wa al-sifat): In this passage, it is defined as referring to 'ilm al-kalam (scholastic theology), not iman.
رسوخ (rusukh): Firmness or rootedness of conviction, which is dependent on 'ilm al-kalam.
علم الكلام ('ilm al-kalam): Scholastic theology, the discipline that provides rational proofs for beliefs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The science of kalam
C) The Quran and Sunnah
D) Fiqh

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, 'ilm al-tawhid wa al-sifat denotes 'ilm al-kalam, not iman, preserving the distinction between foundational theology and the firm conviction it produces.

Scope of Sharia: Principles and Branches
Defining Sharia, usul, and furu' as foundational categories in usul al-fiqh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of Sharia and distinguish between its principles (usul) and branches (furu') as per Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Sharia is broader than fiqh; usul are universal proofs, furu' are detailed rulings with specific causes.

This passage defines the key terms of our field: Sharia, its principles (usul), and its branches (furu'). Understanding this taxonomy is essential before diving into legal rulings. The author establishes that Sharia includes not only fiqh but also theological matters and the methodology of proof (usul).

Guided Path
1
Identify the overarching term
Begin by isolating the term 'Sharia' (الشريعة) and note that it is defined as encompassing fiqh and other matters established by textual proofs, such as the vision of Allah and resurrection. This sets the broad scope.
Sharia is not limited to fiqh; it includes usul and 'aqidah.
2
Distinguish the two components
The passage divides Sharia into 'usul al-shari'a' (principles) and 'furu' al-shari'a' (branches). Identify the defining characteristic of each: usul are the universal proofs (adillah kulliyyah), while furu' are the detailed rulings (ahkam mufassalah) explained in fiqh.
This dichotomy is foundational in Hanafi usul.
3
Analyze the principles (usul)
The text states that the principles of Sharia are its universal proofs, and their foundations (mabani al-usul) are built upon theology (knowledge of Essence, attributes, prophethoods). This connects usul to 'ilm al-kalam.
Usul al-fiqh relies on these theological foundations.
4
Analyze the branches (furu')
The branches are the detailed rulings of fiqh, and their meanings (ma'aniha) are the particular detailed causes ('ilal juz'iyyah tafṣiliyyah) for each issue. Note the subtlety (diqqah) mentioned: these are abstruse and not easily accessible to everyone.
This subtlety underscores the need for rigorous ijtihad.
5
Recognize the practical importance
The passage concludes that through Sharia comes worldly order and otherworldly reward, and through the subtlety of fiqh comes elevation of ranks. This motivates the study of usul and furu'.
The ultimate goal is both worldly benefit and spiritual reward.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَولُهُ عَلى أَن جَعَلَ تَعلِيقٌ لِلمَحَامِدِ بِبَعْضِ النِّعَمِ إِشَارَةٌ إِلَى عِظَمِ أَمرِ العِلمِ الَّذِي وَقَعَ التّصنيفُ فِيهِ وَدَلَالَةٌ عَلَى جَلَالَةِ قَدرِهِ وَالشَّرِيعَةُ تَعُمُّ الفِقْهَ وَغَيْرَهُ مِن الأمُورِ الثَّابِتَةِ بِالادِلَّةِ السَّمْعِيَّةِ كَمَسأَلَةِ الرُّؤيَةِ وَالمَعَادِ وَكَونِ الإِجْمَاعِ وَالْقِيَاسِ حُجَّةً وَمَا أَشْبَهَ ذَلِكَ وَأُصُولُ الشَّرِيعَةِ أَدِلَّتُهَا الكُلِّيَّةُ وَمَبَانِي الْأُصُولِ مَا تُبْتَنَى هِيَ عَلَيْهِ مِن عِلمِ الذَّاتِ وَالصِّفَاتِ وَالنُّبُوَّاتِ وَتَمهِيدُهَا تَسوِيَتُهَا وَإِصْلَاحُهَا بِكَونِهَا عَلَى وَفقِ الحَقِّ وَنَهجِ الصَّوَابِ وَفُرُوعُ الشَّرِيعَةِ أَحكَامُهَا المُفَصَّلَةُ المُبَيَّنَةُ فِي عِلمِ الفِقْهِ وَمَعَانِيهَا العِلَلُ الجُزْئِيَّةُ التَّفصِيلِيَّةُ عَلَى كُلِّ مَسْأَلَةٍ وَدِقَّتُهَا كُونُهَا عَامِضَةٌ لَطِيفَةٌ لَا يَصِلُ إِلَيْهَا كُلُّ أَحَدٍ بِسُهُولَةٍ وَجَمِيعُ ذَلِكَ نِعَمْ تَستَوجِبُ الحَمدَ إذ بالشَّرِيعَةِ نِظَامُ الدُّنْيَا وَثَوَابُ العُقبَى وَبِدِقَةِ مَعَانِي الْفِقْهِ رِفعَةُ دَرَجَاتِ
His saying: that he made the connection of praises to some of the blessings is an indication of the greatness of the knowledge which the book is about, and a proof of its sublime rank. And the Sharia comprises fiqh and other matters established by textual proofs, such as the issue of vision (of Allah), resurrection, the fact that consensus and analogy are proofs, and the like. And the principles of Sharia are its universal proofs. The foundations of usul are what they are built upon from the knowledge of the Essence, attributes, and prophethoods. Their preparation is their adjustment and correction by being in accordance with truth and the path of correctness. The branches of Sharia are its detailed rulings explained in the science of fiqh. Their meanings are the particular detailed causes (illal) for each issue. Their subtlety is that they are abstruse and fine, not everyone can easily attain them. All of that are blessings that require praise, because through Sharia is the order of this world and the reward of the hereafter, and through the subtlety of the meanings of fiqh is the elevation of ranks.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage is a usul definition passage that defines the scope of Sharia, its principles (usul), and its branches (furu'). The author explains that Sharia includes not only fiqh but also matters like the vision of Allah, resurrection, and the validity of consensus and analogy as proofs. The principles of Sharia are the universal proofs (adillah kulliyyah), and the foundations of usul are based on theology (knowledge of the Essence, attributes, prophethoods). The branches are the detailed rulings of fiqh, and their meanings are the specific legal causes. The subtlety of fiqh lies in its depth, which requires effort to attain. This establishes the importance of the science of usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
شریعت (shari'a): Comprehensive term including fiqh and other religious matters established by textual proofs
اصول الشریعة (usul al-shari'a): The universal proofs (adillah kulliyyah) of Sharia
علل جزئیہ تفصیلیہ (ilal juz'iyyah tafṣiliyyah): Particular detailed causes for each legal issue

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what are the 'principles of Sharia' (usul al-shari'ah)?
A) The detailed rulings of fiqh
B) The universal proofs
C) The knowledge of the Essence and attributes
D) The subtle meanings of fiqh

Key Takeaway
Sharia encompasses both principles (universal proofs) and branches (detailed fiqh rulings); mastering usul is essential for correct ijtihad.

Juz'i Dalils Revert to Kulli
Question and answer about the basis of ahkam in kulli vs juz'i dalils

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that specific rulings (juz'i dalils) ultimately derive from general sources (kulli dalils) and apply this principle to identify the basis of a given ruling.

Core Idea
Every specific proof (dalīl juz'ī) in the Quran is an instance of the general proof (dalīl kullī) — the Quran itself.

In this passage, a potential contradiction is raised: if every shar'i ruling (like zakat and hajj) has its own specific verse, how can the author claim that all rulings are based on general evidences? The answer resolves this by showing that specific verses are not independent; they are particular expressions of the overall 'Book of Allah,' which is a general evidence. This distinction between juz'i and kulli is a foundational principle in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The objector points out that specific rulings like zakat and hajj have specific verses, not general ones. Thus the author's claim that all rulings are based on general evidences seems contradicted.
2
State the Hanafi resolution
The answer acknowledges that rulings are constructed on specific proofs but clarifies that these specific proofs revert to the general proof (the Quran). Thus the author's statement is correct.
3
Trace the reversion mechanism
Specific verses like 'establish prayer' and 'give zakat' all fall under the category 'Book of Allah', which is a general evidence. So each juz'i dalil is an instance of the kulli dalil.
4
Apply the principle to a new example
Consider the verse for fasting ('صِيَامُ شَهْرِ رَمَضَانَ'). It is a juz'i dalil, but it reverts to the kulli dalil of the Quran. This shows the principle applies consistently.
You can use any specific verse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
زکوۃ حکم شرعی ہے دلیل آتو الزکوۃ ہے اور حج کرنا حکم شرعی ہے اور اس کی دلیل اللہ علی الناس حج البیت ہے اور یہ سب دلائل جزئیہ ہیں نہ کہ دلائل کلید تو ماتن کا یہ کہنا کہ احکام شرعیہ کی بنا دلائل کلیہ پر ہے درست نہ ہوا؟ جواب: بے شک احکام شرعیہ کی بناء ادلہ جزئیہ پر ہے۔ لیکن ادلہ جزئیہ باوجود اپنی کثرت کے اولہ کلیہ کے طرف لوٹ آتے ہیں۔ کیونکہ اقیمو الصلوٰۃ، آتو الزکوۃ ان سب پر کتاب اللہ کا اطلاق ہوتا ہے۔ اور کتاب اللہ ادلہ کلیہ میں سے ایک دلیل ہے۔
Zakat is a shar'i ruling, its evidence is 'give zakat', and performing Hajj is a shar'i ruling, its evidence is 'upon the people is Hajj of the House'. And all these are individual evidences, not general evidences. So is the author's statement that 'the bases of shar'i rulings are upon general evidences' correct? Answer: Indeed the construction of shar'i rulings is upon individual evidences. But individual evidences, despite their abundance, revert to the side of general ones. Because 'establish prayer', 'give zakat' — all of these the Book of Allah applies to them. And the Book of Allah is one of the general evidences.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This is a question-and-answer passage addressing a potential objection to the author's claim that shar'i rulings are based on general evidences (adillah kulliyyah). The objector points out that specific rulings like zakat and Hajj have specific proofs (juz'i), not general ones. The answer clarifies that while the immediate proofs are particular, they all fall under the general source of the Quran, which is a kulli dalil. Thus the author's statement is correct because the juz'i dalils ultimately revert to kulli dalils. This is a standard Hanafi position that the Quran is a comprehensive source encompassing all specific rulings within its general verses.

Key Terms
دلیل جزئیہ (dalīl juz'ī): A specific proof for a particular ruling, e.g., a single verse or hadith for one act.
دلیل کلیہ (dalīl kullī): A comprehensive source of law encompassing multiple rulings, e.g., the Quran as a whole.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because all juz'i dalils revert to kulli dalils like the Quran.
C) Because kulli dalils are only the Quran.
D) Because the author only considered zakat and Hajj.

Key Takeaway
Specific proofs (juz'i) are not independent; they all revert to general proofs (kulli) like the Quran.

Definition and Conditions of I'jaz in Speech
Defining i'jaz and its relation to eloquence, with two inquiries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define i'jaz (inimitability) in speech, state its essential conditions, and distinguish it from sihr (sorcery) in speech.

Core Idea
I'jaz is the singular, inimitable quality at the peak of eloquence; sorcery has multiple levels and can be imitated.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the inimitability (i'jaz) of the Qur'an is a foundational proof of its divine origin. This passage examines the precise definition of i'jaz, clarifying that it is more than mere eloquence—it involves the inability of others to produce its like. By understanding this definition, you will see how the Qur'an's unique linguistic challenge operates as a definitive argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition being quoted
The passage begins by quoting a definition: i'jaz in speech is conveying meaning in the most eloquent way. Recognize that this is a starting point, not the complete concept.
The author immediately clarifies that this is not a full interpretation.
2
Distinguish between definition and condition
The author argues that i'jaz necessarily requires that others cannot produce its like. Being most eloquent is a condition, but the inability to oppose is equally essential.
3
Survey the differing opinions on the aspect of i'jaz
Various theories are listed: eloquence, news of the unseen, unique style, and divine prevention of opposition. The author indicates the correct view is the first.
This shows a legitimate ikhtilaf among scholars.
4
Understand the analogy with fabric
The passage contrasts the fringes (plural, weak) of a garment with the handle (singular, strong) of a pitcher to illustrate that i'jaz is singular and unified, while sorcery is multiple and varied.
Analogy reinforces the distinction.
5
Reflect on the two inquiries
Two critical questions are raised: (1) whether being most eloquent is sufficient if others cannot oppose, and (2) what is the highest level of eloquence. These probe the definition's adequacy.
The passage ends mid-sentence on the second inquiry.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله الإِعْجَازُ فِي الكَلامِ أَن يُؤدَّى المعنى بِطَرِيقٍ هُوَ أَبْلَغُ مِن جَمِيعِ مَا عَدَاهُ مِن الطُّرُقِ لَيسَ تَفسِيراً لِمَفهُوم إعجازِ الكَلامِ ; لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَلْزَمُ أَن يَكُونَ بِالبَلاغَةِ بَل هُوَ عِبَارَة عَن كَونِ الكَلامِ بِحَيثُ لَا يُمكِنُ مُعَارَضَتْهُ وَالإِنْيَانُ بِمِثْلِهِ مِن أَعجَرْتُهُ إِذَا جَعَلته عَاجِرًا وَلِهَذَا اختَلَفُوا فِي جِهَةِ إعجاز القرآن مَعَ الاتِّفَاقِ عَلَى كَونِهِ مُعجِزًا فَقِيلَ إِنَّهُ بِبَلاغَتِهِ وَقِيلَ بِإِحْبَارِهِ عَن المَغِيْبَاتِ وَقِيلَ بِأُسَلُوبِهِ الغَرِيبِ وَقِيلَ بصَرفِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى العُقُولَ عَن المُعَارَضَةِ بَلِ المُرَادُ أَنَّ إعْجَازَ كَلامِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى إِنَّمَا هُوَ بِهَذَا الطَّرِيقِ وَهُوَ كَونُهُ فِى غَايَةِ البَلَاغَةِ وَنِهَايَةِ الفَصَاحَةِ عَلَى مَا هُوَ الرَّأى الصَّحِيحُ فَبِاعْتِبَارِ أَنَّهُ يُشتَرَطُ فِى إعجازِ الكَلامِ كُونُهُ أَبْلَغَ مِن جَمِيعِ مَا عَدَاهُ يَكُونُ وَاحِدًا لَا تَعَدُّدَ فِيهِ بِخِلَافِ سِحرِ الكَلَامِ فَإِنَّهُ عِبَارَةٌ عَن دِقَّتِهِ وَلُطفِ مَا خَذِهِ وَهَذَا يَقَعُ عَلَى طُرُقٍ مُتَعَدِّدَةٍ وَمَرَاتِبَ مُختَلِفَةٍ فَلِهَذَا قَالَ أَهْدَابُ السِّحرِ بِلَفظِ الجَمع وَعُرَوَةُ الإِعْجَازِ بِلَفظ المُفرَدِ وَهُدَبُ الثّوبِ مَا عَلَى أَطْرَافِهِ وَعُرَوَةُ الكوز كُليَّتُهُ الَّذِى تُؤحَدٌ عِندَ أَخْذِهِ وَهِىَ أقوَى مِن الهُدَبِ فَخَصَّهَا بِالإِعجاز الَّذِي هُوَ أَوثَقُ مِن السِّحرِ وَفِى الصَّحَاحِ السّحرُ الأخذَةُ وَكُلُّ مَا لَطْف مَاخَذُهُ وَدَقَّ فَهُوَ سِحرٌ وَمَعَنَى تَمَسُّكِهِ بِذَلِكَ مُبَالَغَتْهُ فِي تَلْطِيفِ الكَلَامِ وَتَادِيَةِ المَعَانِي بِالعِبَارَاتِ اللَّايُقَةِ الفَايْقَةِ حَتَّى كَأَنَّهُ يَتَقَرَّبُ إِلَى السِّحْرِ وَالإِعْجَازِ وَهَاهُنَا بَحثَانِ الأَوَّلُ أَنْ كَونَ طَرِيقِ تَـادِيَة المَعنى أبْلَغَ مِن جَمِيعِ مَا عَدَاهُ مِن الطُّرُقِ المُحَقَّقَةِ المَوجُودَةِ غَيْرُ كَافٍ فِى الإعجازِ بَل لَا بُدَّ مِن العَجزِ عَن مُعَارَضَتِهِ وَالإِنْيَان بِمِثْلِهِ وَمِنَ الطُّرُقِ المُحَقَّقَةِ وَالمُقَدَّرَةِ حَتَّى لَا يُمكِنَ الإِنْيَانُ بِمِثْلِهِ غَيْرُ مَشْرُوطٍ ; لِأَنَّ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى قَادِرٌ عَلَى الإِنيَانِ بِمِثْلِ القُرآنِ مَعَ كَونِهِ مُعَجِزًا فَمَا مَعَنَىٰ قَولِهِ أَبْلَغَ مِن جَمِيعِ مَا عَدَاهُ وَالثَّانِي أَنَّ الطَّرَف الأعلَى مِن البَلاغَةِ وَمَا يَقرُبُ مِنهُ مِن المَرَاتِبِ
His statement: 'I'jaz in speech is that the meaning is conveyed in a way that is more eloquent than all other ways.' This is not an interpretation of the concept of i'jaz of speech, because it is not necessary that it be through eloquence. Rather, it is an expression of speech being such that it cannot be opposed and [people] cannot produce its like. From 'a'jartuhu' when you render someone incapable. For this reason, they differed about the aspect of i'jaz of the Qur'an while agreeing that it is miraculous. Some said it is through its eloquence, some said through its informing of the unseen, some said through its unique style, and some said through Allah's preventing minds from opposing it. Rather, the intended meaning is that the i'jaz of Allah's speech is only through this way—that it is at the utmost degree of eloquence and the peak of clarity, according to the correct view. Considering that in i'jaz of speech, its being more eloquent than all other ways is a condition, it is singular with no multiplicity, unlike the sorcery of speech, for it is an expression of its subtlety and delicate origin. This occurs in multiple ways and different levels. Therefore, he said 'the fringes of sorcery' in the plural form and 'the handle of i'jaz' in the singular form. The fringe of a garment is what is on its edges, and the handle of a pitcher is its ear by which it is taken when picking it up. It is stronger than fringes, so he specified it for i'jaz, which is more reliable than sorcery. And in al-Sihah, sorcery is a snare, and everything whose origin is subtle and delicate is sorcery. The meaning of his adherence to that is his exaggeration in refining speech and conveying meanings with appropriate and excellent expressions, as if he approaches sorcery and i'jaz. Here there are two inquiries: First, that the way of conveying the meaning being more eloquent than all other verified existing ways is not sufficient for i'jaz; rather, it is necessary that [people] be incapable of opposing it and producing its like from verified and hypothetical ways, so that [they] cannot produce its like is not a condition? Because Allah is capable of producing the like of the Qur'an while it is miraculous, so what is the meaning of his statement 'more eloquent than all other ways'? And the second, that the highest level of eloquence and what is close to it from the levels...
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage is a detailed definition and analysis of i'jaz (inimitability) in speech, specifically the Qur'an. The author begins by quoting a statement that defines i'jaz as conveying meaning in the most eloquent way. He clarifies that this is not a complete definition because i'jaz necessarily involves the inability of others to produce similar speech. He then discusses various scholarly opinions on the nature of the Qur'an's inimitability: eloquence, informing of the unseen, unique style, or divine prevention of opposition. The correct view is that it is due to supreme eloquence and clarity. The author distinguishes i'jaz from 'sihr' (sorcery) in speech: i'jaz is singular and unified, while sorcery can take many forms and levels. He uses the analogy of a garment's fringes (weak) versus a pitcher's handle (strong) to show i'jaz is more reliable. He then raises two critical inquiries: first, whether being the most eloquent is sufficient for i'jaz, arguing that actual inability to imitate is required; second, discussing the highest level of eloquence.

Key Terms
الإعجاز (al-i'jaz): The quality of speech that renders opponents unable to produce its like, associated with the Qur'an
السحر (al-sihr): Speech with subtle and delicate origin that can be imitated on multiple levels
البلاغة (al-balaghah): Eloquence; conveying meaning effectively with appropriate expressions
الفصاحة (al-fasahah): Clarity and purity of speech

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Sorcery is more eloquent than i'jaz

Key Takeaway
I'jaz is the singular, inimitable quality of Qur'anic speech, defined by its unparalleled eloquence and the inability of others to imitate it.

Defining 'Asl' and Refuting Imam Razi's Definition
Defining 'asl' and using logical criteria to refute an alternative definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of asl and apply the conditions of tard and aks al-tard to critique a given definition.

Core Idea
A valid definition must exclude non-members and include all members; Imam Razi's 'muhtaj ilayh' fails the exclusion test.

This lesson explores how the Hanafi school defines a foundational term in usul al-fiqh: 'asl' (the root or origin). We will see how the author not only provides a precise definition but also demonstrates the rigorous logical conditions that any valid definition must meet. By the end, you will understand why a definition proposed by Imam al-Razi is rejected and how the Hanafi position withstands the test of 'tard' and 'aks al-tard'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its definition
Find the explicit definition of 'asl' given in the text. Note that it includes both sensory and intellectual foundations.
The definition is: 'al-asl ma tubna alayhi ghayruhu' (the asl is that upon which another is built).
2
Understand the two types of definition
The text distinguishes definitions of real essences (haqiqi) from conventional concepts (i'tibari). Determine which type applies to 'asl'.
Since 'asl' is a conventional term in usul, it is an i'tibari definition.
3
Apply the conditions of tard and aks al-tard
Explain what tard (exclusivity) and aks al-tard (comprehensiveness) mean. See the examples given for 'human' and 'writer'.
Tard prevents non-members; aks al-tard includes all members.
4
Analyze Imam Razi's definition
Imam Razi defined 'asl' as 'muhtaj ilayh' (that which is needed). Break down the five types of 'muhtaj ilayh' and see which ones are covered.
The five types: material cause, formal cause, efficient cause, final cause, conditions.
5
Identify the flaw
Determine why Imam Razi's definition fails tard. Which types of 'muhtaj ilayh' are not considered 'asl' in actual usage?
Only material cause is called asl (e.g., wood for a stool), but his definition includes all five, violating exclusivity.

الاصل ما تبنی علیہ غیرہ :۔ اصل وہ ہے جس پر غیر کی بنیاد رکھی جائے۔ تو منی کو فرع اور مبنی علیہ کو اصل کہتے ہیں اور یہاں ابتنا ء ابتغاء کی دونوں قسموں کو شامل ہے یعنی ابتنا حسی کو بھی اور ابنا عقلی کو بھی ۔

ابتنا عقلی : ابتاء علی کہتے ہیں جس کا اور اک حواس ظاہرہ نہ کرسکیں بلکہ حواس باطنہ کریں جیسے حکم مبنی ہے اور دلیل منی علیہ ہے۔
امام رازی کی تردید
و تعريفه بالمحتاج اليه لا يطرد : ۔ یہاں سے مصنف نے امام فخر الدین رازی کا رد کیا ہے۔ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ امام نے اپنی کتاب محصول میں اصل کی تعریف محتاج الیہ کے ساتھ کیا ہے ۔ کہ اصل وہ ہے جو محتاج الیہ ہو ۔ ماتن فرماتے ہیں یہ تعریف درست نہیں۔ درست کیوں نہیں ہے؟ اس کا سمجھنا تین مقدموں پر موقوف ہے۔ مقدمہ اولی: تعریف کی دو قسمیں ہیں۔ (۱) تعریف حقیقی ۔ (۲) تعریف امی ۔ (۱) تعریف حقیقی یہ ہے کہ ماھیات حقیقیہ کی تعریف کی جائے۔ (۲) تعریف امی یہ ہے کہ ماھیات اعتباریہ کی تعریف کی جائے۔ ماعیت کی تعریف: ماهیت کہتے ہیں شے کے ان اجزاء کو جن سے مل کر شے بنے ۔ پھر اگر ماهیت خارج میں پائی جائے کسی معتبر کے اعتبار کرنے سے یا فارض کے فرض کرنے سے تو یہ ماهیت اعتبار یہ ہے ۔ اور اگرشی کی ماہیت خارج میں معتبر کے اعتبار اور فارض کے فرض کرنے کے بغیر پائی جائے تو یہ ماهیت حقیقیقہ ہے ۔ ماهیت حقیقیہ کی مثال یہ ہے کہ انسان کی تعریف کی جائے حیوان ناطق کے ساتھ اور ماھیت اعتباریہ کی مثال یہ ہے کہ ہم کسی چیز کو مرکب کریں ایسے امور کے ساتھ جو امور اس ٹی کے اجزاء ہیں پھر ہم اس مرکب ھی کے لیے ایک اسم وضع کریں مثلاً لفظ اصل ہے فقہ ہے جنس و نوع وغیرہ ہیں۔ یعنی تعریف اسی میں وضاحت ہوتی ہے کہ یہ اسم کس شے کے لیے وضع ہوا ہے۔
مقدمہ ثانیہ: ۔ تعریف کی دونوں قسموں کے لیے طر د اور عکس طرد ضروری ہے۔
طرو:۔ کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ تعریف دخول غیر سے مانع ہو۔
عکس طرو:۔ کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ تعریف جامع لجميع الافراد ہو۔ پس اگر انسان کی تعریف میں حیوان ماشی کہا جائے تو اس میں طر د نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ حد تو گھوڑے گدھے پر بھی صادق آتی ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ سب حیوان ماشی ہیں لیکن ان پر محدود ( انسان صادق نہیں آرہا۔ اور اگر انسان کی تعریف میں یہ کہا جائے کہ جو حیوان کا تب بالفعل ۔ تو اسمیں عکس طرد نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ کا تب بالقوہ پر حد ( کاتب بالفعل ) صادق نہیں آرہی۔ لیکن محدود (انسان ) صادق آ رہا ہے۔
مقدمہ ثالثہ: محتاج الیہ کی پانچ قسمیں ہیں ۔ جن کی وجہ حصر یہ ہے کہ محتاج الیہ دو حال سے خالی نہیں محتاج الیہ شی میں داخل ہوگا یا داخل نہیں ہو گا۔ اگر محتاج الیہ شی میں داخل ہو تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں ۔ شی کا وجود محتاج الیہ سے بالقوہ حاصل ہوگا یا بالفعل حاصل ہوگا۔ اگر بالقوہ حاصل ہوتو علت مادیہ ہے اور اگر بالفعل حاصل ہو تو علت صور یہ ہے۔ اور اگر محتاج الیہ شی میں داخل نہ ہو بلکہ خارج ہو تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں۔ شے کا صدور محتاج الیہ سے ہو تو یہ علت فاعلیہ ہے جیسے تپائی کے لیے بڑھئی علت فاعلی ہے۔ اور اگرشی کا وجود علت کی وجہ سے ہو تو یہ علت غائیہ ہے۔ جیسے کتاب تپائی کی علت غائیہ ہے۔ اور اگر کچھ بھی نہ ہوں تو وہ ادوات شرط ہیں جیسے بڑھئی کے اوزار وغیرہ۔ اور تپائی بنانے کے لیے لکڑی کا قابل ہونا وغیرہ اب یہ سمجھیں کہ اصل کی تعریف محتاج الیہ کے ساتھ جو امام رازی نے کی ہے درست نہیں ہے۔ اس لیے کہ ان کی تعریف میں طرد نہیں پایا جارہا ہے۔ کیونکہ ان کی کی ہوئی تعریف علت کی چاروں قسموں پر صادق آتی ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ سب محتاج الیہ ہیں ۔ لیکن محدود ( اصل ) ان میں صرف علت مادیہ پر صادق آتا ہے۔ باقی کسی پر صادق نہیں آتا ۔ کہ تپائی کے لیے صرف لکڑی کو اصل کہا جاتا ہے۔ باقی اشیاء کو اصل نہیں کہا جاتا۔ خلاصہ یہ کہ امام رازی کی تعریف مطرد نہیں ہے۔
According to words, the definition that occurs is called al-hadd al-idafi. And according to meaning, the definition that occurs is called al-hadd al-laqami. So first we will explain al-hadd al-idafi. According to idafi, the definition of mudaf (the added) is separate and the definition of mudaf ilayh (the added to) is separate. So first will be the definition of mudaf i.e. usul (principles). Usul is the plural of asl (root). Asl includes both sensory and intellectual. Al-Asl is that upon which another is built. So the built is far' (branch) and that upon which it is built is asl. And here 'built' includes both types: sensory building and intellectual building. Sensory building is that where the built and that upon which it is built can be perceived with external senses, like roof is built and wall is that upon which it is built. Intellectual building is that which cannot be perceived with external senses but with internal senses, like a ruling is built and evidence is that upon which it is built. Refutation of Imam Razi: And his definition by 'needed' is not inclusive (la yatrud). The author refutes Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi. The summary is that Imam in his book al-Mahsul defined asl as that which is needed (muhtaj ilayh). The matn author says this definition is not correct. Why is it not correct? Understanding it depends on three premises. First premise: There are two types of definition: (1) haqiqi definition (2) i'tibari definition. (1) haqiqi definition is that which defines haqiqi mahiyyat. (2) i'tibari definition is that which defines i'tibari mahiyyat. Definition of mahiyyah: Mahiyyah refers to the components of a thing from which the thing is composed. Then if the mahiyyah is found externally by the consideration of a considerer or the assumption of an assumer, then it is i'tibari mahiyyah. And if the mahiyyah of a thing is found externally without the consideration of a considerer or assumption of an assumer, then it is haqiqi mahiyyah. Example of haqiqi mahiyyah: defining human as rational animal. Example of i'tibari mahiyyah: that we combine a thing with such matters that are its components, then we assign a name for that composite, like the word asl, fiqh, genus, species, etc. That is, definition clarifies for what thing this name was coined. Second premise: For both types of definition, tard and aks al-tard are necessary. Tard means that the definition prevents entry of foreign elements. Aks al-tard means that the definition includes all individuals. So if in the definition of human it is said 'walking animal', it lacks tard because this limit applies to horse, donkey, etc. because these are all walking animals, but the limited (human) does not apply to them. And if in the definition of human it is said 'that which writes with actual writing', then it lacks aks al-tard because the limit (actual writer) does not apply to potential writer, but the limited (human) does apply. Third premise: The needed (muhtaj ilayh) has five types. The reason for the enumeration is that the needed is either inside the thing or not. If the needed is inside the thing, then the existence of the thing from the needed is either potential or actual. If potential, it is material cause; if actual, it is formal cause. And if the needed is not inside the thing but outside, then the thing either originates from the needed, which is the efficient cause, like the carpenter for the stool is the efficient cause; or the existence of the thing is for the sake of the cause, which is the final cause, like the stool is the final cause of the carpenter (i.e., the purpose). And if none of these, they are instrumental conditions, like the carpenter's tools, etc., and the wood being suitable for making the stool, etc. Now understand that the definition of asl by 'needed' given by Imam Razi is not correct because his definition lacks tard. Because his definition applies to all four types of causes, as they are all 'needed'. But the limited (asl) applies only to the material cause, not to the others. For the stool, only the wood is called asl; other items are not called asl. Conclusion: Imam Razi's definition is not muttarid.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul al-fiqh lesson on defining the term 'asl' (root/origin) and critiquing Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi's definition from his work al-Mahsul. The author first distinguishes between definitions based on wording (al-hadd al-idafi) and meaning (al-hadd al-laqami). He then defines 'asl' as 'that upon which another is built' (al-asl ma tubna alayhi ghayruhu), covering both sensory and intellectual foundations. For example, a wall is the asl for a roof, and a legal evidence (dalil) is the asl for a ruling. The author then refutes Imam Razi who defined asl as 'that which is needed' (muhtaj ilayh). To demonstrate the error, he establishes three premises: (1) There are two types of definitions: haqiqi (for real essences) and i'tibari (for conventional concepts). (2) Every valid definition must be muttarid (preventive against non-members) and mun'akis (comprehensive of all members). He illustrates with examples: defining human as 'walking animal' fails tard (includes horses), and 'actual writer' fails aks (excludes potential writers). (3) 'Muhtaj ilayh' has five categories: material cause, formal cause, efficient cause, final cause, and conditions. Imam Razi's definition applies to all five, but 'asl' only refers to the material cause (e.g., wood for a stool), thus lacking tard. Hence, his definition is invalid. This lesson exemplifies Hanafi usul methodology: rigorous logical analysis of definitions and rejection of definitions that fail to be both exclusive and comprehensive.

Key Terms
أصل (asl): ما تبنى عليه غيره (that upon which another is built), including sensory and intellectual foundations.
طرد (tard): A definitional condition: the definition must exclude non-members; it should not apply to things outside the defined category.
عكس طرد (aks al-tard): The definition must include all members; it should apply to every individual that fits the defined concept.
محتاج إليه (muhtaj ilayh): That which is needed for something else; includes five types: material cause, formal cause, efficient cause, final cause, and conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is Imam Razi's definition of 'asl' as 'muhtaj ilayh' rejected in this passage?
A) It fails to be comprehensive (aks al-tard).
B) It fails to be exclusive (tard).
C) It is a haqiqi definition when it should be i'tibari.
D) It includes only the material cause.

Key Takeaway
A valid definition must be both exclusive (tard) and comprehensive (aks al-tard); the Hanafi definition of 'asl' satisfies these conditions, while Imam Razi's does not.

Definition of Usul al-Fiqh: The Linguistic Meaning of 'Asl'
Definition of Usul al-Fiqh: defending the linguistic meaning of 'asl'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of Usul al-Fiqh and explain why the linguistic meaning of 'asl' as 'foundation' is sufficient, using the concept of intellectual 'ibtina'. You will also be able to evaluate the argument against equating 'asl' with 'dalil' in this definition.

Core Idea
'Asl' in Usul al-Fiqh means 'foundation', and this already includes proof without needing a technical transfer.

This passage from a Hanafi usul commentary defends the classical definition of Usul al-Fiqh by examining the linguistic meaning of 'asl' and the relation (idafa) between its parts. The commentator engages with an alternative view that 'asl' here should be interpreted as 'proof' (dalil) in the technical sense. By understanding this argument, you will appreciate why the Hanafi school insists on the literal definition and how it grounds the entire discipline.

Guided Path
1
Identify the components of the definition
Note that 'Usul al-Fiqh' is a compound. The commentator explains that defining it requires defining its parts: 'asl', 'fiqh', and the relation (idafa) between them. The relation is like a formal part, though often omitted because it is understood.
The relation specifies that 'asl' is specific to fiqh in the sense of being its foundation.
2
Understand the linguistic meaning of 'asl'
The commentator defines 'asl' linguistically as 'that upon which something is built, with the qualification that it is built upon it' (qayd al-haythiyya). This excludes cases where something is merely a basis in another respect (e.g., fiqh proofs are built on tawhid, so they are branches from that perspective, not roots).
The restriction 'from the perspective of being built upon' is crucial for relational terms.
3
Contrast with transferred meanings
The commentator notes that 'asl' was later transferred in convention to mean 'preponderant', 'universal rule', and 'proof'. Some scholars argued that in the definition of Usul al-Fiqh, 'asl' means 'proof' (dalil). The author signals that this transfer is contrary to the original linguistic usage.
The author's phrase 'transfer is contrary to the original' indicates a preference for the literal meaning.
4
Analyze the author's argument against the transferred meaning
The author argues that the linguistic meaning of 'asl' as 'foundation' is sufficient because 'ibtina' (building upon) includes both physical and intellectual types. The relationship between a ruling and its proof is an example of intellectual ibtina'. Thus, the linguistic sense already covers the intended concept of 'proof' without needing to resort to a technical transfer.
The key point: intellectual ibtina' is broader than just the ruling-proof relationship; it also includes metaphor, particular rules on universal rules, etc.
5
Address the objection and evaluate the response
A potential objection: 'ibtina' is always intellectual, so why not just take the technical meaning? The author responds by clarifying that physical ibtina' is conventionally understood as sensible placement, and intellectual ibtina' includes abstract relationships. The truth is that the ruling-proof relationship is only an example, not the definition of intellectual ibtina'. Therefore, the linguistic sense is more comprehensive and should be retained.
This demonstrates a method of defending a definition by showing its sufficiency and the lack of necessity for a narrower technical meaning.

الْغَيْرِ الْبَيِّنَةِ ضَرُورَةَ تَوَقُفِ مَعْرِفَةِ الْكُلِّ عَلَى مَعْرِفَةِ أَجْزَائِهِ وَيَحْتَاجُ إِلَى تَعْرِيفِ الْإِضَافَةِ أَيْضًا ، لأَنَّهَا بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْجُزْء الصُّورِى إِلَّا أَنَّهُمْ لَمْ يَتَعَرَّضُوا لَهُ لِلْعِلْمِ بِأَنَّ ؛ مَعْنَى إِضَافَةِ الْمُشْتَقِّ وَمَا فِي مَعْنَاهُ اخْتِصَاصُ الْمُصَافِ إِلَيْهِ بِاعْتِبَارِ مَفهُومٍ الْمُصَافِ مَثَلًا دَلِيلُ الْمَسْأَلَةِ مَا بِهَذَا الْاعْتِبَارِ فُرُوعٌ لَا أُصُولٌ وَقَيدُ الْحَيْثِيَّةِ لَا بُدَّ مِنْهُ فِي تَعْرِيفِ الْإِضَافِيَّاتِ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ كَثِيرًا مَا يُحْذَفَ لِشُهْرَةِ أَمْرِهِ ، ثُمَّ نُقِلَ الْأَصْلُ فِي الْعُرْفِ إِلَى مَعَانِ أُخَرَ ، مِثْلُ الرَّاحِحِ وَالْقَاعِدَةِ الْكُلِّيَّةِ وَالدَّلِيلِ فَذَهَبَ بَعْضُهُمُ إلَى أَنَّ الْمُرَادَ هَاهُنَا الدَّلِيلُ وَأَشَارَ الْمُصَنِّفُ إلَى أَنَّ النَّقْلَ خِلاف الأَصْلِ وَلَا ضَرُورَةَ فِي الْعُدُولِ إِلَيْهِ ؛ لأنَّ الِابْتِنَاء كَمَا يَشْمَلُ الْحِسْيَّ كَابْتِنَاء السَّقْفِ عَلَى الْجُدْرَانِ وَابْتِنَاء أَعَالِي الْجُدْرَانِ عَلَى أَسَاسِهِ وَأَغْصَانِ الشَّجَرِةِ عَلَى دَوْحَتِهِ كَذَلِكَ يَشْمَلُ الابْتِنَاء الْعَقْلِى كَابْتِنَاءِ الْحُكُم عَلَى دَلِيلِهِ فَهَهُنَا يُحْمَلُ عَلَى الْمَعْنَى اللُّغَوِى وَبِالْإِضَافَةِ إِلَى الْفِقْهِ الَّذِي هُوَ مَعْنِّى عَقْلِيٌّ يُعْلَمُ أَنَّ الابْتِنَاءَ هُنَا عَقْلِيٌّ فَيَكُونُ أُصُولُ الْفِقْهِ مَا يُبْتَنى هُوَ عَلَيْهِ وَيُسْتَنَدُ إِلَيْهِ وَلَا مَعْنَى لِمُسْتَنَدِ الْعِلْمِ وَمُبْتَنَاهُ إِلَّا دَلِيلُهُ وَبِهَذَا يَنْدَفِعُ مَا يُقَالُ إِنَّ الْمَعْنَى الْعُرْفِيَّ أَعْنِي الدَّلِيلَ مُرَادٌ قَطعًا فَأَيُّ حَاجَةٍ إِلَى جَعْلِهِ بِالْمَعْنَى اللُّغَوِيِّ الشَّامِلِ لِلْمَقْصُودِ وَغَيْرِهِ فَإِن قُلْتَ : ابْتِنَاء الشَّيْء عَلَى الشَّيْء إِضَافَةٌ بَيْنَهُمَا ، وَهُوَ أَمْرٌ عَقْلِيٌّ قَطعًا قُلْتُ أَرَادَ بِالابْتِنَاءِ الْحِسَى كَوْنَ الشَّيْئَيْنِ مَحْسُوسَيْنِ وَحِينَئِذٍ يَدْخُلُ فِيهِ مِثْلُ ابْتِنَاء السَّقْفِ عَلَى الْجِدَارِ وَابْتِنَاءِ الْمُشْتَقَ عَلَى الْمُشْتَقِّ مِنْهُ كَالْفِعْلِ عَلَى أَرَادَ مَا هُوَ الْمُعْتَبَرُ فِى الْعُرْفِ مِنْ أَنَّ ابْتِنَاءَ السَّقْفِ عَلَى الْجِدَارِ بِمَعْنَى كَوْنِهِ مَبْنِيًّا عَلَيْهِ وَمَوْضُوعًا فَوْقَهُ مِمَّا يُدْرَكَ بِالْحِس وَحِينَئِذٍ يَخْرُجُ مِثْلُ ابْتِنَاءِ الْفِعْلِ عَلَى الْمَصْدَرِ مِنْ الْحِسَى وَلَا يَدْخُلُ فِي الْعَقْلِي بِتَفْسِيرِهِ وَالْحَقُّ أَنَّ تَرَتَّبَ الْحُكْمِ عَلَى دَلِيلِهِ لَا يَصْلُحُ تَفْسِيرًا لِلابْتِنَاء الْعَقْلِي ، وَإِنَّمَا هُوَ مِثَالٌ لَهُ لِلْقَطْعِ بِأَنَّ ابْتِنَاء الْمَجَازِ عَلَى الْحَقِيقَةِ وَالْأَحْكَامِ الْجُزْئِيَّةِ عَلَى الْقَوَاعِدِ الْكُلِّيَّةِ وَالْمَعْلُولَاتِ عَلَى عِلَيْهَا وَالأفْعَالِ عَلَى الْمَصَادِر وَمَا أَشْبَهَ ذَلِكَ ابْتِنَاءٌ عَقْلِيٌّ

ترجمہ: قولہ اما تعریبا الخ بہر حال اسکی تعریف اضافت کیسا تھ پر محتاج ہوگی مضاف کی تعریف کرنے کی طرف اور وہ سول ہے اور مضاف الیہ کی تعریف کرنے کی طرف اور وہ فقہ ہے اسلیئے کہ مرکب کی تعریف محتاج ہوتی ہے اپنے مفردات غیر بینہ کی تعریف کی طرف بوجہ بدیہی ہونے کل کی معرفت کے موقوف ہونے کے اپنے اجزاء کی معرفت پر اور محتاج ہوگی اضافت کی تعریف کرنے کی طرف بھی اسلیئے کہ وہ بمنزلہ جزو صوری کے ہے مگر بے شک وہ نہیں در پے ہوئے اسکی طرف بوجہ معلوم ہونے اس کے کہ مشتق اور اسکے ہم معنی کی اضافت کا مطلب مضاف کا خاص ہوتا ہے مضاف الیہ کے ساتھ مضاف کے مفہوم کے اعتبار سے مثلاً دلیل المسئلہ وہ ہے کہ مختص ہو اس کے ساتھ اس کے دلیل ہونے کے اعتبار سے اس پر ۔ پس فقہ کی اصل وہ ہے کہ جو شخص ہو اس فقہ کے ساتھ اس حیثیت سے کہ بے شک منی ہو فقہ اس پر اور منسوب ہو اسکی طرف۔ پس اصول جمع ہے اصل کی اور و و لغت میں وہ ہے کہ مبنی ہو اس پر کوئی تھی اس حیثیت سے کہ وہ پینی ہے اس پر اور اس قید کے ساتھ نکل جائیں گی ادلتہ فقہ مثلاً اس حیثیت سے کہ وہ مبنی ہوں علم تو حید پر پس وہ اس اعتبار کے ساتھ فرع ہیں نہ کہ اصول۔ اور حیثیت کی قید ضروری ہے اضافیات کی تعریف میں مگر بے شک کثرت سے اس کو حذف کیا جاتا ہے اس کے امر کی شہرت کی وجہ سے پھر نقل کیا گیا ہے اصل کو عرف میں دوسرے معانی کی طرف مثل راج قاعدہ کلیہ اور دلیل پس چلے گئے ان میں سے بعض اس بات کی طرف کہ بیشک مراد اس کے ساتھ یہاں دلیل ہے اور اشارہ کیا مصنف نے اس بات کی طرف کہ بے شک نقل خلاف اصل ہے اور نہیں ہے کوئی ضرورت عدول کرنے میں اسکی طرف اس لئے کہ ابتاء جس طرح مشتمل ہوتی ہے حسی کو جیسے چھت کا بنی ہونا دیواروں پر اور دیواروں کے اوپر والے حصوں کا مبنی ہونا اسکی بنیادوں پر اور درخت کی شاخوں کا اس کے تنے پر اسی طرح شامل ہوتا ہے ابتائے عقلی کو جیسے حکم کا بنی ہونا اس کی دلیل پر پس یہاں محمول کیا جائے گا معنی اموی پر اور اضافت کرنے کے ساتھ اس کی فقہ کی طرف جو معنی عقلی ہے معلوم ہو جاتا ہے کہ بے شک اجتماء یہاں عقلی ہے۔ پس اصول فقہ وہ ہے جس پر فقہ مبنی
[Arabic:] ...necessity of the knowledge of the whole being dependent on knowledge of its parts; and it also needs a definition of the relation (idafa), because it is like a formal part — except that they did not address it because it is known that the meaning of the relation of the derived word and its equivalents is the specification of the related thing to the other in consideration of the concept of the related. For example, the proof of a matter is what is specific to it in consideration of being a proof for it. So the 'asl' of fiqh is what is specific to it in that it is built upon and based on it. So 'usul' is the plural of 'asl', and in language it is that upon which something is built, in the sense that it is built upon it. With this restriction, the proofs of fiqh, for example, are excluded from the perspective that they are built upon the science of tawhid; thus in that respect they are branches, not roots. The restriction of 'perspective' is necessary in definitions of relational terms, though it is often dropped due to its fame. Then 'asl' was transferred in convention to other meanings, such as the preponderant, the universal rule, and the proof. So some went to the view that what is intended here is the proof, and the author indicated that transfer is contrary to the original, and there is no necessity to deviate to it. Because 'ibtina'' (foundation) includes both physical — like the roof being built on walls, the upper parts of walls on their base, and branches on a tree trunk — and intellectual, like a ruling being built on its proof. So here it is taken in the linguistic sense, and by its relation to fiqh, which is an intellectual meaning, it is known that the ibtina' here is intellectual. Thus usul al-fiqh is that upon which fiqh is built and to which it is attributed. And there is no meaning for 'that which knowledge depends on and is built upon' except its proof. With this, the objection is repelled that the conventional meaning, i.e., proof, is definitely intended, so what need to take it in the linguistic sense that includes both the intended and other? If you say: 'The ibtina' of a thing on another is a relation between them, and it is definitely an intellectual matter,' I say: He intended by physical ibtina' the two things being sensible; then it includes the roof on the wall and the derived upon its source like the verb on... He intended what is conventionally considered: that the roof on the wall means it is built upon and placed above it, which is perceived by sense. Then similar things like the verb on the masdar are excluded from the physical, and not included in the intellectual by that interpretation. The truth is that the dependence of a ruling on its proof is not a suitable interpretation for intellectual ibtina'; it is merely an example of it — since it is certain that the ibtina' of metaphor on literal meaning, of particular rulings on universal rules, of effects on their causes, and of actions on their sources, and the like, is intellectual. [Urdu translation of the above Arabic passage.]
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the definition of Usul al-Fiqh. The author begins by establishing that a definition of a compound term like 'Usul al-Fiqh' requires defining its parts (asl and fiqh) and the relation (idafa) between them. The commentator then defines 'asl' etymologically as 'that upon which something is built' and emphasizes the importance of the qualification 'from the perspective of being built upon' (haythiyya) to exclude cases where something is merely a basis in another respect (e.g., the proofs of fiqh are built on tawhid, so they are branches from that perspective, not roots). The central argument of the passage is against those who hold that 'asl' in this context means 'proof' (dalil) in the technical sense. The commentator argues that the linguistic definition already encompasses the notion of proof because intellectual 'building upon' (ibtina' 'aqli) is exactly the relationship between a ruling and its proof. Therefore, there is no need to resort to the transferred technical meaning. The author refutes a potential objection: even if ibtina' is inherently intellectual, the term can still be applied to physical examples, and the true understanding of intellectual ibtina' is broader than just the ruling-proof relationship—it includes metaphor, particular rules, effects, and actions. This demonstrates that the definition of Usul al-Fiqh as 'the foundations upon which fiqh is built' is perfectly sound and covers the intended scope without recourse to a specialized definition. The Urdu translation that follows confirms this understanding, explaining each point in Urdu for the benefit of students.

Key Terms
أصل (asl): That upon which something is built, in the sense of being its foundation; here, the linguistic meaning is defended over the transferred meaning of 'proof'.
دليل (dalil): Proof; the technical meaning some scholars assign to 'asl' in the definition of Usul al-Fiqh.
ابتناء (ibtina'): Foundation; the act of building upon something. Used both physically (e.g., roof on wall) and intellectually (e.g., ruling on proof).
حيثية (haythiyya): Perspective or consideration; a necessary qualification in relational definitions to specify the aspect under which the relation holds.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, why is it unnecessary to interpret 'asl' in 'Usul al-Fiqh' as 'dalil' (proof)?
A) Because the linguistic meaning of 'asl' as 'foundation' already includes the notion of a proof through intellectual ibtina'.
B) Because the term 'asl' is never used in the sense of 'proof' in Hanafi works.
C) Because the definition only concerns physical foundations, not intellectual ones.
D) Because the commentator prefers the Shafi'i definition.

Key Takeaway
The definition of Usul al-Fiqh does not require treating 'asl' as a technical term; its linguistic sense as 'foundation' is sufficient because intellectual ibtina' already includes the concept of proof and much more.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
Definition of Asl and the Need for the Aspect Qualifier
Defines 'asl' and explains the necessity of the aspect qualifier in usul definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify why the qualification of 'haythiyya' is necessary in defining 'asl' and apply the Hanafi preference for the literal meaning over the conventional meaning in usul definitions.

Core Idea
The definition of 'asl' requires an aspect qualifier to exclude the sources' aspect as branches of kalam; the literal meaning is preferred because it is haqiqah and not impossible.

In usul al-fiqh, precision in definitions is crucial. One key term is 'asl' (principle). This passage explains why the definition of 'asl' must include a qualification of aspect (haythiyya) to avoid including the four sources in their capacity as branches of kalam. It then defends the literal meaning of 'asl' as 'foundation' over the conventional 'proof', using the Hanafi principle that haqiqah is preferred over majaz unless necessary.

Guided Path
1
Understand the necessity of 'haythiyya'
Recognise that the four sources have two aspects: as foundations for fiqh rulings (principles) and as branches of kalam (branches). Without the aspect qualifier, the definition would apply in both aspects, causing inclusion of what is not intended.
The qualifier restricts the definition to the respect in which they are principles.
2
Recognise the omission of 'haythiyya' due to notoriety
Definitions of relational terms often omit well-known qualifiers because of their notoriety. The original author of al-Tawdih omitted it, but that is acceptable.
This is a common practice in usul definitions.
3
Analyze the dispute over literal vs. conventional meaning
Identify the two positions: some scholars take 'asl' conventionally as 'proof', while the author of al-Tawdih and the commentator take it literally as 'foundation'. Understand each proof.
The debate hinges on whether haqiqah or majaz is used.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi preference
Apply the rule that haqiqah is used unless impossible. Show that adding 'asl' to 'fiqh' restricts the literal meaning to intellectual foundation, making the literal meaning perfectly suitable and avoiding unnecessary metaphor.
This reasoning supports the literal meaning.
