معنی قطعی طور پر مراد ہونا چاہیے؟ جواب :۔ ٹھیک ہے لغت کے اعتبار سے اصول کی تعریف دونوں کو شامل ہے لیکن جب فقہ کی طرف اسکی نسبت کریں گے تو صرف ابنتناء عقلی مراد ہوگا کیونکہ فقہ ایک علم ہے اور علم کا مبنی علیہ دلیل ہی ہوتی ہے۔ ابتناء مقولہ اضافت سے ہے فان قلت:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا آٹھواں حصہ ہے اس میں شاریخ نے ایک سوال ذکر کے اسکا جواب دیا ہے آپ نے کہا الاصل مايبتنى عليه غيره یعنی اصل ابتناء کا نام ہے اور ابتناء مقولہ اضافت کی قبیل سے ہے اور اضافت کا مطلب ہے نسبت اور ہوتی تو اور کی مین الشیمین اور نسبت صرف عقلی ہی ہوتی ہے جسی نہیں ہوتی تو ابتناء کو حسی اور عقلی کی طرف تقسیم کرنا کیسے درست ہو سکتا ہے۔
With this qualification: This is the fourth part of the commentary's expression; its purpose is to answer an implied question. Question: Why did you include the qualification of 'aspect' (haythiyya) in the definition? Answer: If we did not include the qualification of aspect, the definition would not prevent the entry of what is not [the intended meaning]. This is because the four sources (adillah arba'ah) have two aspects: (1) They are the foundation for particular rulings – in this respect they are principles (usul). (2) They themselves are founded upon the science of kalam – in this respect they are branches (furu'), not principles. So if we did not qualify by aspect and said 'al-asl ma yabtani 'alayhi ghayruh' (the principle is that upon which something else is built), this definition would apply absolutely to the four sources, whereas in one respect they are not principles but branches. In definitions, due to notoriety, the qualification of aspect is omitted. ... 'illa annahu kathirun amma hadhf': This is the fifth part of the commentary; its purpose is to answer an implied question. Question: If the qualification of aspect was necessary in the definition, why did the author (al-matin) not mention it? Answer: The definition of 'asl' belongs to the category of definitions of relational terms, and in these the qualification of aspect is necessary, but because this matter is well-known, the qualification of aspect is omitted due to notoriety; thus the author also did not mention it due to notoriety. The disagreement of usuliyyun regarding the intended meaning of 'asl': 'madhhab tahsim': This is the sixth part of the commentary; its purpose is to mention a disagreement. There is a disagreement between the author of al-Tawdih and some scholars whether the literal or conventional meaning of 'asl' is intended in usul al-fiqh. According to the author of al-Tawdih, the literal meaning is intended, and according to some scholars, the conventional meaning (i.e., dalil) is intended. So according to the author of al-Tawdih, the meaning of usul al-fiqh is 'that upon which fiqh is based', and according to the others, it is 'the proofs of fiqh'. The proof of the others: If the literal meaning is taken, the literal meaning is 'foundation' (ibtina'), and this foundation includes both sensory and intellectual [types]. And [the literal meaning] includes both the intended and unintended. If the conventional meaning (proof) is taken, it applies only to the intended, because usul al-fiqh is a science in which only proofs are discussed, and it is obvious that the meaning that indicates only the intended should be taken, and that is the conventional meaning. The proof of the author of al-Tawdih: The commentator supports the author of al-Tawdih with this proof: The literal meaning is the true (haqiqah) and the conventional meaning is metaphorical (majaz). Metaphorical meaning is taken only due to necessity when the true meaning is not possible, and here there is no necessity because the true meaning is not impossible. Because the literal (true) meaning – that upon which something else is built – is foundation (ibtina'), and it has two types: (1) sensory foundation, like the roof's foundation on walls, the top part's foundation on the foundation, and branches' foundation on the trunk of a tree; (2) intellectual foundation, like rulings' foundation on proofs, the effect's foundation on its cause, actions' foundation on sources, particular rulings' foundation on general principles, and metaphor's foundation on literal meaning. All of these are included in both types. But here the intended is intellectual foundation, and the evidence for that is that here 'asl' is being added to 'fiqh', and fiqh is an intellectual matter because it is the name of knowledge, and knowledge is not a sensory thing. So the addition to an intellectual meaning is evidence that here intellectual foundation is intended. Therefore, the intended is achieved and the true meaning is also achieved, contrary to the opinion of some scholars that in this case the intended would be achieved but the true meaning would not be achieved, necessitating the use of metaphor without necessity. 'wa bihadha indafa'a al-kh': This is the seventh part of the commentary; its purpose is to answer an implied question. Question: If we take the conventional meaning, it indicates only the intended, and if we take the literal meaning, it indicates both the intended and unintended, because foundation (ibtina') is not only the intended; only intellectual foundation is intended. So why should the conventional meaning not be taken definitively? Answer: True, from a linguistic perspective, the definition of 'asl' includes both, but when we relate it to fiqh, only intellectual foundation is intended, because fiqh is knowledge, and the foundation of knowledge is proof. 'Ibtina' is from the category of relation (idafah). 'fa-in qulta': This is the eighth part of the commentary; in it the commentator mentions a question and answers it. You said 'al-asl ma yabtani 'alayhi ghayruh' meaning the principle is called foundation, and foundation is from the category of relation. And relation means correlation, and it exists between two things, and relation is only intellectual, not sensory. How, then, can foundation be divided into sensory and intellectual?
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the definition of 'asl' (principle/origin) in usul al-fiqh, from a commentary on al-Tawdih. The author first explains why the qualification of 'aspect' (haythiyya) is necessary in the definition of 'asl'. Without it, the definition 'that upon which something else is built' would apply to the four sources (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) in all respects, whereas in one respect they themselves are built upon kalam, so they are branches, not principles. Hence the aspect qualifier restricts the definition to the relevant aspect. The commentator then addresses why the original author omitted this qualifier: because definitions of relational terms often omit well-known qualifiers due to their notoriety. Next, a dispute is presented: whether 'asl' in usul al-fiqh is meant literally (foundation) or conventionally (proof). Some scholars argue for the conventional meaning because it directly points to the object of discussion (proofs). The commentator supports the author of al-Tawdih, who holds the literal meaning. The argument is that literal meaning is the true (haqiqah) while conventional is metaphorical (majaz); metaphor is only used when the literal is impossible. Here the literal meaning of 'asl' as 'foundation' is not impossible; it includes both sensory and intellectual foundation, but when added to 'fiqh' (an intellectual science), it becomes restricted to intellectual foundation. Thus both the intended meaning and the true literal meaning are preserved. Finally, a question is raised: if foundation (ibtina') is a relational concept, and all relations are intellectual, how can it be divided into sensory and intellectual? The response would be that the division is based on the nature of the things founded, not on the relation itself, but the text ends with the question, leaving the answer implied from the earlier discussion.

Key Terms
الأصل (al-asl): That upon which something else is built; in usul al-fiqh, the foundations (adillah arba'ah) from which rulings are derived, but with the qualification of aspect (being considered as principles for fiqh, not as branches of kalam).
الحيطة (al-haythiyya): A qualification of aspect or respect, used in definitions of relational terms to restrict the definition to a particular respect in which the term applies.
الابتناء (al-ibtina'): Foundation or being built upon; it is the act of something being established upon another. It has two types: sensory (physical) and intellectual (rational).
الحقيقة (al-haqiqah): The original, literal meaning of a word as established in language.
المجاز (al-majaz): The metaphorical or transferred meaning of a word, used when the literal meaning is not possible or impractical.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the qualification of 'aspect' (haythiyya) necessary in the definition of 'asl' according to the commentary?
A) To distinguish between sensory and intellectual foundations.
B) Because the four sources (adillah arba'ah) have two aspects: as foundations for fiqh and as branches of kalam; without the qualifier they would be considered principles in all respects including when they are branches.
C) To limit the definition to the four sources only.
D) Because matan al-Tawdih omitted it and the commentator decided to include it.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the definition of 'asl' requires an aspect qualifier to restrict its application to the four sources as principles for fiqh, and the literal meaning (foundation) is preferred over the conventional (proof) because it is haqiqah and can be contextually restricted.

Definition of Asl and Objections in Usul Definitions
Defining 'asl' and addressing objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between nominal and real definitions in Hanafi usul, state the Hanafi view on tarid in nominal definitions, and evaluate objections regarding the definition of 'asl'.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school defines 'asl' nominally; tarid is only required for real definitions, not nominal ones.

In this passage from Altarwih, the commentator explains why the definition of 'asl' (origin) is nominal, and addresses objections from other scholars. Understanding the distinction between real and nominal definitions is essential for proper legal reasoning. This lesson examines the criteria for defining foundational terms in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its definition type
Recognize that the passage defines 'asl' as a nominal (ismi) definition, not a real (haqiqi) one. Note the linguistic basis: 'asl' is a relational term coined for something upon which another is built or to which another is in need.
Nominal definitions describe the meaning without full essential attributes.
2
Understand the condition of tarid
Tarid (co-extensiveness) and its converse are required for real definitions. The Hanafi position holds that nominal definitions do not require tarid. The passage cites linguistic dictionaries as evidence.
Verbal definitions (ta'rif lafzi) also do not require tarid.
3
Analyze objections to the definition
Four objections are listed. Focus on the first: the objection that tarid should be required. The response distinguishes between nominal and real definitions. Also the second objection: that the definition 'that upon which another is built' could apply to efficient cause. The response clarifies 'foundational building' excludes efficient cause.
The passage provides answers for each objection.
4
Apply the two conditions for 'asl'
The passage concludes with two essential conditions for something to be an 'asl': (1) it must be foundational for another (mabni 'alayh), and (2) the term 'asl' must be linguistically applicable to it.
Efficient cause is not linguistically called 'asl' for the action.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: In fiqh, when defining terms like 'water is tahir', Hanafi allows broader definitions without tarid, while others may require more precision. This affects the scope of legal rulings derived from such definitions.
The dispute is between Hanafi and some mutakallimun.

ثانیہا: اعتراض (۲):۔ دوسرے اعتراض کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ جس طرح محتاج الیہ کی تعریف علت فاعلی پر صادق آتی ہے اسی طرح ما تنبلی علیہ غیر کی تعریف بھی صادق آتی ہے کیونکہ ابتنا ء کا یہی معنی ہے کہ ایک شئی پر اس کا غیر مرتب ہو اور فعل بھی فاعل پر مرتب ہوتا ہے گویا کہ آپ کی تعریف بھی دخول غیر سے مانع نہ ہوئی تو پھر آپ نے صاحب محصول پر اعتراض کیوں کیا؟ جواب: ابتناء سے مراد ابناء اساسی ہے یعنی ایک چیز دوسری کے لئے بنیاد ہو اور فعل میں فاعل مؤثر تو ہے لیکن اس کے لئے بنیاد نہیں ہے لھذ اما بیتی عالیہ غیرہ والی تعریف صرف علت مادی پر صادق آئی نہ کہ علت فاعلی پر۔ خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ اصل کے لئے دو چیزوں کا ہونا بہت ضروری ہے۔ (1) اصل غیر کے لئے بینی علیہ ہو۔ (۲) لغت میں بھی اس پر اصل کا اطلاق ہوتا ہو۔ یہاں ایک چیز تو پائی جاتی ہے کہ فاعل پر فعل کا ترتب ہے اور فعل فاعل کی طرف مستند ہے لیکن دوسری بات موجود نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ لغت میں فعل کے لئے فاعل کو اصل نہیں کہا جاتا ۔
Third (objection): Indeed, the speech of the author in the chapter on metaphor indicates that at the time of occurrence of originality and dependency, every needed thing is the origin. Fourth (objection): Indeed, when we said that thought is the arrangement of known matters, there is no doubt that known matters are the material for thought and the origin for it, despite the fact that thought's being based on them is neither sensory nor intellectual according to the author's interpretation, and the ruling is arranged upon the proof. Why the definition of origin is nominal? His statement 'no doubt': This is the first part of the commentary's expression, in which the commentator explained the reason for the definition of origin being nominal: that the word 'origin' in language was coined for a composite mental concept with an added attribute, i.e., something upon which something else is built or something to which another is in need. And whichever definition has a mental reality, that is a nominal definition. His statement 'so this': This is the second part, in which the objector objected to the author. The gist of the objection is that the author's saying that the definition of origin is nominal—there was no need to mention it, because tarid and its converse are conditions for it, and also conditions for a real definition. Answer: It is possible that the author only mentioned it for the purpose of increasing knowledge, that the definition of origin is nominal, without intending it as a condition, i.e., he did not stipulate that tarid and its reverse are only conditions for a nominal definition. So no objection. His statement 'in summary': This is the third part, in which the commentator clarified the objection of the author against the author of al-Mahsul, the gist of which is that defining origin as 'that which is needed' is not correct, because the definition of 'needed' applies to material cause, formal cause, efficient cause, final cause, and conditional instruments, whereas origin is only called the material, not the others. So the definition applies but the defined does not; hence this definition does not prevent foreign entry, so tarid is not achieved. The rest of the definition of the part has passed in the text. [Page 205] The commentary on the objections of the objector to the author and their answers. Here is a discussion: This is the last part, in which the historian transmitted four objections against the author. First objection (1): In this expression, the commentator transmitted the first objection that the author said that tarid is a condition in definitions, especially nominal definitions; we do not accept that, because the verifiers have explicitly stated that imperfect definitions can be made with a general word, because sometimes the intended distinction from something specific is achieved through interpretation, and this distinction is obtained via interpretation. For example, when distinction between origin and branch is intended, it is permissible to define origin as 'that which is needed' so that the definition becomes general, applying to both the known and the unknown. Thus it becomes known that tarid is not a condition. This is why dictionaries are filled with interpretations of words with general terms. Answer: If the interpretation of a word is through something general, it is called a verbal definition, not a nominal definition; and in verbal definitions, tarid is not a condition, unlike nominal definitions where tarid is a condition. The summary is that this claim of the commentator is the first proof. Second objection (2): The gist of the second objection is that just as the definition of 'needed' applies to efficient cause, similarly the definition of 'that upon which another is built' also applies, because building means that something else is arranged upon it, and the action is also arranged upon the agent. So your definition also does not prevent foreign entry; then why did you object to the author of al-Mahsul? Answer: By 'building' is meant foundational building, i.e., one thing being a foundation for another. In the action, the agent is effective but not a foundation. Therefore, the definition of 'that upon which another is built' applies only to material cause, not efficient cause. The summary is that for origin, two things are essential: (1) the origin must be foundational for another, (2) in language, the term 'origin' must apply to it. Here, one thing is present: the arrangement of the action upon the agent and its attribution to the agent, but the second is absent, because in language, the agent is not called the origin of the action.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage from Altarwih explains the definition of 'asl' (original) and addresses several objections regarding its definition in usul al-fiqh. The discussion begins by establishing that the definition of 'asl' is a nominal (ismi) definition, not a real (haqiqi) definition. This is because 'asl' in language was coined for a relational concept: something upon which another thing is built (ma yubna 'alayhi ghayruhu) or that to which something else is in need (ma yuhtaj ilayhi ghayruhu). The commentator then clarifies why this matters: nominal definitions have different conditions than real definitions. Specifically, the condition of tarid (co-extensiveness) and 'aks al-tarid (counter-extensiveness) apply only to real definitions, not necessarily to nominal ones. The passage then presents four objections raised by the author of al-Tawdih against the definition of 'asl' given in al-Mahsul. The first objection argues that tarid is not a condition in nominal definitions, citing linguistic dictionaries where words are often defined with broader terms. The response distinguishes between verbal definitions (ta'rif lafzi) and nominal definitions, stating that tarid is only required in the latter. The second objection points out that the definition 'that upon which another is built' could apply to efficient causes as well, not just material causes. The answer clarifies that 'ibna' (building) here means foundational building, not mere arrangement, so only material cause qualifies. The passage concludes by emphasizing two requirements for a true 'asl': it must be foundational (mabni 'alayh) and the term must be linguistically applied to it. This reflects the Hanafi usul approach of precise terminology and conditions for legal definitions.

Key Terms
أصل (asl): That upon which something else is built or that which is needed by something else; the foundation or source.
تعريف اسمي (ta'rif ismi): A nominal definition that explains the meaning of a term without requiring full essential attributes.
طرد (tarid): Co-extensiveness: the definition applies to all instances of the defined term.
عكس الطرد ('aks al-tarid): Counter-extensiveness: the definition excludes all non-instances.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Nominal definitions require tarid; real definitions do not.
B) Nominal definitions are based on mental composites and do not require tarid; real definitions require tarid.
C) Nominal definitions are used only for legal terms; real definitions are used for physical objects.
D) Both types require the same conditions.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position that 'asl' is a nominal definition means that tarid is not a necessary condition, which influences how foundational terms are defined in fiqh.

Definition of Fiqh According to Abu Hanifa
Classic definition of fiqh from Abu Hanifa with commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of fiqh and explain why the word 'action' is added to exclude theology and mysticism.

Core Idea
Fiqh is knowing what benefits and harms the soul in the Hereafter, derived from evidence — not theology or inner states.

In the Hanafi school, fiqh is not simply a set of rulings; it is a specific kind of knowledge. Imam Abu Hanifa defined it as 'the soul's knowledge of what is for it and against it,' with the crucial addition of 'action' to separate law from theology and spirituality. This lesson unpacks that classic definition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core terms
Break down the Arabic definition: الفقه معرفة النفس ما لها وما عليها. Note the three key components: knowledge (معرفة), the soul (النفس), and the phrase 'what is for it and what is against it'.
This is a transmitted definition from Abu Hanifa.
2
Understand the addition of 'action'
The word 'عملًا' is added to explicitly exclude theological beliefs (اعتقادیات) and inner spiritual states (وجدانیات), thus removing kalam and tasawwuf from the scope of fiqh.
Some definitions omit 'action' to include all rulings, but the Hanafi position emphasizes the practical nature.
3
Define 'knowledge' (معرفة) in this context
Ma'rifa is defined as perception of particulars (جزئیات) derived from evidence (دلیل). This excludes general theological knowledge like tawhid.
This distinguishes fiqh from mere belief or speculation.
4
Interpret 'what is for it and against it'
This refers to actions that benefit or harm the soul in the Hereafter, as derived from Quranic usage (Surah Al-Baqarah 2:286).
It indicates practical responsibilities, not theoretical truths.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
توضیح (وَالفِقهُ مَعرِفَةُ النَّفْسِ مَا لَهَا وَمَا عَلَيْهَا وَيُزَادُ عَمَلًا لِيُخْرِجَ الْاعْتِقَادِيَّات والوجدانيات فَيَخْرُجُ الكَلامُ وَالتَّصَرُّف وَمَن لَم يَزِد أَرَادَ الشُّمُولَ هَذَا التَّعرِيفُ مَنقُولٌ عَن أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ رَحِمَهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى فَالمَعرِفَةُ إِدْرَاتُ الجُزِيَّاتِ عَن دَلِيل فَخَرَجَ التَّهْلِيدُ وَقَولُهُ مَا لَهَا وَمَا عَلَيْهَا يُمكِنُ أَن يُرَادَ بِهِ مَا تَنتَفِعُ بِهِ النَّفْسُ وَمَا تَتَضَرَّرُ بِهِ فِي الآخِرَةِ كَمَا فِي قَوله تَعَالَى لَهَا مَا كَسَبَتْ وَعَلَيْهَا مَا اكْتَسبَت
Clarification: Fiqh is the soul's knowledge of what is for it and what is against it. And it is increased with 'action' to exclude theological beliefs and inner spiritual states, thus theology (kalam) and asceticism (tasawwuf) are excluded. Whoever did not add (this word) intended comprehensiveness. This definition is transmitted from Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. So 'knowledge' (ma'rifa) is perception of particulars from evidence, thus tawhid (theology) is excluded. His statement 'what is for it and what is against it' may mean what benefits the soul and what harms it in the Hereafter, as in His statement, exalted: 'For it is what it earned, and against it is what it acquired.'
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage provides the classic definition of fiqh transmitted from Imam Abu Hanifa. The definition has two parts: 'knowledge of the soul of what is for it and what is against it' (معرفة النفس ما لها وما عليها). The commentator explains that the word 'action' (عملا) is added to exclude theological beliefs (اعتقادیات) and inner spiritual states (وجدانیات), thus removing ilm al-kalam (theology) and tasawwuf (mysticism) from the scope of fiqh. Some definitions omit 'action' to include all rulings. 'Knowledge' (معرفة) is defined as perception of particulars (جزئیات) derived from evidence, which excludes general theological knowledge like tawhid. The phrase 'what is for it and what is against it' refers to actions beneficial or harmful in the afterlife, analogous to Quranic usage in Surah Al-Baqarah: 286. This definition establishes fiqh as the science of practical legal rulings (ahkam amaliyyah) deduced from detailed evidence.

Key Terms
الفقه (al-fiqh): Knowledge of the soul of its rights and duties derived from evidence.
معرفة (maʿrifa): Perception of particulars (جزئیات) from evidence.
ما لها وما عليها (mā lahā wa mā ʿalayhā): What benefits and harms the soul in the Hereafter (rights and duties).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To emphasize that fiqh includes all actions, even beliefs.
B) To exclude theological beliefs and inner spiritual states from the scope of fiqh.
C) To include supererogatory acts of worship.
D) To ensure that knowledge is accompanied by practice.

Key Takeaway
Fiqh in the Hanafi school is the knowledge of practical legal rulings derived from detailed evidence, distinct from theology and mysticism.

The Hanafi Definition of Fiqh and Classification of Actions
Defining fiqh and classifying actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to restate Imam Abu Hanifa's definition of fiqh, differentiate it from narrower definitions, and classify actions into the six legal categories with their corresponding rewards and punishments.

Core Idea
Fiqh is the soul's knowledge of its rights and duties; actions are six categories of reward or punishment.

This lesson unpacks the seminal Hanafi definition of fiqh attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa. You will see how this definition encompasses not only actions but also beliefs and inner states, and how it leads to a systematic classification of all human acts in terms of reward and punishment. The passage also explores multiple interpretations of the key phrase 'what is for it and against it,' showing the depth of Hanafi legal theory.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definition
Find the phrase 'وَالفِقهُ مَعرِفَةُ النَّفْسِ مَا لَهَا وَمَا عَلَيْهَا' in the Arabic and note it is transmitted from Abu Hanifa. This is the core definition.
Some later Hanafis add 'amalan' to exclude beliefs, but the original is comprehensive.
2
Analyse each term
Break down 'ma'rifa' (knowledge from evidence), 'nafs' (the soul), and 'ma laha wa ma alayha' (what is for it and against it). Understand that ma'rifa excludes conjecture (tahlid), and the pair indicates rights/duties or benefit/harm.
Hanafi usul distinguishes ma'rifa from 'ilm; here ma'rifa is practical knowledge.
3
Explore possible interpretations
The author considers three interpretations of 'ma laha wa ma alayha': reward/punishment, benefit/harm, permissibility/obligation. See how each interpretation shifts the classification of acts into the categories of reward and punishment.
The author prefers an interpretation with no intermediate between the two categories (i.e., everything is either rewarded or punished or neither).
4
Understand the six categories
The passage lists six types: wajib, mandub, mubah, makruh tanzihi, makruh tahrimi, haram. For each, consider both doing and leaving, giving twelve aspects. Know which actions bring reward, punishment, or neither.
The six categories are the basis of the five rulings (ahkam khamsa) in Hanafi terminology, but here the author explicitly names six including the two types of makruh.
5
Apply the scope
Realise that fiqh according to this definition includes beliefs (theology), inner ethics (tasawwuf), and practical actions (fiqh proper). This broad scope is distinctive of the Hanafi school.
The passage explicitly says fiqh covers i'tiqadiyyat, wijdaniyyat, and amaliyyat.

Clarification: And fiqh is the soul's knowledge of what is for it and what is against it, and one may add 'action' to exclude beliefs and inner states—thus excluding theology and self-discipline. Whoever did not add intended inclusiveness. This definition is transmitted from Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. So knowledge is the perception of particulars from evidence, thus excluding conjecture. And his statement 'what is for it and what is against it' can be taken to mean what the soul benefits from and what harms it in the afterlife, as in His statement: 'For it is what it earned, and against it is what it acquired.'
If by them are meant reward and punishment, then know that what the responsible person does is either obligatory, recommended, permissible, disliked with detestation, disliked with prohibition, or forbidden. These are six. Then for each there are two aspects: aspect of doing and aspect of leaving—i.e., not doing—so they become twelve. So performing the obligatory and recommended are things rewarded; performing the forbidden and prohibitively disliked and leaving the obligatory are things punished; the rest are neither rewarded nor punished, so they do not fall into either category. If by benefit is meant absence of punishment, and by harm is punishment, then performing the forbidden and prohibitively disliked and leaving the obligatory are from the second category—i.e., things punished—and the remaining six are from the first—i.e., things not punished. If by benefit is meant reward, and by harm is absence of reward, then performing the obligatory and recommended are things rewarded; the ten remaining are things not rewarded. And it is possible that by 'what is for it and what is against it' are meant what is permissible for it and what is obligatory upon it. Then doing what is other than the forbidden and prohibitively disliked, and leaving what is other than the obligatory, are things permissible for it; doing the obligatory, and leaving the forbidden and prohibitively disliked, are things obligatory upon it; and performing the forbidden and prohibitively disliked, and leaving the obligatory, remain outside both categories. And it is possible that by 'what is for it and what is against it' are meant what is permissible for it and what is forbidden for it; then they encompass all types. When you know this, then interpretation in a way that has no intermediate between the two categories is preferable. Then, 'what is for it and what is against it' includes beliefs like the obligation of faith and the like, inner states—i.e., inner morals and psychological traits—and actions like prayer, fasting, sale, and the like. So knowledge of what is for it and what is against it from beliefs is the science of theology, and knowledge of what is for it and what is against it from inner states is the science of ethics and self-discipline like asceticism, patience, contentment, and presence of heart in prayer, etc. And knowledge of what is for it
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage clarifies the famous definition of fiqh from Imam Abu Hanifa: 'knowledge of the soul of what is for it and against it.' The author explains that 'knowledge' means perception of particulars through evidence, excluding conjecture. The phrase 'what is for it and against it' can be interpreted in multiple ways: reward/punishment, benefit/harm, permissibility/obligation, etc. The author then classifies actions into six categories (wajib, mandub, mubah, makruh tanzihan, makruh tahriman, haram) and shows how they relate to reward and punishment. It also notes that fiqh covers beliefs (theology), inner states (ethics), and actions (practical rulings).

Key Terms
الفقه (al-fiqh): Knowledge of the soul of what is for it and against it, derived from evidence.
المعرفة (al-ma'rifa): Perception of particulars from evidence (idrāk al-juz'iyyāt 'an dalīl).
واجب (wājib): An action whose performance is rewarded and omission is punished.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Imam Abu Hanifa's Definition of Fiqh: Between Comprehensiveness and Technical Specialization
Definition and analysis of fiqh according to Imam Abu Hanifa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam Abu Hanifa's comprehensive definition of fiqh, explain the meaning of 'ma'rifah', and distinguish it from the later technical definition restricted to actions.

Core Idea
Fiqh according to Abu Hanifa includes beliefs, inner states, and actions; later restrictors limited it to practical rulings.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi definition of fiqh, which is foundational for understanding usul al-fiqh. You will see how Imam Abu Hanifa's term 'al-fiqh al-akbar' reveals the broad scope of the discipline, and how later scholars narrowed it for specialization. We will examine the key terms 'ma'rifah' and 'ma laha wa ma 'alayha' as they appear in the source text.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definition in the text
Find the sentence: 'Fiqh is the recognition of the self's ma laha wa ma 'alayha'. This is the core definition attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa.
The definition appears in both Arabic and Urdu parts of the passage.
2
Interpret 'ma'rifah'
The text explains 'ma'rifah' as 'idrak al-juz'iyyat 'an dalil'—perception of particulars by a proof. This excludes taqlid (blind imitation). Understand why proof-based knowledge is essential.
Ma'rifah is synonymous with 'ilm in this context.
3
Analyze 'ma laha wa ma 'alayha'
The phrase has multiple interpretations: benefit/harm, reward/punishment, permissible/obligatory, etc. Explore how the passage divides rulings into twelve types based on these interpretations.
The text suggests that the best interpretation is one that includes all rulings without intermediary.
4
Distinguish comprehensive vs technical fiqh
Imam Abu Hanifa did not add 'amalan (practical) because he intended a comprehensive definition including beliefs (i'tiqadiyat), spiritual states (wijdaniyat), and actions (amaliyat). Later scholars added 'amalan to restrict fiqh to actions only.
The source emphasizes that Abu Hanifa's definition is more general.
5
Appreciate the madhhab dispute
Why did Abu Hanifa call theology 'al-fiqh al-akbar'? What is the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of the two definitions? The passage shows that the broader definition includes theology and tasawwuf as part of fiqh.
The author of the passage seems to favor the comprehensive definition for foundational teaching.

الاعتِقَادِيَّات أو الوجدَانِيَّاتِ أَو العَمَلِيَّاتِ وَمِنْ ثَمَّ سَمَّى الكَلامَ فِقها أَكبَرَ ترجمہ:۔ اور فقہ پہچاننا ہے نفس کا مالبا اور ماعلیہا کو اور زیادہ کی جاتی ہے عمل کی قید تا کہ نکال دے ( یہ قید ) اعتقاد یات اور وجدانیات کو پس نکل جائے گا علم کلام اور تصوف ۔ اور جس نے نہیں زیادہ کیا اس نے ارادہ کیا ہے عموم کا ۔ یہ تعریف منقول ہے امام ابو حنیفہ ہے۔ پس معرفت " جزئیات کو جانا ہے دلیل ہے۔ پس نکل جائیگی تقلید ۔ اور اس کے قول مالھا و ما علیھا میں ممکن ہے کہ مراد لیا جائے ان چیزوں کو جن سے نفع حاصل کرتا ہے نفس اور ان چیزوں کو جن سے نفس کو آخرت میں ضرر لاحق ہوگا، جس طرح کہ اللہ تعالیٰ کے قول لها ما كسبت و عليها ما اكستبت میں (لام نفع کیلئے ہے اور علیٰ ضرر کیلئے ہے ) پس اگر ابزادہ کیا جائے ان سے ثواب اور عقاب کا پس جان تو کہ تحقیق جو کچھ مکلف بجالاتا ہے یا تو واجب ہوگا یا مستحب یا مباح یا مکروہ ہو گا کراہت تنزیہ کے ساتھ یا مکروہ ہو گا کراہت تحریمی کے ساتھ یا حرام ہوگا پس یہ چھ قسمیں ہیں ، پھر ہر ایک کیلئے دوطرفیں ہیں جانب فعل اور جانب ترک یعنی فعل کو نہ کرنا ، پس ہو گئیں بارہ قسمیں ۔ پس فعل اجب اور فعل مندوب ان اشیاء میں سے ہیں جن پر ثواب دیا جائے گا اور فعل حرام اور مکروہ تحریمی اور ترک واجب ان چیزوں میں سے ہیں جن پر عقاب ہوگا اور باقی پر نہ تو اب ہوگا اور نہ عقاب ہوتا ہے۔ پس نہیں داخل ہوں گی ۔ دونوں قسموں میں سے کسی میں ۔ اور اگر ارادہ کیا جائے نفع سے عدم عقاب کا اور ضرر سے عقاب کا پس فعل حرام اور مکروہ تحریمی اور ترک واجب قسم ثانی سے ہوں گے یعنی جن پر سزادی جائیگی اور باقی نو پہلی قسم سے ہو گی یعنی جن پر سزا نہیں دی جائیگی ۔ اور اگر ارادہ کیا جائے نفع سے ثواب کا اور ضرر سے عدم ثواب کا پس فعل واجب اور مندوب ان چیزوں سے ہوں گے جن پر ثواب دیا جائیگا، پھر باقی دس قسمیں ماسوائے 

التَّرُويْحُ لِحَلَّ التَّوْضِيحِ وَالتَّلُويْحِ 208 وَاجِب کے ترک کے اس کیلئے جائز ہوگا اور فعل واجب ، ترک حرام اور ترک مکروہ تحریمی ان میں سے ہوں گے جو اس (نفس پر واجب ہیں ، پس باقی رہیں گے فعل حرام اور فعل مکروہ تحریمی اور ترک واجب اس حال میں کہ خارج ہوں گے دونوں قسموں سے اور ممکن ہے کہ مراد لیا جائے مالھا و ما علیھا سے جو اس کیلئے جائز ہیں اور جو اس پر حرام ہیں پس یہ دونوں قسمیں تمام احکام کو شامل ہو جائینگی۔ جب تو نے یہ بات پہچان لی پس محمول کرنا ( مالہا وہ علیھا ) کو ایسے احتمال پر کہ جس میں نہ ہو دونوں قسموں کے درمیان کوئی واسطہ بہتر ہے۔ پھر مالھا و ماعلیہا شامل ہیں اعتقادیات کو جیسے ایمان کا واجب ہونا اور اسکی مثل اور وجدانیات کو یعنی اخلاق باطنہ کو اور ملکات نفسانیہ کو اور عبادات کو جیسے نماز ، روزہ اور اسکی مثل ۔ پس مالھاو ماعلیہا کو اعتقادیا ت سے جانا علم کلام ہے، اور بالھا و ما علیھا کو وجدانیات سے جاننا علم اخلاق اور تصوف ہے جیسے زہد ، صبر، رضا اور نماز میں حضور قلب اور اس کی مثل اور مالھا و ما علیھا کو عملیات سے جاننا فقہ اصطلاحی ہے ، پس اگر تو ارادہ کرے فقہ سے اس اصطلاحی فقہ کا تو زیادہ کرے گا عملاً ( کی قید ) اس کے قول الھا و ما علیھا پر اور اگر تو ارادہ کرے اس کا جو شامل ہو تینوں قسموں کو تو اضافہ نہیں کرے گا اور امام ابو حنیفہ نے بہر حال اضافہ نہیں کیا اس عملاً کی قید کا اس لئے کہ انہوں نے شمول کا ارادہ کیا ہے یعنی انہوں نے فقہ کا اطلاق ما لھا و ماعلیہا کے علم پر کیا ہے عام ہے کہ اعتقادیات سے ہوں یا وجدانیات سے ہوں یا عملیات سے ، اسی وجہ سے انہوں علم کلام کا نام فقہ اکبر رکھا ہے۔

تشریح:۔ اصول فقہ کی تعریف اضافی ہو رہی تھی ۔ مضاف (اصول ) کی تعریف گزرچکی ہے اب مضاف الیہ (فقہ) کی تعریف ہو رہی ہے۔
امام ابو حنیفہ رحمہ اللہ تعالیٰ سے منقول فقہ کی تعریف
تعریف:۔ فقہ نام ہے نفس کے مالھاو ا علیھا کے پہچانے کا یہ تعریف امام صاحب کے نزدیک ہے۔ بعض حضرات نے اس تعریف میں عملا کی قید بھی لگائی گئی ہے اور وہ اس لئے کہ تا کہ فقہ کی تعریف سے اعتقادیات اور وجدانیات کا علم یعنی علم کلام اور علم تصوف خارج ہو جائیں۔ لیکن امام صاحب نے ان کو خارج نہیں کیا۔ بہر حال امام صاحب کی تعریف میں دو چیزیں قابل وضاحت ہیں۔ (۱) معنی معرفت (۲) معانی "مالها وما عليها "
فالمعرفتہ ادراک الجزئيات عن دلیل ۔ . یہاں سے پہلی چیز کی وضاحت ہے کہ معرفت نام ہے ۔
And what is upon it from the practical actions is the technical fiqh. For if you intend by fiqh this technical term, you add 'amalan to his saying 'ma laha wa ma 'alayha'. And if you intend what includes the three categories, you do not add. And Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, did not add 'amalan because he intended comprehensiveness, i.e., he applied fiqh to the knowledge of what is for it and against it, whether it is from beliefs or spiritual states or actions. Hence he called theology 'al-fiqh al-akbar'. Translation: And fiqh is recognizing the self's 'ma laha' and 'ma 'alayha'. And the restriction of 'amalan is added so that beliefs and spiritual states are excluded, so theology and tasawwuf are excluded. And whoever did not add intended generality. This definition is transmitted from Imam Abu Hanifa. So ma'rifah is knowledge of particulars from a proof, so taqlid is excluded. And in his statement 'ma laha wa ma 'alayha', it is possible that what is intended is those things by which the self benefits and those things by which the self will suffer harm in the afterlife, like Allah's statement 'Laha ma kasabat wa 'alayha ma iktasabat' (the lam is for benefit and 'ala for harm). Then if reward and punishment are intended, then what the mukallaf performs is either obligatory, recommended, permissible, disliked with tanzih, disliked with tahrim, or forbidden. These are six types, then for each there are two aspects: doing and leaving, so there are twelve types. Obligatory and recommended acts are among those that will be rewarded; forbidden, disliked with tahrim, and leaving obligatory are among those that will be punished; the rest have neither reward nor punishment. So they are not included in either type. And if benefit is intended as non-punishment and harm as punishment, then forbidden, disliked with tahrim, and leaving obligatory are from the second type (i.e., those punished), and the remaining nine are from the first type (i.e., those not punished). And if benefit is intended as reward and harm as non-reward, then obligatory and recommended are from those that will be rewarded, and the remaining ten will not be rewarded. And it is possible that 'ma laha wa ma 'alayha' means what is permissible for the self and what is obligatory upon it, so other than forbidden and disliked with tahrim are for it, and other than obligatory are upon it. . . And leaving obligatory becomes permissible for it, and doing obligatory, leaving forbidden, and leaving disliked with tahrim are among those obligatory upon it. So remaining are doing forbidden, doing disliked with tahrim, and leaving obligatory, which are excluded from both categories. And it is possible that 'ma laha wa ma 'alayha' means what is permissible for it and what is forbidden upon it, so these two categories include all rulings. When you have recognized this, then to carry 'ma laha wa ma 'alayha' onto a probability where there is no intermediary between the two categories is better. Then 'ma laha wa ma 'alayha' includes beliefs, like the obligation of faith and the like, and spiritual states, i.e., inner ethics and soul qualities, and acts of worship like prayer, fasting and the like. So knowing 'ma laha wa ma 'alayha' regarding beliefs is theology, knowing them regarding spiritual states is ethics and tasawwuf, like zuhd, patience, contentment, presence of heart in prayer and the like, and knowing them regarding actions is technical fiqh. So if you intend by fiqh this technical fiqh, you add the restriction of 'amalan to his statement 'ma laha wa ma 'alayha', and if you intend what includes all three categories, you do not add. And Imam Abu Hanifa did not add the restriction of 'amalan, because he intended comprehensiveness, i.e., he applied fiqh to the knowledge of 'ma laha wa ma 'alayha' generally, whether from beliefs or spiritual states or actions. That is why he called theology 'al-fiqh al-akbar'. Tashrih: The definition of usul al-fiqh was compound. The definition of the mudaf (usul) has passed. Now the definition of the mudaf ilayh (fiqh) is given. Definition of fiqh transmitted from Imam Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him: Definition: Fiqh is the name for the recognition of the self's 'ma laha wa ma 'alayha'. This is the definition according to Imam Sahib. Some scholars have added the restriction of 'amalan in this definition so that knowledge of beliefs and spiritual states, i.e., theology and tasawwuf, are excluded from the definition of fiqh. But Imam Sahib did not exclude them. In any case, in Imam Sahib's definition, two things need explanation: (1) the meaning of ma'rifah, (2) the meanings of 'ma laha wa ma 'alayha'. Fa al-ma'rifatu idrak al-juz'iyyat 'an dalil. Here from here the first thing is explained, that ma'rifah is the name for...
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is a definition and analysis of the term 'fiqh' as understood by Imam Abu Hanifa, within the context of defining usul al-fiqh. It begins by explaining that if one intends the technical fiqh (dealing only with actions), one restricts the definition by adding 'amalan (practical) to the phrase 'ma laha wa ma 'alayha' (what is for it and against it). But Imam Abu Hanifa did not add this restriction because his definition was comprehensive, including beliefs (i'tiqadiyat), spiritual states (wijdaniyat), and actions (amaliyat). Therefore, he called theology 'al-fiqh al-akbar' (the greater fiqh). The passage then presents an Urdu translation and commentary which elaborates on various possible interpretations of 'ma laha wa ma 'alayha', relating them to benefit and harm, reward and punishment, obligation and permission. It explores how the twelve divisions of legal rulings (six types each with doing and leaving) fit under different interpretations of benefit and harm. It concludes that the best interpretation is one that includes all rulings without intermediary. Later, it clarifies that 'ma laha wa ma 'alayha' includes three categories: beliefs (theology), spiritual states (ethics/tasawwuf), and actions (technical fiqh). The passage ends with a tashrih (clarification) that the definition of fiqh is now being given as the second part of the definition of usul al-fiqh. The definition from Imam Abu Hanifa is: 'Fiqh is the recognition of the self's ma laha wa ma 'alayha.' Some later scholars added 'amalan to exclude beliefs and spiritual states, but Abu Hanifa did not. Then it begins to explain the two key components: the meaning of ma'rifah (knowledge) and the meaning of 'ma laha wa ma 'alayha'.

Key Terms
الفقه (al-fiqh): According to Imam Abu Hanifa, knowledge of what is for the self and against it, including beliefs, spiritual states, and actions. Some later scholars restrict it to the knowledge of practical actions.
معرفة (ma'rifah): Here it means the perception (idrak) of particulars (juz'iyyat) by means of a proof (dalil). It excludes taqlid (blind following) because that is not based on proof.
مالها وما عليها (ma laha wa ma 'alayha): Literally 'what is for it and what is against it'. For the self (nafs), it refers to beneficial and harmful things, or reward and punishment, or permissible and obligatory, etc. The passage explores multiple interpretations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, which of the following is included in the definition of fiqh?
A) Only practical actions (amaliyat)
B) Only beliefs (i'tiqadiyat)
C) Beliefs, spiritual states, and actions
D) Only spiritual states (wijdaniyat)

Key Takeaway
Imam Abu Hanifa defined fiqh as knowledge of what is for and against the self, covering beliefs, inner states, and actions, later narrowed to only actions.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
15 min
Imam Abu Hanifa's Definition of Fiqh: Scope and Interpretations
Expanding on the definition of fiqh and the meanings of 'ma laha wa ma alayha'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Imam Abu Hanifa's definition of fiqh, distinguish its three components (beliefs, inner states, actions), and analyze the three interpretations of 'ma laha wa ma alayha' using the twelve categories of acts.

Core Idea
Fiqh is knowledge of what benefits and harms the self, covering beliefs, inner states, and actions.

Imam Abu Hanifa's definition of fiqh is remarkably broad, encompassing not only practical legal rulings but also theology (kalam) and spirituality (tasawwuf). This passage unpacks that definition, showing how the phrase 'ma laha wa ma alayha' (what belongs to the self and what is upon it) can be interpreted in multiple ways, each affecting which acts are included. By working through this expansion, you will grasp the foundational Hanafi understanding of the scope of sacred knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition's components
The definition is 'ma'rifat al-nafs ma laha wa ma alayha' (knowing what belongs to the self and what is upon it). Break down 'ma'rifa' (cognition with proof) and 'ma laha wa ma alayha' (what benefits/harms).
Ma'rifa excludes taqlid because it requires dalil.
2
Understand the three included domains
Imam Abu Hanifa includes i'tiqadiyat (beliefs), wijdaniyat (inner states/ethics), and amaliyat (practical actions). Note that later scholars added 'amalan' to restrict fiqh to actions only.
3
Master the twelve categories of acts
From six hukm types (wajib, mandub, mubah, makruh tanzihi, makruh tahrimi, haram) each with act (fi'l) and omission (tark), derive 12 categories. This is the analytical framework used in the interpretations.
Memorize the six rulings and their act/omission pairs.
4
Apply the three interpretations
Each interpretation of 'ma laha wa ma alayha' (reward/punishment, absence of punishment/punishment, reward/absence of reward) includes a different set of the 12 categories. Work through each to see which categories are in 'ma laha' and which in 'ma alayha'.
This shows how definitional choices affect scope.

الترويج لحل التوضيح والتلويج
جزئیات کو دلیل کے ساتھ پہچانے کا دلیل کی قید لگا کر ماتن نے تقلید کو خارج کر دیا کیونکہ تقلید میں اگر چہ جزئیات کا ادراک ہوتا ہے لیکن دلیل کے ساتھ نہیں ہوتا بلکہ مجتہد کے اقوال کے ساتھ ہوتا ہے، لہذا تقلید پر معرفت کا اطلاق نہیں ہوسکتا۔ اسی لیے اس کو تعریف سے خارج کرنے کیلئے مائن نے ”دلیل“ کی قید لگائی ہے۔
الھا و ما علیھا“ کے معانی کا بیان
مالھا و ما علیھا ۔۔۔۔۔۔۔۔ یہاں سے ماتن نے دوسری چیز کی وضاحت کی ہے یعنی مالھاو ما علیھا“ کے معانی کی تفصیل۔ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ الھا و ما علیھا“ کے تین معانی ہیں۔
(1) نفع کیلئے ہو اور علی ضرر کیلئے ہو ۔ یعنی ماتھا" سے مراد اینتفع بھا النفس اور با علیھا سے مراد محضر رکھا النفس ہو۔ اس معنی میں پھر تین احتمال ہیں جن کو سمجھنے سے پہلے بطور تمہید ایک مقدمہ کا سمجھنا ضروری ہے۔
مقدمہ:۔ دنیا میں انسان جو بھی عمل کرتا ہے اس کی اولا چھ قسمیں ہیں ۔ (۱) واجب (۲) مندوب (۳) مباح (۴) مکروہ تحریمی (۵) مکروہ تنزیہی (۶) حرام ۔ پھر ان میں سے ہر ایک میں دو دو احتمال ہیں۔ (۱) فعل (۲) عدم فعل یعنی ترک ۔ توکل بارہ اقسام ہو گئیں ۔ (۱) فعل واجب (۲) ترک واجب (۳) فعل مندوب (۴) ترک مندوب (۵) فعل مباح (۶) ترک مباح (۷) فعل مکروہ تنزیہی (۸) ترک مکروہ تنزیہی (۹) فعل مکروہ تحریمی (۱۰) ترک مکروہ تحریمی (۱۱) فعل حرام (۱۲) ترک حرام ۔ اب مالہا اور علیھا سے مراد اگر نفع اور ضرر ہو تو اس میں مزید تین احتمال ہیں ۔ (۱) نفع " سے مراد ثواب اور ضرر سے مراد عقاب ہو ۔ اس صورت میں فقہ کی تعریف مذکورہ بالا اقسام میں سے صرف پانچ قسموں کو شامل ہوگی ۔ اور وہ اس طرح کہ " مالھا میں دو قسمیں یعنی فعل واجب اور فعل مندوب شامل ہوں گے کیونکہ ان دونوں میں ثواب ہوتا ہے اور ما علیھا یعنی عقاب میں تین چیز میں یعنی ترک واجب فعل حرام اور فعل مکروہ تحریمی شامل ہوں گے۔ اور باقی سات اقسام فقہ کی تعریف سے خارج ہو جائیں گی۔ کیونکہ یہ اقسام نہ تو ثواب میں داخل ہیں نہ عقاب میں ۔ (۲) نفع سے مراد عدم عقاب اور ضرر سے مراد عقاب ہو ۔ اس صورت میں ساری اقسام فقہ کی تعریف میں شامل ہو جائیں گی۔ وہ اس طرح کہ تین قسمیں یعنی فعل حرام، فعل مکروہ تحریمی اور ترک واجب ما علیھا میں داخل ہو جائیں گی کہ ان پر عقاب ہو گا اور باقی دس اقسام مالھا میں داخل ہو جائیں گی کہ ان پر عقاب نہیں ہو گا آگے عام ہے کہ ان پر ثواب ہو یا نہ ہو۔ (۳) نفع سے مراد ثواب اور ضرر سے مراد عدم ثواب ہو۔ اس صورت میں بھی ساری اقسام تعریف میں داخل ہو جائیں گی۔ کہ دو قسمیں یعنی فعل واجب اور فعل مندوب
At-tarwih li hall at-tawdih wa at-talwih. 208. Its leaving the wajib will be permissible for him, and the act of wajib, leaving of haram, and leaving of makruh tahrimi are from among those that are obligatory upon the self. So remaining will be the act of haram and the act of makruh tahrimi and leaving of wajib, in such a state that they will be excluded from both categories. And it is possible that by 'ma laha wa ma alayha' is intended what is permissible for it and what is forbidden upon it. So these two categories will include all rulings. When you have recognized this, then to carry 'ma laha wa ma alayha' upon a probability in which there is no intermediary between the two categories is better. Then 'ma laha wa ma alayha' includes beliefs (i'tiqadiyat) like the obligation of faith and the like, and existential matters (wijdaniyat) i.e., inner ethics and psychological dispositions, and acts of worship like prayer, fasting and the like. So knowing 'ma laha wa ma alayha' from beliefs is the science of kalam; knowing 'ma laha wa ma alayha' from existential matters is the science of ethics and tasawwuf like asceticism, patience, contentment, presence of heart in prayer and the like; and knowing 'ma laha wa ma alayha' from practical matters is fiqh in the technical sense. So if you intend by fiqh this technical fiqh, you will add the restriction of 'amalan' to his statement 'ma laha wa ma alayha'; and if you intend what includes all three categories, you will not add. And Imam Abu Hanifa, in any case, did not add the restriction of 'amalan', because he intended inclusiveness, meaning he applied the term fiqh to the knowledge of 'ma laha wa ma alayha' universally, whether from beliefs, existential matters, or practical matters. For this reason, he named the science of kalam 'al-fiqh al-akbar'. Commentary: The definition of usul al-fiqh was being added. The definition of the addendum (usul) has passed; now the definition of the addendum-to (fiqh) is given. Definition of fiqh transmitted from Imam Abu Hanifa: Definition: Fiqh is the name for knowing what belongs to the self and what is upon it. This is the definition according to Imam Sahib. Some individuals added the restriction of 'amalan' (practical) to this definition, so that knowledge of beliefs and existential matters, i.e., kalam and tasawwuf, would be excluded from the definition of fiqh. But Imam Sahib did not exclude them. In any case, in Imam Sahib's definition, two things are worthy of clarification: (1) the meaning of ma'rifa (recognition), and (2) the meanings of 'ma laha wa ma alayha'. So al-ma'rifatu idrak al-juz'iyyat 'an dalil. From here, the first thing is clarified: that ma'rifa is the name for recognizing particular matters with a proof. By adding the restriction of 'dalil', the author excludes taqlid, because in taqlid, although there is perception of particular matters, it is not with a proof, but rather with the statements of a mujtahid. Therefore, the term ma'rifa cannot be applied to taqlid. For this reason, the author added the restriction of 'dalil' to exclude it. Statement of the meanings of 'ma laha wa ma alayha': 'Ma laha wa ma alayha'... From here, the author clarifies the second thing, i.e., the details of the meanings of 'ma laha wa ma alayha'. The summary is that 'ma laha wa ma alayha' has three meanings: (1) 'ma laha' is for benefit and 'ma alayha' is for harm, i.e., by 'ma laha' is meant what benefits the self and by 'ma alayha' is meant what harms the self. In this meaning, there are three probabilities, to understand which it is necessary first to understand a premise as an introduction. Premise: Whatever action a human performs in the world, its types are initially six: (1) wajib, (2) mandub, (3) mubah, (4) makruh tahrimi, (5) makruh tanzihi, (6) haram. Then for each of these, there are two probabilities: (1) the act (fi'l), (2) non-act, i.e., leaving (tark). So total twelve types: (1) act of wajib, (2) leaving of wajib, (3) act of mandub, (4) leaving of mandub, (5) act of mubah, (6) leaving of mubah, (7) act of makruh tanzihi, (8) leaving of makruh tanzihi, (9) act of makruh tahrimi, (10) leaving of makruh tahrimi, (11) act of haram, (12) leaving of haram. Now if by 'ma laha' and 'ma alayha' is meant benefit and harm, then there are three further probabilities: (1) By 'benefit' is meant reward (thawab) and by 'harm' is meant punishment (iqab). In this case, the definition of fiqh includes only five of the above types, and that is: in 'ma laha' two types are included, i.e., act of wajib and act of mandub, because in these two there is reward; and in 'ma alayha' i.e., punishment, three things are included: leaving of wajib, act of haram, and act of makruh tahrimi. And the remaining seven types are excluded from the definition of fiqh, because these types are neither included in reward nor in punishment. (2) By 'benefit' is meant absence of punishment and by 'harm' is meant punishment. In this case, all types are included in the definition of fiqh, such that three types (act of haram, act of makruh tahrimi, and leaving of wajib) enter into 'ma alayha' because there is punishment on them, and the remaining ten types enter into 'ma laha' because there is no punishment on them, regardless of whether there is reward or not. (3) By 'benefit' is meant reward and by 'harm' is meant absence of reward. In this case also, all types are included in the definition, because two types (act of wajib and act of mandub) have reward, and the remaining ten types have no reward.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
The passage is a detailed commentary on the definition of fiqh attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa. It begins by differentiating between various types of actions (wajib, haram, etc.) and then clarifies that the phrase 'ma laha wa ma alayha' (what belongs to it and what is upon it) can be interpreted in multiple ways. The commentator explains that Imam Abu Hanifa's definition of fiqh is comprehensive: it is knowledge of what benefits and harms the self, covering beliefs (i'tiqadiyat), inner states (wijdaniyat), and practical actions (amaliyat). Some later scholars added the restriction 'amalan' (practical) to exclude kalam and tasawwuf, but Imam Abu Hanifa did not, as he considered all three to be included under fiqh. The passage then delves into the term 'ma'rifa', noting that it means cognition of particulars with a proof (dalil), thereby excluding taqlid. Finally, it presents three possible interpretations of 'ma laha wa ma alayha' based on whether benefit and harm are understood as reward/punishment, absence of punishment/punishment, or reward/absence of reward. Each interpretation affects which of the twelve categories of acts (derived from six rulings each with act and omission) are included in the definition of fiqh. This analysis demonstrates the depth of Hanafi usul in defining fundamental terms.

Key Terms
الفقه (al-fiqh): Knowledge of what belongs to the self (ma laha) and what is upon it (ma alayha), including beliefs, inner states, and practical actions.
ما لها وما عليها (ma laha wa ma alayha): What benefits or harms the self; can be interpreted as reward/punishment, absence of punishment/punishment, or reward/absence of reward.
المعرفة (al-ma'rifa): Cognition of particulars with a proof (dalil), excluding taqlid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a possible interpretation of 'ma laha wa ma alayha'?
A) Benefit = reward, harm = punishment
B) Benefit = absence of punishment, harm = punishment
C) Benefit = reward, harm = absence of reward
D) Benefit = absence of reward, harm = punishment

Key Takeaway
Imam Abu Hanifa defined fiqh broadly as knowledge of what benefits and harms the self, covering beliefs, inner states, and actions, and this definition's inclusiveness varies with the interpretation of 'benefit' and 'harm'.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
Meanings of 'ma laha wa ma alayha' in the Definition of Fiqh
Explaining the possible meanings of 'ma laha wa ma alayha' in the definition of fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the multiple possible interpretations of the phrase 'ma laha wa ma alayha' and identify which interpretations include all twelve categories of actions in the Hanafi definition of fiqh.

Core Idea
The phrase 'ma laha wa ma alayha' has five interpretations; only three encompass all twelve action types.

This passage explores the critical phrase 'ma laha wa ma alayha' that appears in the classical Hanafi definition of fiqh. The commentator systematically unpacks its possible meanings, showing that it can refer to benefit/harm, reward/punishment, or permissibility/obligation. Understanding these nuances is essential to grasping the full scope of what fiqh covers according to Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the phrase in context
Note that 'ma laha wa ma alayha' is part of the definition of fiqh, and the author previously excluded taqlid by requiring proof.
2
Understand the premise of twelve action categories
Each of the six hukm types (wajib, mandub, mubah, etc.) has both a doing and a leaving, giving twelve scenarios.
3
Analyze the first major meaning (benefit/harm) and its three sub-probabilities
For each sub-meaning (reward/punishment, absence of punishment/punishment, reward/absence of reward), determine which actions are included and excluded.
4
Analyze the second meaning (permissible/obligatory)
Identify which actions are included in 'ma laha' (permissible) and which in 'ma alayha' (obligatory).
5
Analyze the third meaning (permissible/forbidden)
Identify which actions are included in 'ma laha' (permissible) and which in 'ma alayha' (forbidden).
6
Summarize the five probabilities and identify the preferred ones
List all five interpretations and note that three of them (absence of punishment/punishment, reward/absence of reward, permissible/forbidden) include all twelve actions.

جزئیات کو دلیل کے ساتھ پہچانے کا دلیل کی قید لگا کر ماتن نے تقلید کو خارج کر دیا کیونکہ تقلید میں اگر چہ جزئیات کا ادراک ہوتا ہے لیکن دلیل کے ساتھ نہیں ہوتا بلکہ مجتہد کے اقوال کے ساتھ ہوتا ہے، لہذا تقلید پر معرفت کا اطلاق نہیں ہوسکتا۔ اسی لیے اس کو تعریف سے خارج کرنے کیلئے مائن نے ”دلیل“ کی قید لگائی ہے۔

معنی ثانی کا بیان
و یمکن ان مراد بما لها وماعليها ما یجوز لها و ایجب علیھا:۔ یہاں سے مات مالھا اور اعلیھا کے دوسرے معنی کو بیان فرما رہے ہیں کہ دل جواز کے لئے اور علی وجوب کے لئے ہو۔ تو مالھا" سے مراد ما یجوز لھا یعنی جائز چیز اور " سے مراد ما یجب علیھا ، یعنی واجب چیزیں ہیں۔ اس صورت میں تین قسمیں یعنی فعل واجب ، ترک حرام اور ترک مکروہ تحریمی ما علیھا میں داخل ہو جائیں گی کیونکہ یہ تینوں واجب ہیں۔ اور فعل ماسوی الحرام اور فعل مکروہ تحریمی اور ترک ما سوى الواجب "الھا میں داخل ہو جائیں گے کیونکہ یہ جائز ہیں تو اب تین قسمیں یعنی فعل حرام فعل مکروہ تحریمی اور ترک واجب فقہ کی تعریف سے خارج ہو جائیں گی کیونکہ یہ سب نہ تو جائز ہیں نہ واجب۔
معنی ثالث کا بیان
(۳) و یمکن ان مراد بما لها وما عليها مايجوز لها ما تكرم عليها:۔ یہاں سے مصنف الہا اور علیھا کے تیسرے معنی کو بیان فرما رہے ہیں کہ مالہا سے مراد جائز چیزیں ہیں اور ما علیھا سے مراد حرام چیزیں ہیں ۔ اس صورت میں بھی ساری اقسام فقہ کی تعریف میں داخل ہو جائیں گی تو فعل حرام فعل مکروہ تحریمی ، ترک واجب یہ تین صورتیں ماعلیہا میں داخل ہونگی کیو نکہ یہ حرام ہیں اور باقی نو اقسام مالھا میں داخل ہو جائیں گی کیونکہ وہ سب جائز ہیں آگے عام ہے کہ واجب ہوں یا نہ ہوں ۔ خلاصہ یہ نکلا کہ مالھا اور اعلیھا" کی مراد میں کل پانچ احتمال ہیں (1) اس سے مراد ثواب اور عقاب ہے ۔ (2) اس سے مراد عقاب اور عدم عقاب ہے۔ (3) اس سے مراد ثواب اور عدم ثواب ہے ۔ (4) اس سے مراد جواز اور وجوب ہے۔ (5) اس سے مراد جواز اور حرمت ہے۔
فائل علی وجہ :۔ سے مصنف نے رائج احتمال کی طرف اشارہ فرمایا ہے کہ وہ احتمال جس میں بارہ کی بارہ اقسام فقہ کی تعریف میں داخل ہو جاتی ہیں۔ وہ احتمال راجح ہے اور ایسے تین احتمال ہیں یعنی دوسرا تیسرا اور پانچواں۔
تعریف فقہ اصطلاحی، علم کلام، علم تصوف کو شامل ہے
ثم مالها وماعلیہا میتاول:۔ یہاں سے مصنف یہ بیان فرمارہے ہیں کہ امام صاحب نے جو فقہ کی تعریف کی ہے اس میں
He said: By specifying 'with its proof' (dalil) for recognizing particulars, the author excludes taqlid, because in taqlid, even though particular rulings are perceived, they are not perceived with proof but with the statements of a mujtahid. Therefore, knowledge (ma'rifa) cannot be applied to taqlid. So to exclude it from the definition, the author put the condition of 'proof' (dalil).

Explanation of the meanings of 'ma laha wa ma alayha'
From here, the author explains the second thing, i.e., the detail of the meanings of 'ma laha wa ma alayha'. The upshot is that 'ma laha wa ma alayha' has three meanings:
(1) That 'ma laha' is for benefit and 'ma alayha' is for harm. That is, by 'ma laha' is meant that by which the soul benefits, and by 'ma alayha' is meant that which harms the soul. In this meaning, there are three probabilities. Before understanding them, it is necessary to understand a preliminary premise.
Premise: Whatever action a person does in the world, first there are six types: (1) obligatory (wajib), (2) recommended (mandub), (3) permissible (mubah), (4) prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi), (5) discretely disliked (makruh tanzihi), (6) forbidden (haram). Then in each of these, there are two probabilities: (1) doing (fi'l), (2) not doing (tark). Thus there become twelve types: (1) doing obligatory, (2) leaving obligatory, (3) doing recommended, (4) leaving recommended, (5) doing permissible, (6) leaving permissible, (7) doing discretely disliked, (8) leaving discretely disliked, (9) doing prohibitively disliked, (10) leaving prohibitively disliked, (11) doing forbidden, (12) leaving forbidden. Now if by 'ma laha' and 'ma alayha' are meant benefit and harm, then there are three further probabilities:
(a) By benefit is meant reward (thawab) and by harm is meant punishment (iqab). In this case, the definition of fiqh will include only five of the above types: in 'ma laha' will include two types: doing obligatory and doing recommended, because both have reward; and in 'ma alayha' (i.e., punishment) will include three: leaving obligatory, doing forbidden, and doing prohibitively disliked. The remaining seven types will be excluded from the definition of fiqh, because they are neither included in reward nor in punishment.
(b) By benefit is meant absence of punishment, and by harm is meant punishment. In this case, all twelve types will be included in the definition of fiqh: three types (doing forbidden, doing prohibitively disliked, leaving obligatory) will be included in 'ma alayha' because they have punishment; the remaining nine types will be included in 'ma laha' because they have no punishment; regardless of whether they have reward or not.
(c) By benefit is meant reward, and by harm is meant absence of reward. In this case also, all types are included: two types (doing obligatory and doing recommended) are in 'ma laha' because they have reward; the remaining ten types are in 'ma alayha' because they have no reward; regardless of whether they have punishment or not.

Explanation of the second meaning
'And it is possible that by 'ma laha wa ma alayha' is meant what is permissible for it and what is obligatory upon it': From here, the author explains the second meaning that 'lam' is for permissibility (jawaz) and 'ala' is for obligation (wujub). So by 'ma laha' is meant 'ma yajuzu laha' i.e., permissible things, and by 'ma alayha' is meant 'ma yajibu alayha' i.e., obligatory things. In this case, three types: doing obligatory, leaving forbidden, and leaving prohibitively disliked, will be included in 'ma alayha' because they are obligatory. And all actions other than the forbidden, and doing prohibitively disliked, and leaving other than obligatory, will be included in 'ma laha' because they are permissible. So now three types: doing forbidden, doing prohibitively disliked, and leaving obligatory, will be excluded from the definition of fiqh because they are neither permissible nor obligatory.

Explanation of the third meaning
(3) 'And it is possible that by 'ma laha wa ma alayha' is meant what is permissible for it and what is forbidden upon it': From here, the author explains the third meaning that by 'ma laha' is meant permissible things, and by 'ma alayha' is meant forbidden things. In this case also, all types will be included in the definition: doing forbidden, doing prohibitively disliked, leaving obligatory — these three are included in 'ma alayha' because they are forbidden; the remaining nine types are included in 'ma laha' because they are permissible; regardless of whether they are obligatory or not.

Summary: There are a total of five probabilities for the meaning of 'ma laha wa ma alayha': (1) What is meant is reward and punishment. (2) What is meant is punishment and absence of punishment. (3) What is meant is reward and absence of reward. (4) What is meant is permissibility and obligation. (5) What is meant is permissibility and prohibition.

'And the preferred (rajih) probability': With this, the author points to the prevalent probability, i.e., that probability in which all twelve types are included in the definition of fiqh. That probability is preferred (rajih), and there are three such probabilities: the second, third, and fifth.

Then he says: The definition of fiqh includes conventional (istilahi) fiqh, kalam, and tasawwuf.

'Then 'ma laha wa ma alayha' is expansive': From here, the author states that Imam Sahib (the author of the matn) in his definition of fiqh has...
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a definition of fiqh, specifically analyzing the phrase 'ma laha wa ma alayha' (ما لها وما عليها). The commentator explains that the matn author introduces this phrase as part of the definition of fiqh. The matn author first clarifies that by adding the condition 'with its proof', taqlid is excluded from being called 'knowledge' (ma'rifa) because taqlid relies on a mujtahid's statements, not direct proof. Then the commentator proceeds to explain the possible meanings of 'ma laha wa ma alayha'.

The commentator first establishes a premise: human actions are categorized into six types (wajib, mandub, mubah, makruh tahrimi, makruh tanzihi, haram). Each type can be done or left, so there are twelve scenarios (فعل/ترك of each). 

Then he gives three possible interpretations of the phrase:
1) 'Laha' = benefit (naf'), 'Alayha' = harm (darar). Under this, three sub-possibilities arise:
   a) Benefit = reward (thawab), harm = punishment ('iqab). Only 5 of the 12 actions are covered.
   b) Benefit = absence of punishment, harm = punishment. All 12 are covered.
   c) Benefit = reward, harm = absence of reward. All 12 are covered.
2) 'Laha' = permissible (ja'iz), 'Alayha' = obligatory (wajib). Here, 9 of the 12 are covered (excluding haram, etc.).
3) 'Laha' = permissible, 'Alayha' = forbidden (haram). All 12 are covered.

The commentator summarizes that there are five total probabilities: (1) reward/punishment, (2) absence of punishment/punishment, (3) reward/absence of reward, (4) permissible/obligatory, (5) permissible/forbidden. He then indicates that the preferred (rajih) meanings are those that include all twelve types: meanings 2, 3, and 5. These are worth noting because they ensure the definition of fiqh is comprehensive.

Finally, the commentator notes that the definition of fiqh also encompasses conventional fiqh, kalam (theology), and tasawwuf (mysticism), showing that the term 'fiqh' in the classical sense is broader than positive law. This passage is valuable for understanding the scope of fiqh in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
ما لها وما عليها (ma laha wa ma alayha): The phrase in the definition of fiqh referring to what is for and against the actions of a mukallaf; interpreted in multiple ways: benefit/harm, reward/punishment, permissible/obligatory, or permissible/forbidden.
فقہ (fiqh): Knowledge of the detailed practical rulings derived from their specific proofs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following interpretations of 'ma laha wa ma alayha' includes all twelve types of actions (six categories each with doing and leaving)?
A) Reward and punishment
B) Absence of punishment and punishment
C) Permissibility and obligation
D) Reward and absence of punishment

Key Takeaway
The definition of fiqh is comprehensive only when 'ma laha wa ma alayha' is interpreted as absence of punishment/punishment, reward/absence of reward, or permissible/forbidden, as these cover all twelve action types.

The Six Categories of Legal Actions and the Makruh Dispute
Explanation of the six ahkam taklifiyya and the disagreement between Imam Muhammad and the two shaykhs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six Hanafi categories of legal actions and explain the difference between Imam Muhammad's view and the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding makruh.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school divides actions into six categories, with a key internal dispute on the thresholds of makruh.

This passage from Sharh al-Tarweeh presents the foundational classification of legal actions (ahkam taklifiyya) in the Hanafi school. It first outlines Imam Muhammad's six-fold division based on preference and prevention, then introduces an alternative view from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf that refines the category of makruh. Understanding this dispute is essential for correctly applying the hierarchy of rulings in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six categories according to Imam Muhammad
Read the passage and list mubah, wajib, mandub, haram, makruh tahrimi, and makruh tanzihi. Note the criteria for each: preference, prevention, and proof strength.
2
Analyze the defining features of each category
Focus on how 'doing is preferable' vs. 'leaving is preferable', and whether there is 'prevention' from the opposite action. For haram and makruh tahrimi, note the difference in proof strength (qat'i vs. zanni).
Prevention means the law indicates the opposite action is not allowed.
3
Compare with the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
Under their view, when leaving is preferable, if there is prevention it is haram; without prevention, it is makruh tanzihi if closer to halal, or makruh tahrimi if closer to haram. Note the absence of a separate haram from zanni proof.
Imam Muhammad assigns haram and makruh tahrimi based on proof strength; the two shaykhs use proximity to halal/haram.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The same action (e.g., eating garlic before mosque) may be classified differently: on Imam Muhammad's view, if there's a probable prohibition, it is makruh tahrimi; on Abu Hanifa's, it could be either tanzihi or tahrimi depending on perceived closeness to haram.
The difference affects how the mufti advises the questioner.
5
Understand why the author prefers Imam Muhammad's view here
The author states that the matn (the base text) defined makruh tanzihi as 'permissible to do' and makruh tahrimi as 'not permissible to do' (like haram). This matches Imam Muhammad's scheme, so it is adopted for this commentary.
This shows how later Hanafi scholars often choose the view that best fits the text they are explaining.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْأَقْسَامُ اثْنَا عَشَرَ ؛ لِأَنَّ مَا يَأْتِي بِهِ الْمُكَلَّفَ إِنْ تَسَاوَى فِعْلُهُ وَتَرُكُهُ فَمُبَاحٌ وَإِلَّا ، فَإِنْ كَانَ فِعْلُهُ أَوْلَى فَمَعَ الْمَنْعِ عَنْ التَّرْكِ وَاجِبٌ وَبِدُونِهِ مَنْدُوبٌ ، وَإِنْ كَانَ تَرْكُهُ أَوْلَى فَمَعَ الْمَنْعِ عَنْ الْفِعْلِ بِدَلِيل قَطْعِى حَرَامٌ وَبِدَلِيلٍ ظَنِّيٍّ مَكْرُوهُ كَرَاهَةَ التَّحْرِيمِ وَبِدُونِ الْمَنْعِ عَنْ الْفِعْلِ مَكْرُوهُ كَرَاهَةَ التَّنْزِيهِ هَذَا عَلَى رَأْي مُحَمَّدٍ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ ، وَهُوَ الْمُنَاسِبُ هَهُنَا ؛ لأنَّ الْمُصَنِّفَ جَعَلَ الْمَكْرُوهَ تَنْزِيهَا مِمَّا يَجُوزُ فِعْلُهُ وَالْمَكْرُوه تَحْرِيمًا مِمَّا لَا يَجُوزُ فِعْلُهُ ، بَلْ يَجِبُ تَرُكُهُ كَالْحَرَامِ ، وَهَذَا لَا يَصِحُ عَلَى رَأْيِهِمَا ، وَهُوَ أَنَّ مَا يَكُونُ تَرُكُهُ أَوْلَى مِنْ فِعْلِهِ فَهُوَ مَعَ الْمَنْعِ عَنْ الْفِعْلِ حَرَامٌ وَبِدُونِهِ مَكْرُوهُ كَرَاهَةَ التَّنْزِيهِ إِنْ كَانَ إِلَى الْحِلِّ أَقْرَبَ بِمَعْنَى أَنَّهُ لَا يُعَاقَبُ فَاعِلُهُ لَكِنْ يُثَابُ تَارِكُهُ أَدْنَى ثَوَابٍ وَكَرَاهَةُ التَّحْرِيمِ إِن كَانَ إِلَى الْحَرَامِ أَقْرَبَ بِمَعْنَى أَنَّ فَاعِلَهُ مُسْتَحِقٌ مَذْمُومًا دُونَ الْعُقُوبَةِ بِالنَّارِ كَحِرْمَانِ الشَّفَاعَةِ .
And the divisions are twelve: because what the obligated person does, if its doing and leaving are equal, then it is permissible. Otherwise, if its doing is preferable, then with prevention from leaving it is obligatory, and without it [it is] recommended. And if its leaving is preferable, then with prevention from doing it by a definitive proof it is forbidden, and by a probable proof it is disliked with the dislike of prohibition, and without prevention from doing it, it is disliked with the dislike of detestability. This is according to the opinion of Muhammad, may God have mercy on him, and it is appropriate here because the author made the disliked of detestability from that which its doing is permissible, and the disliked of prohibition from that which its doing is not permissible, rather its leaving is obligatory like the forbidden. And this is not correct according to the opinion of them both, which is that that which its leaving is preferable to its doing, then with prevention from doing it is forbidden, and without it is disliked with the dislike of detestability if it is closer to the permissible, meaning that its doer is not punished but its leaver is rewarded with a minimal reward; and [it is] disliked with the dislike of prohibition if it is closer to the forbidden, meaning that its doer deserves blame without punishment by fire, like deprivation of intercession.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the classification of legal actions (ahkam taklifiyya) according to the Hanafi school, focusing on the internal dispute between Imam Muhammad and the two elder imams (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). The author first presents the six-fold division on the view of Imam Muhammad: mubah (permissible) when act and omission are equal; wajib (obligatory) when the act is preferable and omission is prevented; mandub (recommended) when act is preferable but without prevention; haram (forbidden) when omission is preferable and act is prevented by a definitive proof; makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) when omission is preferable and act is prevented by a probable proof; makruh tanzihi (detestably disliked) when omission is preferable but without prevention. The author notes that this classification aligns with the matn's definition of makruh tanzihi as permissible to do and makruh tahrimi as impermissible to do (like haram). He then contrasts the opinion of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, who divide the case where omission is preferable into: (a) if act is prevented, it is simply haram; (b) if not prevented, then it is makruh tanzihi if closer to halal (doer not punished, leaver gets minimal reward) or makruh tahrimi if closer to haram (doer deserves blame but not hellfire, e.g., deprivation of intercession). The passage thus clarifies a key usul principle about the hierarchy of rulings and shows how different imams within the Hanafi school applied the criteria.

Key Terms
مُبَاح (mubah): An action whose doing and leaving are equal; neither preferred nor prevented.
وَاجِب (wajib): An action whose doing is preferable and whose leaving is prevented (by a proof).
مَنْدُوب (mandub): An action whose doing is preferable but without prevention from leaving.
حَرَام (haram): An action whose leaving is preferable and whose doing is prevented by a definitive proof.
مَكْرُوهُ كَرَاهَةَ التَّحْرِيمِ (makruh karaahati al-tahrim): An action whose leaving is preferable, doing is prevented by a probable proof; doer is blameworthy but not punished with hellfire.
مَكْرُوهُ كَرَاهَةَ التَّنْزِيهِ (makruh karaahati al-tanzih): An action whose leaving is preferable but without prevention; doer not punished, leaver gets minimal reward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, how does makruh tahrimi differ from haram?
A) Makruh tahrimi is established by a definitive proof, haram by a probable proof.
B) Makruh tahrimi is established by a probable proof, haram by a definitive proof.
C) Makruh tahrimi is permissible to do, haram is not.
D) Makruh tahrimi and haram are identical.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines six legal categories, with a crucial distinction between the two types of makruh based on proof strength and the absence of punishment.
