The Five Categories of Actions and the Makruh Dispute
Explaining the types of legal actions and the internal Hanafi dispute on makruh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi classification of the five legal actions (ahkam) and distinguish between the views of Imam Muhammad and the two shaykhs on makruh tanzihi and tahrimi.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, makruh tahrimi is prohibited by conjectural proof, while makruh tanzihi is not prohibited; Imam Muhammad differs from the two shaykhs on the basis for this distinction.

This passage from the commentary on al-Tawdih and al-Talwih outlines the fundamental classification of actions (ahkam) in Hanafi usul. It then zooms into a key internal dispute: the definition of makruh tanzihi and tahrimi according to Imam Muhammad versus the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). Understanding this dispute is crucial for correctly applying the terms in fiqh and fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Five Categories
Name the five basic categories of actions (mubah, wajib, mandub, haram, makruh) and their definitions as given in the passage.
The passage lists six when splitting makruh into two subtypes.
2
Distinguish Makruh Tanzihi and Tahrimi
Note the two subtypes of makruh based on the strength of proof (qat'i vs zanni) and the presence/absence of prohibition.
For Imam Muhammad: tanzihi is permissible; tahrimi is impermissible like haram but with zanni proof.
3
Locate the Internal Ikhtilaf
Identify that Imam Muhammad defines them differently from the two shaykhs. The passage states the dispute explicitly.
The two shaykhs use proximity to halal/haram and presence of censure as criteria.
4
Compare the Two Definitions
For Imam Muhammad, makruh tanzihi is permissible to do; for the two shaykhs, it is similar to halal but with minor reward for avoidance. For makruh tahrimi, Imam Muhammad says its avoidance is obligatory like haram; the two shaykhs say it is closer to haram and entails blame.
The thamarah al-khilaf is in how to classify actions based on evidence vs. censure.
5
Understand the Tarjih
Note that the author (matn) adopts Imam Muhammad's view as appropriate here, though both positions are within the school.
The passage says 'and it is appropriate here' indicating a preference.

الترويج لحل التوضيح والتلويج لفظ معرفت کی جزئیات کا دلیل سے اور اک کرنے کے ساتھ۔ اور قید اخیر (عن دلیل ) ان اشیا میں سے ہے کہ نہیں ہے کوئی دلالت اس پر بالکل نہ لغتہ نہ اصطلاحا۔ اور گئے ہیں ( ماتن) اپنے قول مالہا و ما علیہا میں اس بات کی طرف جو کہی جاتی ہے کہ ل انتفاع کیلئے ہے اور "علی" ضر ر کیلئے ہے اور مقید کیا ہے ان دونوں کو اخروی کی قید کے ساتھ احتر از کبر تھے کیلئے اس سے کہ نفع اٹھاتا ہے اس کے ساتھ نفس یا نقصان ہوتا ہے اس کے ساتھ دنیا میں یعنی لذات اور آلام (وغیرہ) سے اور اشارہ کیا گیا ہے اس قید کے ساتھ اس بات کے مشہور ہونے کے کہ فقہ علوم دینیہ میں سے ہے پس ذکر کئے ان دونوں کے لئے اس تقدیر پر تین معانی پھر ذکر کیا دوسرے دو معانی کو پس ہو گئے معانی محتملہ پانچ تین ان میں سے مشتمل ہیں تمام ان اقسام کو جن کو مکلف بجالاتا ہے اور دو مشتمل نہیں ہیں ان تمام اقسام کو اور اقسام بارہ ہیں اس لئے جس (فنی ) کو مکلف بجالاتا ہے یا تو برابر ہو گا اس کا فعل اور اس کا ترک پس یہ مباح ہے وگرنہ پس اگر ہے اس کا فصل اولی تو پس ترک سے منع کے ساتھ واجب ہے اور اس کے خیر مندوب ہے اور اگر ہو اس کا ترک اولی تو پس فعل سے منع کے ساتھ دلیل قطعی سے حرام ہے اور دلیل ظنی سے مکر وہ کر است تحریمی ہے اور منع کے بغیر فعل سے مکروہ کراہتہ تنزیہی ہے۔ یہ امام محمد کی رائے پر ہے اور یہی مناسب ہے یہاں اس لئے کہ مصنف نے بتایا ہے مکروہ تنزیہی کو ان میں سے کہ جائز ہے ان کا فعل اور مکروہ تحریمی کو ان میں سے کہ نہیں ہے جائز ان کا فعل بلکہ واجب ہے اس کا ترک مثل حرام کے اور یہ نہیں ہے صحیح ان دونوں (شیخین) کی رائے پر اور وہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ہو اس کا ترک اولی اس کے فعل سے پس وہ مطلع کے ساتھ فعل سے حرام ہے اس کے بغیر مکروہ کراہتہ منتر یہی ہے اگر ہو حلال کے زیادہ قریب اس معنی کے ساتھ کہ بے شک نہیں عذاب دیا جائے گا اسکے کرنے والے کو لیکن ثواب دیا جائے گا اس کے ترک کرنے والے کو ادنی ثواب اور کراہتہ تحریمی کے ساتھ اگر ہو حرام کی طرف زیادہ قریب اس معنی کے ساتھ کہ بے شک اسکا کر نیوالا ستحق ہو گا ملامت (تنبیہ) کا آگ کے ساتھ سزا کے علاوہ مثل شفاعت سے محروم ہونے کے۔
The Tamhīd on the Solution of al-Tawḍīḥ and al-Talwīḥ. The word maʿrifah's particulars with evidence and... The last restriction (from evidence) is among things that have no indication at all, neither linguistically nor technically. The author (matn) points with his statement 'what is for it and what is against it' to what is said that 'lām' is for benefit and 'ʿalā' is for harm. He restricted both with the restriction of the Hereafter to avoid the case that benefit is for the self or harm is for the self in this world, i.e., pleasures and pains. With this restriction, it is indicated that fiqh is among religious sciences. Then he mentioned for both, on this assumption, three meanings, then he mentioned two other meanings, so the possible meanings became five. Three of them include all the categories that the legally responsible person does, and two do not include all those categories. The categories are twelve. Therefore, whatever the responsible person does: either his action and his abandonment are equal — that is permissible (mubāḥ). Otherwise, if his action is more virtuous, then with prohibition of abandonment it is obligatory (wājib), and without that it is recommended (mandūb). If his abandonment is more virtuous, then with prohibition of action by a definitive proof it is forbidden (ḥarām), and by a conjectural proof it is prohibitively disliked (makrūh taḥrīmī). Without prohibition, it is lightly disliked (makrūh tanzīhī). This is according to Imam Muḥammad's opinion, and it is appropriate here because the author stated that makrūh tanzīhī is among those whose action is permissible, and makrūh taḥrīmī is among those whose action is not permissible; rather, its abandonment is obligatory like ḥarām. But this is not correct according to the two shaykhs (Imām Abū Ḥanīfa and Abū Yūsuf). Their view is: if abandonment is more virtuous than action, then if accompanied by censure, action is ḥarām; if without censure, it is makrūh karāhah — that is, if it is closer to ḥalāl in the sense that the doer will not be punished but the abandoner will receive minor reward. And if it is closer to ḥarām, then it is makrūh taḥrīmī in the sense that the doer deserves blame (admonition) in addition to punishment, such as deprivation of intercession.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage is an expansion by the commentator (shārīḥ) explaining the author's (matn) classification of legal actions and the difference between Imām Muḥammad and the two shaykhs (Imām Abū Ḥanīfa and Abū Yūsuf) regarding the definition of makrūh. The author begins by discussing the word maʿrifah and its particulars, noting that the final restriction (from evidence) refers to things that have no indication linguistically or technically. He then explains the author's phrase 'what is for it and what is against it,' noting that lām indicates benefit and ʿalā indicates harm. Both are restricted to the Hereafter to exclude worldly benefits and harms. The author then mentions five possible meanings for this phrase, three of which cover all actions of the mukallaf and two that do not. The passage then lists the categories of actions: mubāḥ (where action and abandonment are equal), wājib (action preferred, abandonment prohibited), mandūb (action preferred without prohibition), ḥarām (abandonment preferred, action prohibited by definitive proof), makrūh taḥrīmī (abandonment preferred, action prohibited by conjectural proof), and makrūh tanzīhī (abandonment preferred, action not prohibited). The commentator notes that this classification follows Imām Muḥammad's view, where makrūh tanzīhī is permissible and makrūh taḥrīmī is impermissible (its avoidance is obligatory like ḥarām). However, according to the two shaykhs, the distinction is based on proximity to ḥalāl or ḥarām. If abandonment is considered more virtuous, then if the action is accompanied by censure, it is ḥarām; if not, it is makrūh (tanzīhī). They define makrūh tanzīhī as being closer to ḥalāl (no punishment for action, minor reward for avoidance) and makrūh taḥrīmī as being closer to ḥarām (doer deserves blame and may be deprived of intercession). The passage thus clarifies the Hanafī internal disagreement on the classification of disliked actions, emphasizing that the author (Ṣadr al‐Sharīʿa?) adopts Imām Muḥammad's classification as appropriate here.

Key Terms
مُباح (mubāḥ): Action whose doing and leaving are equal, neither favored.
واجب (wājib): Action whose performance is preferred and its abandonment is prohibited.
مندوب (mandūb): Action whose performance is preferred without prohibition of abandonment.
حرام (ḥarām): Action whose abandonment is preferred and its performance is prohibited by a definitive proof.
مكروه تحريمي (makrūh taḥrīmī): Action whose performance is prohibited by a conjectural proof; its abandonment is obligatory.
مكروه تنزيهي (makrūh tanzīhī): Action whose performance is not prohibited but its abandonment is preferred.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, what is the classification of an action whose abandonment is more virtuous and whose performance is prohibited by a conjectural proof?
A) Haram
B) Makruh Tahrimi
C) Makruh Tanzihi
D) Wajib

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school divides disliked actions (makruh) into two: tanzihi (not prohibited) and tahrimi (prohibited by zanni evidence); the exact definition varies between Imam Muhammad and the two shaykhs, with the author preferring Imam Muhammad's view.

Why Ma‘rifa Requires a Proof: Defending 'an Dalil
Defending the inclusion of 'an dalil in the definition of ma‘rifa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school requires the condition 'an dalil in the definition of ma‘rifa in fiqh, and apply this to distinguish ma‘rifa from other types of knowledge.

Core Idea
For the knowledge of rulings (ma‘rifa) in fiqh, proof is not optional — it is the very condition that makes it ma‘rifa.

The commentator objects that the restriction 'an dalil has no basis in language or convention. The author provides two robust answers: one from the linguistic definition of ma‘rifa itself (citing Imam Raghib al-Isfahani), and another from the nature of fiqh — that the ma‘rifa intended here is specifically knowledge of rulings (mā lahā wa mā ‘alayhā), which inevitably requires inference from proofs. This lesson unpacks that reasoning and shows why, for the Hanafi school, ma‘rifa of ahkam always requires istidlal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested term and restriction
Locate the term ma‘rifa and the added restriction 'an dalil in the definition. Understand the commentator's objection: that this restriction has no evidence in language or convention.
The objection is not against ma‘rifa itself, but against the necessity of the restriction.
2
Examine the first answer: linguistic evidence
Read the citation from Imam Raghib al-Isfahani's linguistic definition. Note that he includes the concept of istidlal (inference) in his definition of ma‘rifa.
This shows the restriction is grounded in Arabic usage, not an arbitrary insertion.
3
Examine the second answer: teleological necessity
Even if the linguistic definition were unrestricted, the ma‘rifa intended in fiqh is not absolute ma‘rifa but knowledge of rulings (mā lahā wa mā ‘alayhā). Rulings are derived from proofs, so the restriction is necessary.
This answer reframes the objection: the restriction is not about ma‘rifa in general, but about the specific ma‘rifa relevant to fiqh.
4
Derive the methodological implication
Understand that in Hanafi usul, any claim to know a ruling without a proof (dalil) is not considered ma‘rifa. This ensures that rulings are based on evidence, not conjecture.
This distinguishes ma‘rifa from mere opinion or sensory knowledge.
5
Apply to a scenario
Consider a student who says 'I know that drinking grape juice is halal without looking at any text.' Would this be considered ma‘rifa? No, because it lacks istidlal.
The lesson reinforces that ma‘rifa in fiqh always requires a proof chain.

جواب:۔ یہاں روح سے محض روح مراد نہیں بلکہ روح حالہ فی الجسد یعنی وہ روح مراد ہے جو جسم میں حلول کئے ہوئے ہو اور اس ہے متکلمین بحث کرتے ہیں۔ فلا اشکال۔ معرفت کی قید میں عن دلیل کی قید لگانا درست ہے وفسر المعرفةہ بادراک الجزئیات عن دلیل : یہ شرح کی عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے یہاں سے شاریخ مصنف کی عبارت پر اعتراض کر رہے ہیں کہ ماتن نے معرفہ کی تعریف میں عمن دلیل کی قید لگائی ہے اور ماتن کا یہ قید لگانا بغیر ولیل کے ہے کیونکہ اس قید پر نہ تو لفتہ کوئی ثبوت ہے اور نہ اصطلا حالہذا یہ قید درست نہیں ہے لیکن اس اعتراض کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اولا تو آپ کا یہ کہنا درست نہیں ہے کہ لغت میں اس کا ثبوت نہیں کیونکہ علامہ راغب اصفہانی نے لغت کی کتاب میں معرفتہ کی تعریف کی ہے اور انہوں نے یہ قید لگائی ہے اور وہ تعریف یہ ہے المعرفة اسم لما تحصل من العلم بعد تذكر المعهو دوالاستدلال بالآثار كه معرفت نام ہے ایسی شی کا جو حاصل ہو علم سے بھولے ہوئے کو یاد کرنے کے بعد اور علامات کے ساتھ استدلال کرنے کے بعد تو تعریف میں استدلال کا لفظ ہے جس کے معنی دلیل پکڑنا ہی ہوتا ہے لھذا شاریخ کا یہ کہنا غلط ہوا کہ لغتہ دلیل کی قید پر کوئی ثبوت نہیں دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ اگر مان لیا جائے کہ لغت میں معرفہ کی تعریف دلیل کی قید کے بغیر ہے تب بھی ماتن کی تعریف درست ہے کیونکہ یہاں مطلقا معرفت کی تعریف نہیں ہو رہی بلکہ اس معرفت کی تعریف ہے جس کا ذکر فقہ کی تعریف میں ہے. اور وہ ہے معرفہ النفس مالھاو ماعلیہا اور مالھاو ماعلیہا سے مرادا حکام ہیں اور احکام کی معرفت کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ استدلال کی صلاحیت بھی ہو اس لئے معرفت کی تعریف میں دلیل کی قید لگانا ضروری ہے کیونکہ اس کے بغیر مالھا و ماعلیھا کی معرفت حاصل ہی نہیں ہو سکتی۔
Answer: Here, by 'soul' is not meant pure soul, but the soul in the body, i.e., that soul which is dwelling in the body. And the Mutakallimun discuss this. So no problem. Restricting ma‘rifa with 'an dalil is correct. 'And he interpreted ma‘rifa as perception of particulars from a proof': this is the third part of the commentary's expression. From here, the commentator objects to the author's expression, saying that the author placed the restriction 'an dalil in the definition of ma‘rifa, and the author's placing this restriction is without evidence, because for this restriction there is neither any proof in language nor in convention? so this restriction is not correct. But the answer to this objection is that, first, your saying that there is no proof for it in language is not correct, because Allamah Raghib al-Isfahani defined ma‘rifa in his book on language, and he placed this restriction. And that definition is: 'Al-ma‘rifa is a name for that which is obtained from knowledge after recalling the forgotten and inferring by signs.' So in the definition there is the word 'istidlal' which means to take a proof. Therefore, the commentator's statement that there is no proof for the restriction of proof in language is wrong. The second answer is that if it is accepted that in language the definition of ma‘rifa is without the restriction of proof, even then the author's definition is correct, because here the definition of ma‘rifa is not absolute, but rather the definition of that ma‘rifa which is mentioned in the definition of fiqh. And that is 'ma‘rifat al-nafs mā lahā wa mā ‘alayhā', and by 'mā lahā wa mā ‘alayhā' is meant the rulings. And for the knowledge of rulings, it is necessary to have the ability to infer. Therefore, it is necessary to place the restriction of proof in the definition of ma‘rifa, because without it, knowledge of mā lahā wa mā ‘alayhā cannot be attained.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage is a defense of the definition of ma‘rifa that includes the restriction 'an dalil (from a proof). The author (al-Matn) had defined ma‘rifa as perception of particulars from a proof, and the commentator (al-Sharih) objected that this restriction has no basis in language or convention. The text provides two answers. First, it cites Imam Raghib al-Isfahani's linguistic definition which includes the concept of istidlal (inference), proving that the restriction is rooted in language. Second, even if the linguistic definition were unrestricted, the ma‘rifa intended in fiqh is specifically the knowledge of rulings (mā lahā wa mā ‘alayhā), which inevitably requires inference from proofs. Therefore, the restriction is necessary. The commentary follows the Hanafi usul tradition of emphasizing the role of inference (istidlal) in deriving rulings.

Key Terms
معرفت (ma‘rifa): Perception of particulars from a proof, specifically knowledge of rulings (mā lahā wa mā ‘alayhā).
عن دلیل ('an dalil): From a proof; the condition that knowledge must be based on evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the Mutakallimun require it.
B) Because the definition of fiqh involves knowledge of rulings (mā lahā wa mā ‘alayhā) which requires inference.
C) Because Imam Raghib al-Isfahani included it.
D) Because without it, ma‘rifa would be impossible.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of ma‘rifa in fiqh necessarily includes the condition 'an dalil because knowledge of rulings can only be attained through inferential reasoning from evidence.

Understanding 'Mā Lahā wa Mā ‘Alayhā' and the Otherworldly Restriction
Analysis of a key phrase in the definition of fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the meaning of 'mā lahā wa mā ‘alayhā' in the Hanafi definition of fiqh and justify why the qayd al-ukhrāwī is necessary.

Core Idea
Fiqh concerns only otherworldly benefit and harm, excluding worldly pleasures and pains.

The definition of fiqh includes the phrase 'mā lahā wa mā ‘alayhā'—what is for it and against it. But not all benefits and harms are meant; the text explicitly adds 'ukhrāwī' (otherworldly). This lesson unpacks why this restriction is critical and how it shapes the subject matter of fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phrase and its components
Locate 'mā lahā wa mā ‘alayhā' in the definition. Note that 'lām' indicates benefit and 'alā' indicates harm.
This is the core of the definition.
2
Recognize the restriction (qayd al-ukhrāwī)
The benefit and harm are limited to the Hereafter. This excludes worldly benefits (e.g., pleasure) and worldly harms (e.g., pain).
Without this restriction, fiqh could be confused with worldly sciences.
3
Understand the objection and its answer
An objection: why add 'ukhrāwī' when fiqh is already a religious science? The answer: the fame (shuhra) of fiqh as a religious science itself indicates that the benefits and harms are otherworldly.
The objection tests the necessity of the explicit qayd.
4
Consider the five probabilities
The author mentioned five probabilities regarding the scope of 'mā lahā wa mā ‘alayhā'. Three cover all actions of the mukallaf; two do not. This shows the depth of analysis.
This step is optional but demonstrates Hanafi precision.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذهب في قوله مالھاو ماعلیھا :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا چوتھا حصہ ہے۔ غرض شاریخ : ۔ یہاں سے شاریخ عبارت کی وضاحت فرمارہے ہیں کہ مائن نے مالھا میں لام کو نفع کے لئے اور ماعلیھا میں علی کوضرر کے لئے بنایا ہے اور اس نفع اور ضرر کو اخروی کی قید کے ساتھ مقید فرمایا ہے اور یہ اخروی کی قید اس لئے لگائی کہ ان سے وہ چیز خارج ہو جائے جن سے نفس کو دنیوی فائدہ مثلا لذات اور دنیوی ضرر مثلا آلام حاصل ہوتے ہیں۔ والمشعر بهذا القيد : ۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پانچواں حصہ ہے۔ غرض شاریخ:۔ ایک اعتراض کا جواب دینا ہے۔  اعتراض:۔ مصنف نے اخروی کی قید کا اضافہ کیوں کیا ہے اس پر کیا قرینہ ہے؟ جواب:۔ یہ بات مشہور ہے کہ فقہ علوم دینیہ میں سے ہے اور یہی شہرت اس بات پر دلیل ہے کہ یہاں نفع وضرر سے مراد اخروی نفع و ضرر ہے۔ فذكر على هذا التقدیر:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا چھٹا حصہ ہے۔ غرض: توضیح بالمتن ہے یہاں سے اس بات کی وضاحت فرما رہے ہیں کہ مائن نے مالھا میں لام نفع کے لئے اور وما علیھا میں علی کو ضرر کے لئے بنایا ہے پھر آئیں تین احتمال بیان کیے ہیں تو کل پانچ احتمال ہو گئے جن میں سے تین احتمال ( دوسرا۔ تیسرا ۔ اور پانچواں ) تو مکلف کے افعال کی ساری اقسام کو شامل ہے اور دو احتمال تمام اقسام کو شامل نہیں ہیں بلکہ بعض اقسام کو شامل ہیں بعض کو نہیں ۔
And he (the author) said 'mā lahā wa mā ‘alayhā': This is the fourth part of the commentary's expression. Purpose of the commentator: From here, the commentator explains that the author used 'lām' in 'mā lahā' for benefit and 'alā' in 'mā ‘alayhā' for harm, and he restricted this benefit and harm with the qayd al-ukhrāwī (otherworldly). And this qayd al-ukhrāwī was placed so that those things by which worldly benefit like pleasures and worldly harm like pains are obtained are excluded. 'And indicating by this qayd': This is the fifth part of the commentary's expression. Purpose of the commentator: To answer an objection. [Page 217] Objection: Why did the author add the qayd al-ukhrāwī? What is the evidence for it? Answer: It is well known that fiqh is among the religious sciences, and this fame is proof that here by benefit and harm is meant otherworldly benefit and harm. 'So he mentioned on this basis': This is the sixth part of the commentary's expression. Purpose: Explanation of the text. From here, it is clarified that the author used 'lām' in 'mā lahā' for benefit and 'alā' in 'mā ‘alayhā' for harm. Then three probabilities are mentioned, so there are five probabilities in total. Among them, three probabilities (second, third, and fifth) include all categories of the actions of the mukallaf, and two probabilities do not include all categories but include some and not others.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage explains the key phrase 'mā lahā wa mā ‘alayhā' (what is for it and what is against it) in the definition of fiqh. The commentator clarifies that 'lām' indicates benefit and 'alā' indicates harm, and both are restricted to the akhira (otherworldly) context. This is to exclude worldly benefits and harms like pleasure and pain. An objection is raised: why add this otherworldly restriction? The answer is that fiqh is a religious science, so its benefits and harms are inherently otherworldly. The passage then mentions that the author considered five probabilities regarding the scope of this phrase, three of which cover all actions of the mukallaf, while two do not. This analysis is typical of Hanafi usul, emphasizing the precise scope of definitions.

Key Terms
مالھا و ماعلیھا (mā lahā wa mā ‘alayhā): What is for it (benefit) and what is against it (harm); specifically otherworldly benefit and harm.
اخروی (ukhrāwī): Pertaining to the Hereafter; otherworldly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

What is the purpose of the qayd al-ukhrāwī in the definition of fiqh?
A) To include worldly pleasures and pains.
B) To exclude worldly benefits and harms, ensuring fiqh focuses on otherworldly consequences.
C) To indicate that fiqh is a worldly science.
D) To limit the definition to actions of worship only.

Key Takeaway
Fiqh is defined by otherworldly benefit and harm; the qayd al-ukhrāwī is necessary to distinguish it from worldly sciences.

The 12 Divisions of Ahkām and the Ikhtilāf on Makrūh Tahrimī
Logical division of ahkām into 12 types with ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi classification of the 12 types of rulings (ahkām) and explain the disagreement between Imam Muhammad and the Shaykhayn regarding the placement of makrūh tahrimī.

Core Idea
Makrūh tahrimī is prohibited by a zannī proof, unlike haram which is from a qat‘ī proof — a key Hanafi distinction.

This passage details the logical enumeration of the actions of a mukallaf into 12 categories. While the first part — covering mubāḥ, wājib, and mandūb — is agreed upon, there is a notable ikhtilāf regarding the classification when omission is preponderant. Imam Muhammad introduces a further subdivision based on the strength of the prohibitory evidence, leading to the distinct category of makrūh tahrimī.

Guided Path
1
Understand the enumeration principle
Actions are first divided by whether act and omission are equal (mubāḥ) or not. If not equal, the preponderant side is either act or omission.
This part is agreed upon by all.
2
Trace the agreed-upon part for preponderant act
If act is preponderant and omission is prohibited → wājib; if omission is not prohibited → mandūb.
These are the first two categories after mubāḥ.
3
Locate the point of ikhtilāf
When omission is preponderant, there is a difference between Imam Muhammad and the Shaykhayn (Abū Hanīfa and Abū Yūsuf).
The text cuts off for Shaykhayn's view; we reconstruct from standard Hanafi usul.
4
Follow Imam Muhammad's division
If act is not prohibited → makrūh tanzihī; if prohibited, check proof strength: qat‘ī → haram, zannī → makrūh tahrimī.
This yields 12 total categories when combined with the earlier divisions.
5
Note the gap for Shaykhayn
The text is incomplete for Shaykhayn. Known from other sources, they consider any prohibition (regardless of proof strength) as haram, thus merging the last two categories.
This ikhtilāf affects the practical weight of actions prohibited by speculative evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والاقسام اثنی عشر: یہ شرح کی عبارت کا ساتواں حصہ ہے۔ غرض: مکلف کے افعال کی وضاحت کرتا ہے کہ مکلف جن افعال کو بجالاتا ہے انکی بارہ اقسام ہیں جنکی وجہ ھر مندرجہ ذیل ہے۔ وجه حصر: مکلف جس چیز کو بجالاتا ہے وہ دو حال سے خالی نہیں کہ اسکا فعل اور ترک برابر ہوگا یا نہیں : اگر فعل اور ترک برابر ہے تو وہ مباح ہے اور اگر برابر نہیں تو پھر دو حال سے خالی نہیں کہ جانب فعل رائج ہوگی یا جانب ترک، اگر جانب فعل را جج ہو تو پھر دو حال سے خالی نہیں کہ اس کے ترک سے منع کیا گیا ہوگا یا نہیں : اگر منع کیا گیا ہو تو واجب ہے۔ اور اگر منع نہ کیا گیا ہو تو مندوب ہے۔ قائدہ : یہاں تک وجہ حصر متفق علیہ ہے لیکن اس سے انگلی وجہ حصر میں امام محمد اور شینیون کا اختلاف ہے۔ امام محمد کے نزدیک آگے والی وجہ حصر یوں ہے کہ اگر اس کی جانب ترک اولی ہے تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں کہ جانب فعل سے منع کیا گیا ہوگا یا منع نہیں کیا گیا ہوگا اگر منع نہ کیا گیا ہو تو یہ مکروہ تنزیہی ہے اور اگر منع کیا گیا ہو تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں کہ یہ مع دلیل قطعی سے ہوگا یا دلیل تنطنی سے اگر دلیل قطعی سے ہو تو وہ حرام ہے اور اگر دلیل فنی سے ہو تو مکروہ تحریمی ہے۔ اور شیخین کے نزدیک وجہ عصر کیوں ہے کہ اگر اس لئی کی جاب ترک اولی ہے تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں کہ اس کے فعل
And the divisions are twelve: This is the seventh part of the commentary's expression. Purpose: It clarifies the actions of the mukallaf, that the actions performed by the mukallaf have twelve types, the reason for which is as follows. Reason for enumeration: The thing that the mukallaf does is not free from two states: either its doing and leaving are equal, or not. If doing and leaving are equal, then it is mubah. If not equal, then it is not free from two states: either the side of doing is preponderant or the side of leaving. If the side of doing is preponderant, then it is not free from two states: either its leaving has been prohibited or not. If its leaving has been prohibited, then it is wajib. And if it has not been prohibited, then it is mandub. Principle: Up to here, the reason for enumeration is agreed upon. But after this, there is a difference between Imam Muhammad and the Shaykhayn regarding the reason for enumeration. According to Imam Muhammad, the subsequent reason for enumeration is as follows: If the side of leaving is preponderant, then it is not free from two states: either doing has been prohibited or not prohibited. If it has not been prohibited, then it is makruh tanzihi. And if it has been prohibited, then it is not free from two states: either this is with a definitive proof or with a speculative proof. If with a definitive proof, then it is haram. And if with a speculative proof, then it is makruh tahrimi. And according to the Shaykhayn, the reason for enumeration is that if the side of leaving is preponderant, then it is not free from two states: its doing... [cut off]
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage presents the standard Hanafi classification of the 12 types of ahkam (rulings) related to the actions of the mukallaf. The first part, agreed upon by all, divides actions based on whether act and omission are equal (mubah) or one side is preponderant. If act is preponderant, and omission is forbidden, it is wajib; if not forbidden, it is mandub. The second part deals with cases where omission is preponderant, and here there is ikhtilaf. According to Imam Muhammad (one of the major Hanafi authorities), if omission is preponderant and the act is not prohibited, it is makruh tanzihi (disliked but not prohibited). If the act is prohibited, then depending on the strength of the proof: if the proof is qat‘i (definitive), it is haram; if it is zanni (speculative), it is makruh tahrimi (prohibitedly disliked). The Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, or according to some, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) have a different division, but the text cuts off before detailing it. This ikhtilaf is important in Hanafi usul as it affects how rulings are categorized and prioritized.

Key Terms
مکروہ تحریمی (makruh tahrimi): An action whose prohibition is established by a speculative (zanni) proof; it is prohibited but not as severely as haram.
مکروہ تنزیہی (makruh tanzihi): An action that is disliked but not prohibited; its omission is preponderant but there is no prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, an action whose omission is preponderant and whose doing is prohibited by a speculative (zanni) proof is classified as:
A) Haram
B) Makruh Tahrimi
C) Makruh Tanzihi
D) Wajib

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification of ahkām distinguishes between prohibitions based on proof certainty, leading to the unique category of makrūh tahrimī.

Logical Classification of Actions: The 12 Categories and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explaining the 12 categories and the ikhtilaf in their derivation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi classification system for actions by tracing the logical chain and distinguishing between Imam Muhammad's and the Shaykhayn's methods for subdividing when omission is preferable.

Core Idea
The 12 categories derive from a logical dichotomy; the dispute is how to subdivide when omission is preferable.

The Hanafi school classifies all actions (af‘al al-mukallaf) into 12 categories, derived from a logical chain starting with the equality or preference of act vs. omission. While the first steps are agreed upon, a key intra-Hanafi dispute arises at the stage where omission is preferable: Imam Muhammad uses the strength of evidence (qat‘i vs. zanni) to distinguish haram from makruh tahrimi, while the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) use the closeness of the act to halal or haram. This lesson will walk you through the logical chain and the practical consequences of this ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Agreed initial dichotomy
Start with the act and omission: are they equal or not? If equal, the action is mubah. If not, the side of act or omission is preponderant.
This is the starting point of the classification.
2
Act side preponderant (agreed)
If the act side is preponderant, check if omission is prohibited. If prohibited, it is wajib. If not prohibited, it is mandub.
No disagreement up to this point.
3
Omission side preponderant (point of dispute)
Now both agree that further subdivision is needed, but differ in method. Study Imam Muhammad's method: first check if the act is prohibited. If not, it is makruh tanzihi. If prohibited, check evidence strength: qat‘i → haram, zanni → makruh tahrimi.
4
Shaykhayn's alternative method
Under the Shaykhayn, if the act is prohibited, it is haram directly. If not prohibited, judge closeness: close to halal → makruh tanzihi; close to haram → makruh tahrimi.
This yields different classifications for some actions.
5
Practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The difference affects the Hereafter: according to Imam Muhammad, the doer of makruh tahrimi deserves punishment in fire; according to the Shaykhayn, he is deprived of intercession for higher ranks but not punished in fire.
The commentator notes that Imam Muhammad's view fits the matn's pairing of tanzihi with permissibility and tahrimi with impermissibility.

Source Text

فذكر على هذا التقدیر:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا چھٹا حصہ ہے۔ غرض: توضیح بالمتن ہے یہاں سے اس بات کی وضاحت فرما رہے ہیں کہ مائن نے مالھا میں لام نفع کے لئے اور وما علیھا میں علی کو ضرر کے لئے بنایا ہے پھر فعل کا مرتکب ہو یعنی مکروہ تحریمی کا۔ جواب:۔ شفاعت کی دو تمیں میں ایک ہے جہنم سے نجات کے لئے شفاعت اور دوسری ہے جنت میں ترقی درجات کیلئے شفاعت (جیسے اولاد کا والدین کے پاس پہنچنا ) تو حدیث میں اول شفاعت کا ذکر ہے اور مصنف نے جو بات کی ہے اس سے مراد وہ شفاعت ہے جو ترقی درجات کیلئے ہوتی ہے یعنی مکروہ تحریمی کا مرتکب ترقی درجات والی شفاعت سے محروم ہو گا۔
Objection: Why did the author add the restriction 'otherworldly' and what is the contextual indicator? Answer: It is well-known that fiqh is among the religious sciences, and this notoriety indicates that here benefit and harm mean otherworldly benefit and harm. Then he said: upon this estimation. This is the sixth part of the commentary text. Purpose: It is an elaboration with the matn; from here he is clarifying that the author (matn) placed the lam in 'laha' for benefit and the 'ala' in 'ma alayha' for harm. Then he mentioned three probabilities, so there are five probabilities in total. Among them, three probabilities (second, third, fifth) encompass all categories of the mukallaf's actions, and two probabilities do not encompass all categories but include some and exclude others. The disagreement between the Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad regarding the basis for the twelve categories of rulings. 'And the categories are twelve': this is the seventh part of the commentary text. Purpose: Explaining the actions of the mukallaf, that the actions he performs have twelve categories, the basis of which is as follows. Basis for enumeration: Whatever the mukallaf does is not free from two states: either his act and omission are equal or not. If act and omission are equal, it is mubah. If not equal, then it is not free from two states: either the side of the act is preponderant or the side of omission. If the side of the act is preponderant, then it is not free from two states: is its omission prohibited or not? If prohibited, it is wajib. If not prohibited, it is mandub. Rule: Up to here the basis is agreed upon, but after this there is disagreement between Imam Muhammad and the Shaykhayn in the basis. According to Imam Muhammad, the subsequent basis is: if the side of omission is preferable, then it is not free from two states: is its act prohibited or not? If not prohibited, it is makruh tanzihi. If prohibited, then it is not free from two states: is this prohibition by definitive evidence or speculative evidence? If by definitive evidence, it is haram; if by speculative evidence, it is makruh tahrimi. According to the Shaykhayn, the basis is: if the side of omission is preferable, then it is not free from two states: is its act prohibited or not? If prohibited, it is haram. If not prohibited, then it is not free from two states: is it closer to permissibility or prohibition? If closer to permissibility, it is makruh tanzihi; if closer to prohibition, it is makruh tahrimi. And it (Imam Muhammad's view) is appropriate here: This is the eighth part of the commentary text. The commentator determined the appropriate madhhab according to context: since the matn considered tanzihi as permissible and tahrimi as impermissible, and this is the madhhab of Imam Muhammad, so taking his basis for enumeration is appropriate here. Practical difference: The commentator stated that according to Imam Muhammad, the committer of makruh tahrimi deserves punishment and torment in fire; according to the Shaykhayn, the committer of makruh tahrimi does not deserve torment in fire, but he deserves deprivation, for example he will be deprived of intercession. Is the committer of makruh tahrimi deprived of intercession? Objection: Your statement (ﷺ) 'My intercession is for the people of major sins from my ummah' indicates that even the committer of a major sin (i.e., haram) will not be deprived of intercession. So how can a person who commits only an act close to haram (i.e., makruh tahrimi) be deprived of intercession? Answer: There are two types of intercession: one is intercession for deliverance from Hell, and the second is intercession for elevation of ranks in Paradise (like a child reaching their parents). The hadith refers to the first intercession, and what the author said refers to intercession for elevation of ranks, i.e., the committer of makruh tahrimi will be deprived of the intercession for elevation of ranks.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the classification of actions (ahkam al-taklifiyya) from Al-Tawdih. It begins by addressing an objection: why did the author of the matn add 'otherworldly' to the definition of fiqh? The answer is that the benefit and harm in fiqh are understood to be otherworldly due to common usage. The commentator then explains that the text clarifies the five probabilities regarding benefit and harm in the verse. The main discussion is about the twelve categories of actions and the disagreement between Imam Muhammad and the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) on the reasoning for the later subdivisions. Up to the point of balancing act and omission, all agree: if equal, mubah; if act side is preponderant and omission prohibited, wajib; otherwise mandub. After that, when omission is preferable, they differ. Imam Muhammad's method: if act not prohibited, makruh tanzihi; if prohibited, then see evidence: qat'i → haram, zanni → makruh tahrimi. The Shaykhayn's method: if act prohibited, haram; if not, then judge closeness: close to halal → tanzihi; close to haram → tahrimi. The commentator notes that the matn adopted Imam Muhammad's view, which matches its pairing of tanzihi with permissibility and tahrimi with impermissibility. The practical consequence is regarding punishment: according to Imam Muhammad, the doer of makruh tahrimi deserves punishment in fire; according to the Shaykhayn, he does not, but is deprived of intercession for higher ranks. An objection based on the hadith about intercession for major sinners is answered by distinguishing between intercession for deliverance from Hell (for major sins) and intercession for elevation of ranks (which the doer of makruh tahrimi misses).

Key Terms
وجہ حصر (wajh al-hasr): The logical basis or reasoning by which the categories are enumerated (divided into 12).
مکروہ تحریمی (makruh tahrimi): An act that is prohibited by speculative (zanni) evidence; it is impermissible but does not necessitate punishment in the Hereafter according to some (Shaykhayn), but according to others (Imam Muhammad) it does necessitate punishment.
مکروہ تنزیہی (makruh tanzihi): An act that is disliked but not prohibited; its omission is preferable but performance is not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, what distinguishes haram from makruh tahrimi when omission is preferable and the act is prohibited?
A) Whether the act is close to halal or haram
B) The strength of the evidence (qat'i vs zanni)
C) Whether the act is performed intentionally
D) The presence of intercession

Key Takeaway
The 12 categories are derived by a logical chain; the main intra-Hanafi dispute is whether makruh tahrimi is determined by evidence strength (Imam Muhammad) or proximity to haram (Shaykhayn).

Broad Hanafi Usage of Wajib and Mandub
Terminological clarification with classification implication

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafi usul includes fard under 'wajib' and sunnah/nafl under 'mandub', and apply this broad classification to derive the twelve categories of actions.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, 'wajib' broadly includes fard; 'mandub' includes sunnah and nafl.

This passage from Al-Tawdih addresses a common terminological point: in the classification of the twelve categories of actions, the terms 'wajib' and 'mandub' are not used in their narrow senses. Instead, they encompass all obligatory and recommended acts respectively. Understanding this broad usage is essential for correctly mapping the six primary rulings onto the twelve-fold classification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the broad definition of 'wajib'
The passage states that 'wajib' here includes fard. This is supported by common usage: e.g., 'Zakat is wajib' despite Zakat being fard. Note the contrast: they do not extend 'haram' to makruh tahrimi.
This broad use is specific to the classification context, not always.
2
Identify the broad definition of 'mandub'
Similarly, 'mandub' includes both sunnah and nafl. This grouping simplifies the primary categories to six.
Sunnah is emphasized, nafl is supererogatory, but both are non-obligatory.
3
Understand the six primary categories
With these broad meanings, the primary categories are: wajib (includes fard), mandub (includes sunnah+nafl), mubah, makruh tanzihi, makruh tahrimi, haram. Each is a single hukm.
These are the six Ahkam al-Taklifiyyah in this classification.
4
Derive the twelve categories
Each of the six rulings has two sides: act (doing) and omission (not doing). Thus, 6 × 2 = 12. The passage emphasizes that these are not separate rulings but aspects of the same ruling.
For example, 'wajib performance' and 'wajib omission' are not separate rulings; the ruling is wajib, and its breach is sin.

ثُمَّ الْمُرَادُ بِالْوَاجِبِ مَا يَشْمَلُ الْفَرْضَ أَيْضًا ؛ لِأَنَّ اسْتِعْمَالَهُ بِهَذَا الْمَعْنَى شَائِعٌ عِنْدَهُمْ كَقَوْلِهِمُ الزَّكَاةَ وَاجِبَةٌ وَالْحَج وَاجِبٌ بِخِلَافِ إِطْلَاقِ الْحَرَامِ عَلَى الْمَكْرُوهِ تَحْرِيمًا . وَالْمُرَادُ بِالْمَنْدُوبِ مَا يَشْمَلُ السُّنَّةَ وَالنَّفْلَ فَصَارَتِ الْأَقْسَامُ سِتَّةَ وَلِكُلِّ مِنْهَا طَرَفَانِ فِعَل أَى إِيقَاعٌ عَلَى مَا هُوَ الْمَعْنَى الْمَصْدَرِى وَتَرْك أَى عَدَمُ فِعْلٍ فَتَصِيرُ
Then what is meant by 'wajib' includes fard as well, because its usage in this sense is common among them, like their saying Zakat is wajib and Hajj is wajib, contrary to applying 'haram' to makruh tahrimi. And what is meant by 'mandub' includes sunnah and nafl. So the categories become six, and each of them has two sides: act (i.e., performance, which is the verbal noun meaning) and omission (i.e., not doing), so they become (twelve).
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage is a terminological clarification from the matn (Al-Tawdih). It explains that in the classification of the twelve categories, the term 'wajib' is used in a broad sense that includes both fard (established by definitive evidence) and wajib (established by speculative evidence). This is standard Hanafi usage, as in 'Zakat is wajib' and 'Hajj is wajib'—these are fard acts. However, they do not apply the term 'haram' to makruh tahrimi; that would be a misuse. Similarly, 'mandub' includes both sunnah (emphasized voluntary acts) and nafl (non-emphasized voluntary acts). By this broad understanding, the primary categories of actions are six: wajib (including fard), mandub (including sunnah and nafl), mubah, makruh tanzihi, makruh tahrimi, and haram. Each of these six has two aspects: performing the action and omitting it. Thus, the total number of rulings becomes twelve (6 categories × 2 sides). This explains the earlier claim that there are twelve categories of actions.

Key Terms
الوَاجِب (al-wajib): In this classification, it is used broadly to include fard (established by qat'i evidence) and wajib (established by zanni evidence).
المَنْدُوب (al-mandub): Includes both sunnah (emphasized voluntary acts) and nafl (non-emphasized voluntary acts).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi twelve-category classification, 'wajib' includes fard, and 'mandub' includes sunnah and nafl, forming six primary rulings each with act and omission sides.

From Six to Twelve: Act and Omission in the Ahkam
Defining terms and doubling categories via act and omission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain how the six basic ahkam become twelve by considering both the act of performing and the act of omitting, and apply this classification to given scenarios.

Core Idea
Every hukm has two aspects: performing the act and omitting it; thus six categories become twelve.

In Hanafi usul, the five (or six) categories of rulings are not limited to the act of commission; omission also carries a ruling. This passage clarifies that 'wajib' and 'mandub' are used broadly to include fard and sunnah/nafl respectively. Then, by applying both the act and its omission to each category, the six become twelve. This precision is essential to avoid confusion in reward and punishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six basic ahkam
The passage builds on the six categories: wajib (including fard), mandub (including sunnah and nafl), mubah, makruh tanzihi, makruh tahrimi, and haram. Note that wajib and mandub are defined broadly.
The six are not explicitly listed here but are assumed from earlier context.
2
Understand the broad definitions
Wajib includes fard (e.g., zakat and hajj are called wajib). Mandub includes sunnah and nafl. This is common Hanafi usage.
Contrast with the stricter definitions in other madhahib.
3
Recognize the two aspects of each hukm
Each of the six ahkam has two sides: performing the act (fi'l) and omitting it (tark). For example, the ruling 'wajib' can apply to the act of performing a duty or to the act of omitting a prohibition.
The act is the concrete performance (e.g., the state of prayer), not the abstract masdar.
4
Derive the twelve categories
Multiply the six ahkam by two (act and omission) to get twelve. For instance, the wajib of the act (performing a wajib) and the wajib of the omission (omitting a haram, which is itself wajib).
The passage explicitly gives the example: non-performance of the wajib is haram, and non-performance of the haram is wajib.
5
Apply to a concrete example
Take the hukm 'haram'. Its act-aspect is performing the haram (which is haram). Its omission-aspect is refraining from the haram (which is wajib). Thus we have two rulings from one original hukm.
This shows why the distinction is necessary for precise attribution of reward and punishment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ المُرَادُ بِالْوَاجِبِ مَا يَشْمَلُ الْفَرْضَ أَيْضًا ؛ لِأَنَّ اسْتِعْمَالَهُ بِهَذَا الْمَعْنَى شَائِعٌ عِنْدَهُمْ كَقَوْلِهِمُ الزَّكَاةَ وَاجِبَةٌ وَالْحَج وَاجِبٌ بِخِلَافِ إِطْلَاقِ الْحَرَامِ عَلَى الْمَكْرُوهِ تَحْرِيمًا . وَالْمُرَادُ بِالْمَنْدُوبِ مَا يَشْمَلُ السُّنَّةَ وَالنَّفْلَ فَصَارَتِ الْأَقْسَامُ سِتَّةَ وَلِكُلِّ مِنْهَا طَرَفَانِ فِعَل أَى إِيقَاعٌ عَلَى مَا هُوَ الْمَعْنَى الْمَصْدَرِى وَتَرْك أَى عَدَمُ فِعْلٍ فَتَصِيرُ اثْنَتَيْ عَشَرَ وَالْمُرَادُ بِمَا يَأْتِي بِهِ الْمُكَلَّفُ الْفِعْلُ بِمَعْنَى الْحَاصِلِ مِنْ الْمَصْدَرِ كَالْهَيْئَةِ الَّتِي تُسَمَّى صَلَاةٌ وَالْحَالَةُ الَّتِي تُسَمَّى صَوْمًا وَنَحْوُ ذَلِكَ مِمَّا هُوَ أَثَرٌ صَادِرٌ عَنْ الْمُكَلَّفِ وَطَرَفٌ فِعْلِهِ إِيقَاعُهُ وَطَرَف تَرْكِهِ عَدَمُ إِيقَاعِهِ وَالْأُمُورُ الْمَذْكُورَةُ مِنْ الْوَاجِبِ وَالْحَرَامِ وَغَيْرِهِمَا ، وَإِنْ كَانَتْ فِي الْحَقِيقَةِ مِنْ صِفَاتِ فِعْلِ الْمُكَلَّفِ خَاصَّةً إِلَّا أَنَّهَا قَدْ تُطْلَقُ عَلَى عَدَمِ الْفِعْلِ أَيْضًا فَيُقَالُ عَدَمُ مُبَاشَرَةِ الْوَاجِبِ حَرَامٌ وَعَدَمُ مُبَاشَرَةِ الْحَرَامِ وَاجِبٌ ، وَهُوَ الْمُرَادُ هَهُنَا ، وَإِنَّمَا فَسَّرَ الشَّرُكَ بِعَدَمِ الْفِعْلِ لِبَصِيرَ قِسْمًا آخَرَ ، إِذْ لَوْ أُرِيدَ بِهِ كَفُّ النَّفْسِ لَكَانَ تَرُكُ أن حَرَامِ مَثَلًا فِعْلَ الْوَاجِبِ بِعَيْنِهِ ، فَإِنْ قُلْتَ : أَيُّ حَاجَةٍ إِلَى اعْتِبَارِ الْفِعْلِ وَالتَّرْكِ وَجَعَلِ الأقسامِ اثْنَى عَشَرَ وَهَلَّا اقْتَصَرَ عَلَى السِّيِّةِ بأن يُرَادَ بِالْوَاجِبِ مَثلا أعَمُّ مِنْ الْفِعْلِ وَالتّرْكِ قُلْتُ ؛ لأنَّهُ إِذَا قَالَ الْوَاجِبُ يَدْخُلُ فِيمَا يُثَابُ عَلَيْهِ لَمْ يَصِحْ ذَلِكَ فِي الْوَاجِبِ بِمَعْنَى عَدَمِ فِعْلِ الْحَرَامِ فَلا بُدَّ مِنَ التَّفْصِيلِ الْمَذْكُورِ ، ثُمَّ لَا يَخْفَى أَنَّ الْمُرَادَ أَنَّ عَدَمَ الْإِثْيَانِ بِالْوَاجِبِ يَسْتَحِقُ الْعِقَابَ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ قَدْ لَا يُعَاقَبُ لِعَفْوِ مِنْ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى أَوْ سَهْوِ مِنْ الْعَبْدِ أَوْ نَحْوِ ذَلِكَ .
Then the intended meaning of wajib is that which includes fard as well, because its usage in this sense is common among them, like their saying: 'Zakat is wajib,' 'Hajj is wajib,' contrary to applying haram to makruh tahrimi. And the intended meaning of mandub is that which includes sunnah and nafl. So the categories become six, and for each of them there are two aspects: act, i.e., performance based on its masdari meaning, and omission, i.e., non-performance. So they become twelve. And the intended meaning of what the mukallaf brings is the act in the sense of the result of the source (al-hasil min al-masdar), like the state called prayer, and the state called fasting, and similar things that are effects issuing from the mukallaf. Its act-aspect is its performance, its omission-aspect is non-performance. And the mentioned matters — wajib, haram, and others — although in reality they are specifically attributes of the mukallaf's act, yet they may also be applied to non-act. So it is said: 'Non-performance of the wajib is haram,' and 'Non-performance of the haram is wajib.' And that is what is intended here. And the reason he interpreted 'shirk' as non-performance is to establish another division, because if it were intended as refraining from the self, then omitting something haram, for example, would be the very act of the wajib. If you say: 'What need is there to consider act and omission, making twelve divisions? Why not restrict to six by meaning wajib, for example, as inclusive of both act and omission?' I say: Because if one says 'wajib enters into what one is rewarded for,' that would not be correct for wajib in the sense of non-performance of the haram. So the mentioned detail is necessary. Then it is not hidden that the intended meaning is that non-performance of the wajib deserves punishment, except that one may not be punished due to forgiveness from Allah or forgetfulness from the servant or the like.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of the five (or six) ahkam in Hanafi usul. It begins by clarifying that the term 'wajib' here includes 'fard'; this is a common usage among Hanafis (e.g., they say zakat is wajib, hajj is wajib, even though technically fard is more specific). Similarly, 'mandub' includes both sunnah and nafl. Thus the basic five categories (wajib, mandub, mubah, makruh, haram) become six by splitting makruh into tanzihi and tahrimi? Actually the text says 'categories become six' — this is because in the preceding discussion (not fully shown here) the categories were likely the five plus a sixth? Or it refers to the five original plus the distinction within mandub? It then states that each of these six has two aspects: performing the act (fi'l) and omitting it (tark). This yields twelve categories. The author then clarifies that the 'act' spoken of is the resultant state (al-hasil min al-masdar), i.e., the concrete action like the state of prayer or fasting, not the abstract source meaning. The attributes like 'wajib' etc. are primarily attributes of the act, but they can also be applied to the omission. For example, 'non-performance of wajib is haram' and 'non-performance of haram is wajib'. The commentator justifies this by noting that if we did not distinguish between act and omission, then saying 'wajib' would ambiguously include both the act of performing a wajib and the act of omitting a haram, which would cause confusion in reward and punishment. Therefore, the detailed twelve-fold classification is necessary. Finally, he notes that 'deserving punishment' for omitting a wajib does not necessarily mean actual punishment if there is forgiveness or forgetfulness. This is a typical Hanafi precision in defining the hukm as it is in the divine address, not necessarily as realized in every instance.

Key Terms
الْوَاجِب (al-wajib): In this text, wajib is defined broadly to include fard. It is an act whose performance is rewarded and omission deserves punishment.
الْمَنْدُوب (al-mandub): Includes sunnah and nafl; performance is rewarded, omission is not punished.
فِعَل (فعل) وتَرْك (fi'l wa tark): Two aspects of each hukm: the act of performing and the act of omitting. Applied to all six basic categories to yield twelve.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To increase the number of categories for academic completeness.
B) Because the term 'wajib' cannot correctly apply to omission of haram without causing confusion in reward and punishment.
C) To align with the madhhab of Imam Shafi'i.
D) Because the Quran mentions both act and omission.

Key Takeaway
The six ahkam each have two aspects — act and omission — making twelve distinct rulings, a necessary precision to avoid ambiguity in reward and punishment.

The Twelve Categories of Hukm Taklifi: Why Act and Omission Are Distinct
Expansion probe on act-omission distinction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi usul distinguishes between act and omission for each legal ruling, and apply this distinction to identify the correct hukm for both aspects.

Core Idea
Every legal ruling has two sides: what you do and what you leave undone.

In this passage, the commentator defends the twelve-fold division of hukm taklifi, showing that each primary ruling must be considered from two perspectives: the act performed and its omission. This is not mere classification; it is essential because reward and punishment attach differently to each side. You will learn to see both dimensions of any ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary rulings
List the six categories of hukm taklifi: wajib, haram, mandub, makruh, mubah, and the sixth (e.g., makruh tahrimi). Note that Hanafis often distinguish five or six.
The exact count may vary, but the principle applies.
2
Recognize the two aspects
For each ruling, consider both the act (fi‘l) and its omission (tark). The act is the performance; the omission is the non-performance.
Omission is defined as 'adam al-fi‘l, not as an act itself.
3
Understand why omission is not the opposite act
Omitting a haram act is not the same as performing a wajib act. The commentator argues that treating omission merely as 'kuff al-nafs' would conflate distinct rulings.
Reward for omitting haram differs from reward for performing wajib.
4
Trace the proof for twelve categories
The author uses logical necessity: if we say 'wajib' includes both act and omission, then the statement 'wajib earns reward' would be false for omission (since omitting haram is not rewarded the same). Thus, detail is needed.
This is a dalil 'aqli (rational proof) grounded in the nature of reward.
5
Apply the distinction
Given any ruling, state its act-side and omission-side. For example: act of wajib = wajib, omission of wajib = haram. Act of haram = haram, omission of haram = wajib.
Use this to construct the full twelve categories.

التي عَشَرَ وَالْمُرَادُ بِمَا يَأْتِي بِهِ الْمُكَلَّفُ الْفِعْلُ بِمَعْنَى الْحَاصِلِ مِنْ الْمَصْدَرِ كَالْهَيْئَةِ الَّتِي تُسَمَّى صَلَاةٌ وَالْحَالَةُ الَّتِي تُسَمَّى صَوْمًا وَنَحْوُ ذَلِكَ مِمَّا هُوَ أَثَرٌ صَادِرٌ عَنْ الْمُكَلَّفِ وَطَرَفٌ فِعْلِهِ إِيقَاعُهُ وَطَرَف تَرْكِهِ عَدَمُ إِيقَاعِهِ وَالْأُمُورُ الْمَذْكُورَةُ مِنْ الْوَاجِبِ وَالْحَرَامِ وَغَيْرِهِمَا ، وَإِنْ كَانَتْ فِي الْحَقِيقَةِ مِنْ صِفَاتِ فِعْلِ الْمُكَلَّفِ خَاصَّةً إِلَّا أَنَّهَا قَدْ تُطْلَقُ عَلَى عَدَمِ الْفِعْلِ أَيْضًا فَيُقَالُ عَدَمُ مُبَاشَرَةِ الْوَاجِبِ حَرَامٌ وَعَدَمُ مُبَاشَرَةِ الْحَرَامِ وَاجِبٌ ، وَهُوَ الْمُرَادُ هَهُنَا ، وَإِنَّمَا فَسَّرَ الشَّرُكَ بِعَدَمِ الْفِعْلِ لِبَصِيرَ قِسْمًا آخَرَ ، إِذْ لَوْ أُرِيدَ بِهِ كَفُّ النَّفْسِ لَكَانَ تَرُكُ أن حَرَامِ مَثَلًا فِعْلَ الْوَاجِبِ بِعَيْنِهِ ، فَإِنْ قُلْتَ : أَيُّ حَاجَةٍ إِلَى اعْتِبَارِ الْفِعْلِ وَالتَّرْكِ وَجَعَلِ الأقسامِ اثْنَى عَشَرَ وَهَلَّا اقْتَصَرَ عَلَى السِّيِّةِ بأن يُرَادَ بِالْوَاجِبِ مَثلا أعَمُّ مِنْ الْفِعْلِ وَالتّرْكِ قُلْتُ ؛ لأنَّهُ إِذَا قَالَ الْوَاجِبُ يَدْخُلُ فِيمَا يُثَابُ عَلَيْهِ لَمْ يَصِحْ ذَلِكَ فِي الْوَاجِبِ بِمَعْنَى عَدَمِ فِعْلِ الْحَرَامِ فَلا بُدَّ مِنَ التَّفْصِيلِ الْمَذْكُورِ ، ثُمَّ لَا يَخْفَى أَنَّ الْمُرَادَ أَنَّ عَدَمَ الْإِثْيَانِ بِالْوَاجِبِ يَسْتَحِقُ الْعِقَابَ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ قَدْ لَا يُعَاقَبُ لِعَفْوِ مِنْ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى أَوْ سَهْوِ مِنْ الْعَبْدِ أَوْ نَحْوِ ذَلِكَ .

ترجمہ: پھر مرا دوا جب سے وہ ہے جو شامل ہوتا ہے فرض کو بھی اس لئے کہ اس کا استعمال اس معنی میں شائع ہے ان کے نزدیک مثل ان کے قول " الزکوۃ واجبتہ ، احج واجب" کے بخلاف خرام کا اطلاق کرنے کے مکروہ تحریمی پر اور مراد مندوب سے وہ ہے جو شامل ہوتا ہے سنت کو اور نفل کو۔ پس ہو جائیں گی اقسام چھ اور ہر ایک کے لیے ان میں سے دو طرفیں ہیں فعل یعنی واقع کرنا او پر اس کے وہ معنی مصدری ہے اور ترک یعنی فعل کا نہ ہونا پس ہو جائیں گی بارہ قسمیں ۔ اور مراد اس سے جس کو مکلف لاتا ہے وہ فعل ہے جو حاصل من المصدر" کے معنی میں ہو مثل اس حالت کے جس کا نام رکھا جاتا ہے صلوۃ اور وہ حالت کہ جس کا نام رکھا جاتا ہے صوم اور اس کی مثل سے ان سے جو ایسا اثر ہے جو صادر ہوتا ہے مکلف سے اور طرف فعل اس کا واقع کرنا ہے اور طرف ترک اس (فعل) کا واقع نہ کرنا ہے اور وہ امور جن کو ذکر کیا گیا ہے یعنی واجب اور حرام اور ان دونوں کے علاوہ اگر چہ حقیقت میں مکلف کے فعل کی صفات میں سے ہیں خاص طور پر مگر بیشک کبھی ان کا اطلاق کیا جاتا ہے عدم فعل پر بھی پس کہا جاتا ہے عدم المباشرة الواجب حرام اور عدم مباشرة الحرام واجب۔ اور یہی مراد ہے یہاں ۔سوائے اس کے نہیں کہ تعبیر کی ہے ترک کی عدم فعل کے ساتھ تاکہ ہو جائے دوسری قسم۔ اس لئے کہ اگر ارادہ کیا جائے اس کے ساتھ کف انفس کا تو البتہ ہو جائے گا ترک حرام مشکلی کے طور پر فعل واجب بعینہ ۔ پس اگر تو کہے کہ کیا حاجت ہے فعل کے اعتبار کرنے کی اور ترک کے اعتبار کرنے کی اور اقسام کو بارہ بنانے کی کیوں نہیں اکتفاء کیا گیا چھ پر بائیں طور کہ مراد لیا جا تا واجب کے ساتھ مثال کے طور پر وہ جو اعم ہو فعل سے اور ترک سے ، تو میں کہوں گا ، اس لئے کہ جب کہا واجب داخل ہے ان احکام میں جن پر ثواب دیا جاتا ہے تو یہ میچ نہیں ہو گا واجب بمعنی عدم الفعل کے، پس ضروری ہے تفصیل مذکور۔ پھر نہیں مخفی کہ بیشک مراد یہ ہے کہ واجب کے نہ لانے سے مستحق ہوگا اس کی وجہ سے عتاب کا مگر وہ بیشک کبھی نہیں عقاب (سزا) دیا جاتا اللہ تعالیٰ کی جانب سے معاف کرنے کے ساتھ یا بھول جانے کے ساتھ بندے کی جانب سے یا اس کی مثل سے۔

فقہا کی اصطلاح میں فرض پر واجب کا اطلاق ہوتا ہے

تشریح: ثم المراد:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا حصہ نہم ہے۔ غرض:۔ اعتراض کا جواب دینا ہے۔ اعتراض:- آپ کی بیان کردہ وجہ حضر درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس میں فرض کا ذکر نہیں ہے۔

جواب: فرض کو ذکر کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ واجب ہی میں داخل ہے اور وہ اس طرح کہ واجب وہ ہے جس میں جانب فعل اولی اور جانب ترک ممنوع ہو اب اگر ترک سے منع قطعی دلیل سے ہو تو فرض ہے اور اگر دلیل ظنی سے ہو تو وہ واجب ہے۔

اعتراض:۔ پھر تو مکروہ تحریمی کو بھی ذکر کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں تھی کیونکہ وہ بھی حرام میں داخل ہے۔

جواب: مکروہ تحریمی حرام میں داخل تو ہے لیکن اس کو ذکر کرنا ضروری تھا کیونکہ کروہ تحریمی پر حرام کا اطلاق عام طور پر نہیں ہوتا لیکن واجب کا اطلاق فرض پر فقہاء کے ہاں مشہور ہے جیسا کہ فقہ کی کتابوں میں مذکور ہے الزکوۃ واجبتہ ، اور امج واجب ، یہاں زکوۃ اور حج پر واجب کا اطلاق کیا گیا ہے حالانکہ یہ دونوں فرض ہیں ۔

والمراد بالمندوب:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دسواں حصہ ہے غرض : اعتراض کا جواب دینا ہے۔

اعتراض:۔ آپ کی وجہ حصر درست نہیں کیونکہ اس میں سنت اور نفل کا ذکر نہیں ہے۔
Then the intended [meaning] of what the mukallaf performs is the act (fi‘l) in the sense of the product of the verbal noun (masdar), like the state which is called prayer and the state which is called fasting, and similar things that are effects emanating from the mukallaf. The side of its action is its performance, and the side of its omission is its non-performance. The matters mentioned — obligatory, prohibited, and others — although in reality they are attributes of the mukallaf’s act specifically, they are sometimes also applied to non-action, so it is said: 'Non-performance of the obligatory is prohibited, and non-performance of the prohibited is obligatory.' That is what is intended here. He explained 'omission' as non-action only to make it another division. For if by it he meant restraint of the self, then the omission of the prohibited would be exactly the performance of the obligatory. If you say: What need is there to consider action and omission and to make the divisions twelve? Why not suffice with six by intending by 'obligatory', for example, something that includes both action and omission? I say: Because if one says 'the obligatory enters into that for which reward is given', that would not be correct for obligatory in the sense of non-action of the prohibited. So the aforementioned detail is necessary. Moreover, it is not hidden that what is intended is that non-performance of the obligatory deserves punishment, although he may not be punished due to forgiveness from Allah Most High or forgetfulness from the servant or the like.

Translation: Then the intended [meaning] of what includes fard as well, because its usage is common in that sense among them, like their saying 'Zakat is wajib, Hajj is wajib', unlike the application of 'haram' to makruh tahrimi. And the intended by 'mandub' is that which includes sunna and nafl. So the divisions become six, and for each of them there are two sides: act, i.e., performance, and omission, i.e., non-performance. So they become twelve divisions. And what is meant by what the mukallaf brings is the act in the sense of the product of the masdar, like the state called salat and the state called sawm and similar things that are effects emanating from the mukallaf. The side of the act is its performance, and the side of omission is its non-performance. And the matters mentioned — wajib, haram, and others — although in reality they are attributes of the mukallaf's act specifically, they are sometimes applied to non-action as well, so it is said: 'Non-performance of the obligatory is haram, and non-performance of the prohibited is wajib.' And that is what is intended here. It is only that he expressed omission as non-action so that it becomes another division. Because if by it he meant restraint of the self, then the omission of the prohibited would be exactly the performance of the obligatory. So if you say: What need is there to consider action and omission and to make the divisions twelve? Why not suffice with six by intending by 'obligatory', for example, something that includes both action and omission? I say: Because when it is said that wajib enters into those rulings for which reward is given, that would not match wajib in the sense of non-action. So the aforementioned detail is necessary. Then it is not hidden that what is intended is that non-performance of the wajib deserves punishment, but he may not be punished due to forgiveness from Allah or forgetfulness from the servant or the like.

In the terminology of the jurists, the term 'wajib' is applied to fard.

Commentary: 'Then the intended' is the ninth part of the commentary. Purpose: To answer an objection. Objection: Your stated reason is not correct because it does not mention fard. Answer: It is not necessary to mention fard because it is included in wajib. And that is such: wajib is that in which the side of doing is preferred and the side of omission is prohibited. If the prohibition of omission is by a definitive proof, then it is fard; if by a presumptive proof, then it is wajib. Objection: Then it was not necessary to mention makruh tahrimi either, because it is included in haram. Answer: Makruh tahrimi is indeed included in haram, but it was necessary to mention it because the term 'haram' is not generally applied to makruh tahrimi, while the application of 'wajib' to fard is well-known among the jurists, as in the books of fiqh: 'Zakat is wajib', 'Hajj is wajib'. Here zakat and hajj are called wajib although they are fard. 'And the intended by mandub' is the tenth part. Purpose: To answer an objection. Objection: Your stated reason is not correct because it does not mention sunna and nafl.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the division of legal rulings (ahkam taklifiyya) into twelve categories. The author explains why each of the five or six primary rulings (wajib, haram, mandub, etc.) must be considered from two perspectives: the act itself (fi'l) and its omission (tark). The core insight is that when we speak of a ruling like 'wajib', it applies both to performing the wajib act and to omitting a haram act. Similarly, 'haram' applies both to performing a haram act and to omitting a wajib act. The passage argues that simply having six categories (the five plus possibly a sixth) would be insufficient because reward and punishment are attached differently to acts and omissions. For example, omitting a prohibited act is not itself rewarded in the same way as performing an obligatory act, so they must be distinguished. The author then responds to potential objections: (1) Why not just include fard under wajib? Answer: Wajib includes fard by usage; the term 'wajib' is commonly applied to fard in fiqh texts. (2) Why include makruh tahrimi separately when it is under haram? Answer: Because 'haram' is not commonly applied to makruh tahrimi, so it needs explicit mention. (3) Why not include sunna and nafl under mandub? The response begins here but trails off. Overall, the passage grounds the necessity of the twelve-fold division in the practical need to correctly assign reward and punishment.

Key Terms
الْفِعْلُ (al-fi‘l): The act performed by the mukallaf, understood as the product (hāsīl) of the verbal noun (masdar), e.g., the state called 'prayer' or 'fasting'.
التَّرْكُ (al-tark): The omission of the act, defined as non-performance (adam al-fi‘l). It is a separate legal category, distinct from the act itself.
الْوَاجِبُ (al-wajib): An act whose performance is preferred and whose omission is prohibited; it includes both fard (by definitive proof) and wajib (by presumptive proof).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the commentator insist on making twelve categories instead of six?
A) Because each of the six primary rulings has two aspects: performance and omission, which have different reward/punishment implications.
B) Because there are exactly twelve different types of actions in the Shari'ah.
C) Because the original matn explicitly listed twelve categories.
D) Because the author wanted to match the number of months in a year.

Key Takeaway
The twelve-fold division of hukm taklifi is essential for accurate legal analysis, as it distinguishes the consequences of performing an act from omitting its opposite.

Why Six Become Twelve: Doing and Leaving in Hukm
Logical proof for twelve-fold hukm classification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why each hukm category must be considered for both action and abandonment, and classify the leaving of an act according to its opposite ruling.

Core Idea
Every hukm is two-sided: doing carries one ruling, leaving carries the opposite.

This passage reveals a key usul al-fiqh insight: each of the five or six rulings (wajib, haram, etc.) applies not only to performing an act but also to abstaining from it. The author demonstrates why we cannot collapse these into a single concept, and explains the consequences of neglecting the distinction. By the end, you'll understand the usul basis for the twelve-fold classification of hukm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six base categories
Recall the six categories of hukm in Hanafi usul: fard/wajib, mandub, mubah, haram, makruh tahrimi, makruh tanzihi. These are the 'doing' aspects.
2
Recognize the opposite of each category
For each category, the opposite concerns the act of leaving (tark). For example, leaving wajib is haram, leaving haram is wajib, leaving mandub is makruh tanzihi, etc. This yields six more categories.
3
Understand the author's proof
The author argues that the definition of wajib as 'rewarded upon its performance' (thawab) cannot include its non-performance. Therefore, the non-performance of wajib must be classified separately as haram. This reasoning justifies the necessity of twelve categories.
The passage addresses an objection: why not just six, taking 'wajib' to include both doing and leaving? The answer is that the definition of wajib as reward-worthy excludes the non-action.
4
Note the nuance of blame vs. punishment
Leaving wajib makes one deserving of blame (itāb) but not necessarily punishment (iqāb), because Allah may forgive or the person may forget. This shows that the moral categories apply to the act of leaving itself, not just to the consequence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہے عدم المباشرة الواجب حرام اور عدم مباشرة الحرام واجب۔ اور یہی مراد ہے یہاں ۔سوائے اس کے نہیں کہ تعبیر کی ہے ترک کی عدم فعل کے ساتھ تاکہ ہو جائے دوسری قسم۔ اس لئے کہ اگر ارادہ کیا جائے اس کے ساتھ کف انفس کا تو البتہ ہو جائے گا ترک حرام مشکلی کے طور پر فعل واجب بعینہ ۔ پس اگر تو کہے کہ کیا حاجت ہے فعل کے اعتبار کرنے کی اور ترک کے اعتبار کرنے کی اور اقسام کو بارہ بنانے کی کیوں نہیں اکتفاء کیا گیا چھ پر بائیں طور کہ مراد لیا جا تا واجب کے ساتھ مثال کے طور پر وہ جو اعم ہو فعل سے اور ترک سے ، تو میں کہوں گا ، اس لئے کہ جب کہا واجب داخل ہے ان احکام میں جن پر ثواب دیا جاتا ہے تو یہ میچ نہیں ہو گا واجب بمعنی عدم الفعل کے، پس ضروری ہے تفصیل مذکور۔ پھر نہیں مخفی کہ بیشک مراد یہ ہے کہ واجب کے نہ لانے سے مستحق ہوگا اس کی وجہ سے عتاب کا مگر وہ بیشک کبھی نہیں عقاب (سزا) دیا جاتا اللہ تعالیٰ کی جانب سے معاف کرنے کے ساتھ یا بھول جانے کے ساتھ بندے کی جانب سے یا اس کی مثل سے۔
The non-performance of the wajib is haram, and the non-performance of the haram is wajib. And this is what is meant here. Not except that he has expressed 'ترك' (leaving) with 'عدم فعل' (non-action) so that there becomes another division. Because if by that is intended 'كف النفس' (self-restraint), then indeed it will become the leaving of haram as a problematic form of the very act of wajib. So if you say: What need is there to consider action and consider leaving, and to make the divisions twelve? Why not suffice with six, in the manner that by 'wajib' is meant, for example, that which is more general than action and leaving? Then I would say: Because when it is said that wajib is included among those rulings upon which reward is given, then this will not match wajib in the sense of non-action. Thus the mentioned detail is necessary. Then it is not hidden that indeed the intention is that by not performing the wajib one becomes deserving of blame, but he is never punished by Allah, due to forgiveness or due to forgetfulness on the part of the servant, or the like.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage explains why each of the six categories (wajib, mandub, mubah, haram, makruh tahrimi, makruh tanzihi) must be divided into doing and leaving, resulting in twelve. The author argues that 'leaving' is expressed as 'non-action' to create a separate category. If 'leaving' meant self-restraint, it would conflate opposites. The objection: why not just six? The answer: because 'wajib' in the definition as reward-worthy excludes 'non-action of wajib' (which is haram), so both doing and leaving must be considered. Furthermore, leaving the wajib incurs blame but not necessarily punishment, as forgiveness is possible.

Key Terms
ترک (tark): عدم فعل (non-action) of an act; specifically applied to wajib (its tark is haram) and haram (its tark is wajib).
عتاب (itāb): Blame or reproach short of punishment; a consequence of leaving wajib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why can't we simply have six categories (wajib, mandub, etc.) without considering their opposites?
A) Because the six categories are not exhaustive.
B) Because the definition of wajib as reward-worthy does not include its opposite (non-action), yet the non-action of wajib carries a ruling (haram).
C) Because the author wanted exactly twelve categories for symmetry.
D) Because the mukallaf only does actions, not non-actions.

Key Takeaway
Every hukm category must be considered both for performance and abandonment, because the definition of the category (e.g., reward for wajib) does not apply to its opposite, requiring separate classification.

Fard Included in Wajib and Makruh Tahrimi in Haram
Defense of why fard is not separately listed, as it is encompassed by wajib.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school does not list fard separately from wajib in classifications of ahkam, and identify the role of qat'i and zanni proofs in distinguishing them.

Core Idea
Fard is wajib with qat'i proof; makruh tahrimi is haram but avoided in common usage.

In Hanafi usul, the terms 'fard' and 'wajib' are closely linked. This passage from a commentary defends why fard is not separately listed in a classification of rulings, and similarly why makruh tahrimi is listed despite being under haram. Understanding this helps clarify the Hanafi hierarchy of ahkam and how definitions shape legal discourse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objections
Recognize the two objections raised against the commentator's classification: first, fard is missing; second, makruh tahrimi should also be omitted if included in haram.
The objector assumes fard is a distinct category that must be explicitly mentioned.
2
Analyze the response to the first objection
The commentator argues that fard is subsumed under wajib, defined as having a prohibition of leaving. The distinction is based on the strength of the evidence (qat'i vs zanni).
Thus, any act whose leaving is prohibited is wajib; if the prohibition is proven by qat'i evidence, it is fard.
3
Analyze the response to the second objection
Makruh tahrimi, though included in haram, is mentioned separately because the term 'haram' is not commonly applied to it in general usage, unlike 'wajib' which commonly applies to fard.
Common usage among fuqaha justifies the separate listing.
4
Evaluate the practical consequence
Note how this affects reading Hanafi texts: when they say 'wajib', it may include fard. This differs from Shafi'i usage where fard and wajib are distinct.
The thamarah al-khilaf is in the terminology used in fiqh works.

Source Text

فقہا کی اصطلاح میں فرض پر واجب کا اطلاق ہوتا ہے
تشریح: ثم المراد:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا حصہ نہم ہے۔ غرض:۔ اعتراض کا جواب دینا ہے۔ اعتراض:- آپ کی بیان کردہ وجہ حضر درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس میں فرض کا ذکر نہیں ہے۔
جواب: فرض کو ذکر کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ واجب ہی میں داخل ہے اور وہ اس طرح کہ واجب وہ ہے جس میں جانب فعل اولی اور جانب ترک ممنوع ہو اب اگر ترک سے منع قطعی دلیل سے ہو تو فرض ہے اور اگر دلیل ظنی سے ہو تو وہ

جواب: مکروہ تحریمی حرام میں داخل تو ہے لیکن اس کو ذکر کرنا ضروری تھا کیونکہ کروہ تحریمی پر حرام کا اطلاق عام طور پر نہیں ہوتا لیکن واجب کا اطلاق فرض پر فقہاء کے ہاں مشہور ہے جیسا کہ فقہ کی کتابوں میں مذکور ہے الزکوۃ واجبتہ ، اور امج واجب ، یہاں زکوۃ اور حج پر واجب کا اطلاق کیا گیا ہے حالانکہ یہ دونوں فرض ہیں ۔
In the terminology of the fuqaha, the term 'wajib' is applied to 'fard'.
Explanation: Then the intended meaning: This is the ninth part of the commentary's text. Purpose: to answer an objection. Objection: Your stated reason for restriction is not correct because it does not mention fard. Answer: There is no need to mention fard because it is included in wajib, and that is as follows: Wajib is that in which the side of doing is primary and the side of leaving is prohibited. Now if the prohibition of leaving is by a definitive proof, then it is fard; and if by a speculative proof, then it is wajib. Objection: Then there was no need to mention makruh tahrimi either, because it too is included in haram. Answer: Makruh tahrimi is indeed included in haram, but it was necessary to mention it because the term 'haram' is not commonly applied to makruh tahrimi. However, the application of 'wajib' to fard is well-known among the fuqaha, as mentioned in the books of fiqh: 'Zakat is wajib' and 'Hajj is wajib', even though both are fard.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage addresses objections about the classification of rulings. The commentator explains why fard is not listed separately: it is included under wajib, with fard defined as wajib proven by definitive evidence (qat'i), and wajib by speculative evidence (zanni). Similarly, makruh tahrimi is included in haram but separated because the term 'haram' is not commonly used for it in general discourse, whereas 'wajib' commonly includes fard in fiqh works, as seen in phrases like 'zakat is wajib'.

Key Terms
فرض (fard): That which wajib is established by a definitive proof (دلیل قطعی); included in the broader term 'wajib'.
مکروہ تحریمی (makruh tahrimi): Rulings that are closer to haram, included in haram but not commonly called haram.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, fard and wajib are hierarchically related by proof strength, not separate categories, and makruh tahrimi is a subset of haram but mentioned separately due to common usage.
